<t442>“In Purfleet, I came across a place on a side road that resembled what I was looking for and had a dilapidated sign indicating it was for sale.</t442> <t443>It was an old structure, built with heavy stones and surrounded by a high wall that hadn't seen any repairs for many years.</t443> <t444>The closed doors were made of heavy old oak and entirely worn out by rust.</t444>
<t445>The name of the mansion is Carfax; undoubtedly, it is a corrupted form of the old Quatre Face because the building is four-cornered, aligned with the four cardinal points of the compass.</t445><t446>In total, it consists of an eight-hectare area surrounded by the aforementioned massive stone wall.</t446><t447>There are numerous trees and a body of water that make the area dim in some places. The water is both clean and flows in a medium-sized stream, indicating that it is fed by a source, forming a deep and dark-looking pond or small lake.</t447><t448>The house is quite large and I can say that its history dates back to the Middle Ages, because one side is made of extremely thick stone, has few windows high up, and the windows are covered with tight iron bars.</t448><t449>It looks like a part of an inner castle and is very close to an old chapel or church.</t449><t450>I couldn't enter it because I didn't have the key to the door leading there from the house, but I took pictures of it from different angles with my Kodak.</t450><t451>Additions have been made to the house, but these were done very haphazardly, and I can only estimate the area it covers - which must be quite large.</t451><t452>There are only a few houses nearby; one of them is a very large house that has recently been converted into a private mental hospital with various additions.</t452><t453>However, it is not visible from the mansion.</t453><t454>”</t454>
<t455>When I finished, the Count said:</t455>
<t456>"I'm glad it is old and large.</t456> <t457>Personally, I come from an old family, and living in a new house would kill me.</t457> <t458>A house cannot be made livable in a day, and already how few days are needed for a century.</t458> <t459>I'm also very glad that there is an old chapel from ancient times.</t459> <t460>We Transylvanian nobles love to think that our bones will not be among the common dead.</t460> <t461>I'm not after entertainment, joy, or the bright sensuality of daylight and sparkling waters that please the young and cheerful.</t461> <t462>I'm no longer young, and my heart cannot keep up with joy due to the weary years spent mourning the dead.</t462> <t463>Moreover, the walls of my castle are crumbling; the number of shadows is many, and the wind blows coldly through the broken battlements and windows.</t463> <t464>I love shadowy places and shadows, and I prefer to be alone with my thoughts as much as possible.</t464><t465>"</t465>
<t466>In some way, his words and glances did not seem to match, or the expression on his face might have caused his smile to appear malevolent and cold.</t466>
<t467>Immediately, he left my side with an excuse and asked me to gather all my documents as he was leaving.</t467> <t468>After he left the room and quite some time had passed, I started to look at some books around me.</t468> <t469>One of them was an atlas that, as if frequently used, naturally opened to England.</t469> <t470>When I looked at the map, I saw that certain places were circled and upon examining these marks, I realized that one of them was at a point near the east side of London, clearly where his new property was located; the other two were in Exeter and Whitby on the Yorkshire coast.</t470>
<t471>When the Count returned, half an hour had passed.</t471> <t472>“Aha!” he said, “Are you still with your books?</t472> <t473>Good! But you must not work all the time.</t473> <t474>Come; it was said that your dinner is ready.”</t474> <t475>He took me by the arm and we went to the next room where a perfect dinner was ready on the table.</t475> <t476>The Count once again excused himself, saying that he had eaten while he was out.</t476> <t477>But like the previous night, he sat and chatted with me while I ate my meal.</t477> <t478>After dinner, just like the previous night, I smoked a cigar, and the Count stayed with me for hours, chatting and asking questions on all possible topics.</t478> <t479>I felt that it was really late, but I said nothing because I felt I had to fulfill my host's wishes in every aspect.</t479> <t480>Since the long sleep from the previous day had refreshed me, I was not sleepy; but I couldn't help feeling the chill that comes at dawn and resembles the change in tide.</t480> <t481>They say that people close to death often die at dawn or when the tide changes, and anyone who is tired and remains on duty to experience this change can believe this view.</t481> <t482>In the clean morning air, we suddenly heard a rooster crow with an unusual sharpness; Count Dracula, who jumped to his feet, said:</t482>
<t483>“Yaa! It's morning again!</t483> <t484>How careless of me to keep you up for so long.</t484> <t485>To ensure I don't lose track of time, you should make your conversations about my dear new homeland, England, less captivating.”</t485> <t486>After saying this, he respectfully bowed and left my side.</t486>
<t487>I went to my room and drew the curtains, but there was very little to catch the eye; my window opened to the courtyard, and the only thing I could see was the warm grayness of the illuminated sky.</t487> <t488>So I drew the curtains once more and wrote down what happened today.</t488>
<t489>8 May.</t489> <t490>- I have started to worry that I am getting too distracted while writing in this notebook; but now I am glad that I have gone into details from the beginning, because there is something so strange about this place that I cannot help but feel anxious while I am here.</t490> <t491>I wish I had left here safely or never come at all.</t491> <t492>This strange nocturnal life might be affecting me badly; but I wish that was all!</t492> <t493>If there was someone I could talk to, I could endure it, but there is no one.</t493> <t494>I can only talk to the Count!</t494> <t495>- I am afraid I am the only living being here.</t495> <t496>I must be as ordinary as the facts; this will help me endure; my imagination must not find an empty field and rise up against me.</t496> <t497>If it does, I will be ruined.</t497> <t498>Let me immediately explain how I endure or seem to endure.</t498>
<t499>When I went to bed, I could only sleep for a few hours and got up feeling that I couldn't sleep any longer.</t499> <t500>I had hung my shaving mirror on the window and was about to start shaving.</t500> <t501>Suddenly, I felt a hand on my shoulder and heard the Count's voice saying, "Good morning."</t501> <t502>I was startled because I hadn't seen him, as the reflection in the mirror covered the entire room behind me.</t502> <t503>When I was startled, I slightly cut my face, but I didn't realize it at that moment.</t503> <t504>I responded to the Count's greeting and turned back to the mirror to see how I had been mistaken.</t504> <t505>This time, there could be no mistake because the man was close to me and I could see him over my shoulder.</t505> <t506>But there was no reflection of him in the mirror!</t506> <t507>The entire room behind me was visible; but there was no sign of anyone else besides myself.</t507> <t508>This situation was frightening, and piling on top of so many strange things, the vague unease I always felt when the Count was near began to increase, but just then I saw that the cut was bleeding slightly; the blood was running down to my chin.</t508> <t509>I slightly turned to look for a bandage and put down the razor.</t509> <t510>When he saw my face, the Count's eyes gleamed with a demonic rage, and suddenly he grabbed my throat.</t510> <t511>I quickly pulled back and, well, touched the string of the rosary holding the cross.</t511> <t512>This caused an abrupt change in him; his anger passed so quickly that I could barely believe it had existed before.</t512>
<t513>“Be careful,” he said, “be careful how you cut yourself.</t513> <t514>This situation is more dangerous in this country than you think.”</t514> <t515>Then, taking the shaving mirror in his hand, he continued: “And here is the pitiable thing that causes harm.</t515> <t516>The disgusting and meaningless ornament of human arrogance.</t516> <t517>Throw it away,” he said, opening the heavy window with a single stroke of his terrible hand and hurling the mirror outside; the mirror shattered into a thousand pieces on the stone floor of the courtyard below.</t517> <t518>Then, without saying a word, he left the room.</t518> <t519>This is very frustrating, because if it weren't for the protective cover of my watch or the bottom of my shaving bowl, which luckily is metal, I don't know how I would shave.</t519>
<t520>When I went to the dining room, breakfast was ready; but I couldn't find the Count anywhere.</t520> <t521>Therefore, I had my breakfast alone.</t521> <t522>It's strange that I haven't seen the Count eating or drinking anything so far.</t522> <t523>He must be someone out of the ordinary!</t523> <t524>After breakfast, I went on a small exploration of the castle.</t524> <t525>I climbed the stairs and found a room facing south.</t525> <t526>The view was magnificent and offered every opportunity to see it from where I stood.</t526> <t527>The castle was on the edge of a terrifying cliff.</t527> <t528>A stone dropped from the window could fall three hundred meters without hitting anything!</t528> <t529>In the distance, as far as the eye could see, there was a sea of green treetops; occasionally, there were deep ravines where the cliff was.</t529> <t530>Among them, silvery lines stretched where the river wound through deep passes in the forest.</t530>
<t531>But I am not in the mood to describe the beauty, because after watching the scenery, I did some more exploration; doors, doors, everywhere doors and all of them locked and bolted.</t531> <t532>On the castle walls, there is no proper exit except for the windows.</t532>
<t533>The castle is a complete prison, and I am a prisoner!</t533>
<t534>III</t534>
<t535>Jonathan Harker's journal (continued)</t535>
<t536>I was almost out of my mind when I realized I was a prisoner.</t536><t537>I frantically tried every door I could find and looked out of every window, running up and down the stairs; but soon my belief in my helplessness overshadowed everything else.</t537><t538>Looking back a few hours later, I think I must have lost my mind for a short time, because I was acting like a trapped rat.</t538><t539>But when I concluded that I was helpless, I sat down quietly -more quietly than I had ever done in my life- and began to think about what the best course of action would be.</t539><t540>I am still thinking and have not yet come to a definite decision.</t540><t541>I am sure of only one thing: There is no point in explaining my thoughts to the Count.</t541><t542>He knows very well that I am imprisoned here; since he is the one who did it and undoubtedly has his reasons for it, if I trust him with these facts, he will only deceive me.</t542><t543>As far as I can see, my only plan is to keep what I know and fear to myself and stay alert.</t543><t544>I know that either I am being fooled like a baby by my own fears, or I am in a terrible predicament; if it is the latter, I need all my wits and will need them in the future as well.</t544><t545>I had barely come to this decision when I heard the great door below close and realized that the Count had returned.</t545><t546>He did not come to the library immediately, so I carefully went to my own room and found him making the bed.</t546><t547>This was a strange situation, but it confirmed what I had thought from the beginning, that there were no servants in the house.</t547><t548>Later, when I saw him setting the table in the dining room through the crack in the door hinge, I became even more certain; if he was doing all these servant tasks himself, it was proof that there was no one else to do them.</t548><t549>This situation frightened me, because if there was no one else in the castle, the driver of the carriage that brought me here must also have been the Count himself.</t549><t550>This is a terrifying thought; because if so, what does it mean that he could control the wolves by silently raising his hand?</t550><t551>How was it that everyone in Bistriţa and in the carriage was afraid for me?</t551><t552>What did it mean to be given a cross, garlic, wild rose, and rowan?</t552><t553>God bless the good woman who hung the cross around my neck, for every time I touch it, it gives me peace and strength.</t553><t554>How strange that something I was taught to approach with disapproval and see as idolatry is helping me in a time of loneliness and trouble.</t554><t555>Is there something in the nature of this object, or is it a tangible aid that carries memories of love and peace?</t555><t556>If possible, I must investigate this matter and come to a conclusion about it someday.</t556><t557>In the meantime, I must learn everything I can about Count Dracula, as it may help me understand what is happening.</t557><t558>Tonight, if I steer the conversation that way, he might talk about himself.</t558><t559>But I must be very careful not to arouse suspicion.</t559>
<t560>Midnight.</t560> <t561>- I had a long conversation with the Count.</t561> <t562>I asked him a few questions about the history of Transylvania, and he was filled with impeccable enthusiasm on the subject.</t562> <t563>When he spoke of events and people, but especially of wars, he talked as if he had been part of them all.</t563> <t564>Later, while explaining this, he said that for a boyar, the pride of his house and name is his own pride, their glory is his own glory, and their fate is his own fate.</t564> <t565>Whenever he spoke of his house, he always said "we," and he always spoke in the plural as if a king were speaking.</t565> <t566>I wish I could have recorded his words exactly as he expressed them, because it was utterly fascinating to me.</t566> <t567>What he narrated seemed to encompass the entire history of the country.</t567> <t568>As he spoke, his excitement grew, and he wandered around the room, tugging at his large white mustache and grasping everything in his path as if he would crush it with great force.</t568> <t569>Since he told the story of his race in his unique way, I will put down some of his words as close to the original as possible:</t569>
<t570>“We Seklers have the right to be proud, because in our veins flows the blood of many brave races who fought like lions for mastery.</t570> <t571>The Finno-Ugric peoples brought the warrior spirit from Iceland to here, into the whirlpool of European races, given to them by Thor and Odin, and demonstrated with a terror that created the impression that werewolves had arrived in the coastal regions of Europe, yes, and also in the coastal regions of Asia and Africa.</t571> <t572>When they arrived here, they found the Huns, who swept across the earth like a living flame with their warrior fury, making the dying people think that the blood of those ancient witches, driven from Scythian lands and mating with desert demons, flowed in their veins.</t572> <t573>Fools! Fools! What devil or witch could be as great as Attila, whose blood flows in these veins?”</t573> <t574>He raised his arms.</t574> <t575>“Is it surprising that we are a conquering race; that we are proud; that when the Hungarians, Lombards, Avars, Bulgars, or Turks poured thousands into our borders, we repelled them?</t575> <t576>Is it strange that when Árpád and his forces swept through the homeland of the Hungarians and reached the border, they found us here, completing the Honfoglalás here?</t576> <t577>And when the Hungarian incursion swept eastward, the Seklers were considered relatives of the victorious Hungarians, and for centuries, the task of guarding the border of the Turkish country was entrusted to us; yes, and beyond that, the eternal duty of border protection - for, as the Turks say, ‘Water sleeps, the enemy does not’ - which of the ‘Four Nations’ that make up Transylvania took the ‘bloody sword’ with greater satisfaction than us, or who gathered under the King’s banner more quickly when the call to arms was made?</t577> <t578>When was the great shame of my nation, the shame of Kosovo, when the flags of the Vlachs and Hungarians remained under the Crescent, ever compensated?</t578> <t579>Was it not one of my race, as Voivode, who crossed the Danube and defeated the Turks in their own lands?</t579> <t580>He was indeed a Dracula!</t580> <t581>Shame on his worthless brother who, when defeated, sold his people to the Turks and subjected them to the shame of captivity!</t581> <t582>Indeed, was it not this Dracula who inspired another member of his race in later centuries to repeatedly cross the great river with his forces into Turkish lands; or, when repelled, to emerge again, again, and again, even if he alone survived the bloody battlefield where his troops were slaughtered, knowing he could achieve absolute victory alone?</t582> <t583>They said he thought only of himself.</t583> <t584>Pah! What use are peasants without their leaders?</t584> <t585>Where does war end without a brain and heart to lead?</t585> <t586>Again, after the Battle of Mohács, it was we who threw off the Hungarian yoke; we, those descended from Dracula’s blood, were among the leaders, because our spirit could not endure being unfree.</t586> <t587>Ah! Young gentleman, the Seklers - and the Draculas as the blood, brains, and swords of their hearts - can boast of a kind of fame that the mushroom-like Habsburgs and Romanovs could never possess.</t587> <t588>The days of war are over.</t588> <t589>In these disgraceful days of peace, blood is far too precious a thing, and the glories of great races are like tales told.</t589><t590>"</t590>
<t591>It was almost morning, and we went to bed.</t591> <t592>(Note: This diary is starting to resemble the beginning of One Thousand and One Nights quite badly, as everything has to be interrupted by the crowing of a rooster - or it resembles the ghost of Hamlet's father.</t592><t593>)</t593>
<t594>May 12.</t594> <t595>-Let me begin with facts- simple, insufficient, and undeniable facts verified by books and numbers.</t595> <t596>I must mix them with my own experiences that should remain in my observations and memories about them.</t596> <t597>Last night, when the Count left his room, he started by asking me questions about legal matters and how certain tasks should be done.</t597> <t598>I spent the day buried in books, tired and weary, and just to distract my mind, I went over some topics I had studied at Lincoln's Inn.</t598> <t599>There was a certain method in the Count's research; therefore, I must try to note them in a particular order; this information might be useful to me in some way or at some point.</t599>
<t600>First, he asked whether a person in England could have two or more legal advisors.</t600> <t601>I told him that if he wished, he could retain a dozen, but it would not be wise to appoint more than one legal advisor for a single transaction, as only one could act at a time and changing this situation would not be in his best interest.</t601> <t602>He seemed to understand the situation deeply and continued the conversation by asking whether it would cause practical difficulties to appoint another person, for example, to handle transportation matters if his advisor dealing with banking needed local assistance for a job in another country.</t602> <t603>To avoid misleading him in any way, I asked him to explain in more detail, and he said:</t603>
<t604>“Let me give you an example.</t604> <t605>Our mutual friend Mr. Peter Hawkins, from the shadow of your beautiful cathedral in Exeter, which is quite far from London, is purchasing my house in London through your trustworthy person.</t605> <t606>Good! So that you do not think it strange that I seek the services of someone so far away instead of someone living in London, I must clearly state here that my reason was to avoid serving any local interest other than my own; someone living in London might aim to serve themselves or a friend, so I sought a representative who would work solely for my benefit.</t606> <t607>Now, let's assume that I, being very busy, wanted to ship goods by sea to, say, Newcastle, Durham, Harwich, or Dover. Wouldn't it be easier to entrust the task to someone at those ports?”</t607> <t608>I said that it would undoubtedly be easier, but we legal advisors have a proxy system, so local matters can be handled locally with an instruction from any legal advisor, allowing the client to have their desires fulfilled without facing more issues by placing themselves in the hands of a single person.</t608>
<t609>“But,” he said, “I can be free to manage my own affairs.</t609> <t610>Isn't that right?</t610><t611>”</t611>
<t612>“Of course,” I replied; “businessmen who do not want any of their affairs to be learned by anyone often resort to this method.</t612><t613>”</t613>
<t614>“Beautiful!” he said and continued asking questions about ways to make deliveries, the routes to follow, and any difficulties that could be prevented by taking precautions.</t614> <t615>I explained all of this to him as best as I could, and he gave me the impression that he could be an excellent legal advisor, because there wasn't a single thing he hadn't thought of or foreseen beforehand.</t615> <t616>For someone who had never been in the country and clearly hadn't been much involved in business, his knowledge and intelligence were excellent.</t616> <t617>After satisfying himself on these points and after I had verified everything as best as I could through the available books, he suddenly stood up and said: “Since the first letter you wrote to our friend Mr. Peter Hawkins, have you written to him or anyone else?”</t617> <t618>With a bit of unease in my heart, I said that I hadn't, that I hadn't yet had the opportunity to send a letter to anyone.</t618>
<t619>“Then write now, my young friend,” he said, placing his heavy hand on my shoulder.</t619> <t620>“Write to our friend and others, and if you like, tell them you will stay with me for another month.”</t620> <t621>“Do you want me to stay that long?” I asked, for my heart had frozen at the thought.</t621>
<t622>“I want it very much; no, I do not accept objections.</t622> <t623>Your master, your employer, however you call him, it was understood that only my needs would be considered when someone was decided to replace him.</t623> <t624>I did not spare any expense.</t624> <t625>Isn't that so?</t625><t626>”</t626>
<t627>What else could I do but accept this situation and submit?</t627> <t628>The matter at hand was not my interest but Mr. Hawkins', and I had to think of him, not myself; besides, there was something in Count Dracula's eyes and behavior that reminded me I was a prisoner and suggested that I had no other choice even if I wanted one.</t628> <t629>The Count saw his triumph in my submission and his dominance in my unease, for he immediately began to use these with his own soft and yielding manner: "I beg you, my dear young friend, do not speak of matters other than business in your letters.</t629> <t630>Surely, your friends will be pleased to learn that you are well and eagerly awaiting your return to them.</t630> <t631>Isn't that so?"</t631> <t632>As he said this, he handed me three sheets of letter paper and three envelopes.</t632> <t633>They were all of the finest kind used in overseas mail, and when I looked at the papers and then at the Count, I noticed him silently smiling with his sharp canine tooth protruding over his red lower lip, as if to say aloud that I should be careful about what I wrote because he could read it.</t633> <t634>Therefore, I decided to write only formal letters for now but to secretly write everything to Mr. Hawkins and Mina—because I could write to her in shorthand, which would confuse the Count if he saw the letter.</t634> <t635>After writing my two letters, I sat quietly reading a book; meanwhile, the Count wrote a few notes, consulting some books on his desk.</t635> <t636>Then, he took my two letters and placed them with his own by the writing materials; as soon as the door closed behind him, I leaned over to look at the letters, their faces turned to the table.</t636> <t637>I felt no remorse in doing this because, under these circumstances, I felt I had to protect myself in every way I could.</t637>
<t638>One of the letters was addressed to Samuel F.</t638> <t639>Billington, No.</t639> <t640>7, Crescent, Whitby, another to Herr Leuther, Varna; the third to Coutts & Co., London, and the fourth to Herren Klopstock & Billreuth, bankers, Budapest.</t640> <t641>The second and fourth letters were unsealed.</t641> <t642>I was just about to look at them when I saw the door handle move.</t642> <t643>Before the Count, holding another letter, entered the room, I had enough time to put the letters back in their places, return to my book, and settle into my chair.</t643> <t644>The Count took the letters from the table, carefully affixed the stamps, and then turned to me and said:</t644>
<t645>“I believe you will forgive me, but I have a lot of work to do alone tonight.</t645> <t646>I hope you find everything as you wish.”</t646> <t647>He turned at the door and after a moment's hesitation, he added:</t647>
<t648>“Let me give you some advice, my dear young friend - no, let me warn you in all seriousness - if you ever leave these rooms, do not sleep anywhere else in the castle under any circumstances.</t648> <t649>The castle is old, it holds many memories and bad dreams for those who sleep unwisely.</t649> <t650>Be careful!</t650> <t651>If now or in the future sleep overcomes you or seems about to overcome you, immediately return to your own room or one of these rooms so that your sleep will be safe.</t651> <t652>But if you are not careful about this, then,” - He ended his speech in a terrifying manner, as if he was making a gesture of washing his hands.</t652> <t653>I understood very well; my only doubt was whether any dream could be more terrifying than the strange, dreadful darkness and web of mystery that seemed to surround me.</t653>
<t654>Later.</t654> <t655>- I confirm the last words I wrote, but this time there is no doubt.</t655> <t656>I will not be afraid to sleep anywhere he is not.</t656> <t657>I hung the cross at the head of my bed - thus I assume my sleep will be free from dreams; the cross will stay there.</t657>
<t658>When the Count left my side, I went to my room.</t658> <t659>Shortly after, not hearing any sound, I went outside and climbed the stone stairs from which I could look south.</t659> <t660>Compared to the narrow darkness of the courtyard, there was a sense of freedom in the vast area I saw, even though it was unattainable.</t660> <t661>Looking at the view, I truly felt that I was being held in a prison, and despite it being night, I seemed to want to take a breath of fresh air.</t661> <t662>I began to feel that this nocturnal way of life was affecting me badly.</t662> <t663>It's getting on my nerves.</t663> <t664>I'm afraid of my own shadow, and my mind is filled with all sorts of terrifying imaginations.</t664> <t665>God knows, there is ample ground for every kind of horrifying fear in this cursed place!</t665> <t666>I looked at the beautiful expanse bathed in the soft, yellow moonlight until it was almost as bright as day.</t666> <t667>Under the soft light, the distant hills, the shadows of the valleys, and the velvety black passes melted away.</t667> <t668>This simple beauty seemed to have cheered me up; there was peace and comfort in every breath I took.</t668> <t669>When I leaned out of the window, something moving caught my eye, a floor below, slightly to my left, in the place where I assumed the windows of the Count's own room would be, according to the arrangement of the rooms.</t669> <t670>The window I stood at was high, deep, and stone-latticed, and although it was weather-worn, it was still in perfect condition; but it was very clear that the window frame had been here for a long time.</t670> <t671>I pulled back behind the stonework and looked out carefully.</t671>
<t672>What I saw was the Count's head sticking out of the window.</t672> <t673>I couldn't see his face, but I recognized the man by his neck and the movement of his back and arms.</t673> <t674>In any case, it was impossible not to recognize the hands I had so many opportunities to examine.</t674> <t675>This situation first caught my interest and then somehow amused me; it's amazing how even such a small matter can catch and amuse one's interest when one is a captive.</t675> <t676>But when I saw the man slowly emerging from the window, descending down the castle wall into the terrifying void, his cloak spread around him like wide wings, crawling face down, my feelings turned to disgust and horror.</t676> <t677>At first, I couldn't believe my eyes.</t677> <t678>I thought it was some kind of trick played by the moonlight, a strange effect of the shadow; but I kept looking; it couldn't be an optical illusion.</t678> <t679>I saw his fingers and toes grasping the edges of the stones, whose mortar had worn away over the years, and thus, like a lizard moving on the wall, he used every protrusion and roughness to make his way down.</t679>
<t680>What kind of person is this, or what kind of creature in the guise of a human?</t680> <t681>I feel that the horror of this dreadful place has deeply affected me; I am in fear -great fear- and there is no escape for me; I am surrounded by fears that I dare not even think about...</t681>
<t682>15 May.</t682> <t683>- I saw the Count slipping out like a lizard once again.</t683> <t684>He was moving sideways, descending about thirty meters down and quite a bit to the left.</t684> <t685>He disappeared into a hole or a window.</t685> <t686>When his head vanished from sight, I leaned out to see more, but it was no use - the distance was too great to allow a proper viewing angle.</t686> <t687>I knew he had left the castle, and I thought of using this opportunity to explore more than I had dared so far.</t687> <t688>I returned to the room, took the lamp, and tried all the doors.</t688> <t689>As I had guessed, they were all locked, and the locks were relatively new; but I went down the stone stairs to the hall where I had first entered.</t689> <t690>I found that I could easily pull the bolts and remove the huge chains, but the door was locked and there was no key!</t690> <t691>That key must be in the Count's room; I must watch for a time when the door to his room is not locked so I can take the key and escape.</t691> <t692>I continued to carefully examine various stairs and corridors, trying the doors that opened onto them.</t692> <t693>A few small rooms near the hall had open doors, but inside there was nothing to see except old, moth-eaten furniture covered in years of dust.</t693> <t694>But finally, at the top of a staircase, I found a door that, although it appeared to be locked, opened with a bit of force.</t694> <t695>I pushed harder and saw that it was not truly locked, the resistance came from the hinges somehow dropping, and the heavy door was resting on the ground.</t695> <t696>This was an opportunity that might not come again, so after using all my strength and many attempts, I pushed it back enough to get inside.</t696> <t697>Now, I was in the right wing of the castle, one floor below the rooms I knew.</t697> <t698>From the window, I could see that the connected rooms extended along the south wing of the castle, with the room at the end facing both west and south.</t698> <t699>As on the first side, there was a deep chasm on the second side as well.</t699> <t700>The castle was built on the corner of a large rock, making it quite impregnable from three sides, and the large windows were placed where no slingshot, arrow, or rifle could reach, thus providing light and comfort impossible for a place that needed to be defended.</t700> <t701>To the west, there was a wide valley and behind it, in the distance, rows of sharp-peaked mountains rising summit upon summit, with rowan trees and thorny bushes clinging to the cracks, crevices, and fissures in the rock.</t701> <t702>This part of the castle was evidently inhabited in the past because the furniture had a more comfortable air than what I had seen before.</t702> <t703>There were no curtains on the windows, and the yellow moonlight streaming through the diamond-shaped window panes weakened the layer of dust covering everything, somewhat concealing the damage caused by time and moths, making it possible to see colors.</t703> <t704>Under the bright moonlight, my lamp seemed almost useless, but I was glad to have it with me because there was a dreadful loneliness in this place that chilled my blood and unnerved me.</t704> <t705>Still, it was better than being alone in the rooms I had come to hate due to the Count's presence, and <t709>Later: the morning of May 16.</t709> <t710>- My God, keep my mind safe, because in the end, I have fallen to this state.</t710> <t711>Security and the assurance of security are things of the past.</t711> <t712>During my time here, there is only one thing to wish for: Not to go mad, that is, if I am not already mad.</t712> <t713>If I am in my right mind, it is truly maddening to think that among the horrible things lurking in this hateful place, the least terrifying for me is the Count, and that as long as I work for his purpose, the only person I can go to for safety is the Count.</t713> <t714>Oh, Almighty God! Merciful God! <t718>I must write these down...</t718> <t719>11</t719>
<t720>Now I feel as if my mind has lost its balance or as if the shock that should end its ruin has come, and I turn to my journal for peace.</t720> <t721>The habit of writing everything down completely will comfort me.</t721>

<t724>After writing in my journal and fortunately putting the notebook and pen in my pocket, I felt sleepy.</t724> <t725>I remembered the Count's warning, but I enjoyed defying him.</t725> <t726>The feeling of sleep had settled over me, and stubbornness had come along as sleep's servant.</t726> <t727>The soft moonlight was soothing me, and the vastness outside was giving me a sense of freedom that delighted me.</t727> <t728>Tonight, I decided not to return to those gloomy rooms and to sleep in this room where, in old times, ladies with sensitive hearts would sit and sing in sorrow because their men were far away in merciless wars, and they lived sweet lives.</t728> <t729>I pulled a large sofa close to the corner so that I could watch the beautiful view of the east and south while lying down and prepare myself for sleep without worrying about the dust.</t729>
<t730>I must have fallen asleep; I hope so, but I fear what happened afterward was terrifyingly real - so real that now, as I sit here in the bright daylight of the morning, I can't believe even a little that it was all a dream.</t730>
<t731>I was not alone.</t731> <t732>The room was the same, it hadn't changed at all since I entered; in the bright moonlight, I could see the long dust trails disturbed by my own footprints all across the floor.</t732> <t733>In the moonlight, directly in front of me were three young women; judging by their clothes and demeanor, they were noble ladies.</t733> <t734>At that moment, when I saw them, I thought I was dreaming, because despite the moonlight being behind them, their shadows did not fall on the ground.</t734> <t735>They approached me and looked at me for a while, then whispered together.</t735> <t736>Two of them were brunettes and had high noses resembling an eagle's beak like the Count's, and large, dark, piercing eyes that seemed almost red compared to the pale, yellow moon.</t736> <t737>The other was as blonde as could be, with wavy golden hair and pale, sapphire-like eyes.</t737> <t738>It was as if I knew her face from somewhere, in connection with an imaginary fear, but at that moment, I couldn't figure out how and where I knew her from.</t738> <t739>All three had dazzling white teeth that shone like pearls against the redness of their voluptuous lips.</t739> <t740>There was something about them that made me uneasy, a bit of longing and at the same time, a deadly fear.</t740> <t741>In my heart, I felt a wicked, burning desire for them to kiss me with those red lips.</t741> <t742>It's not good for me to write these here, as one day Mina might see them and it could cause her pain, but this is the truth.</t742> <t743>They whispered and then all three laughed - such silvery and harmonious, yet harsh laughs that seemed like they could never come from the softness of human lips.</t743> <t744>It was like the unbearable, chilling delight that comes from a glass of water when played by a skillful hand.</t744> <t745>The blonde girl coquettishly nodded her head and the other two encouraged her.</t745> <t746>One of them said:</t746>
<t747>"Come on! You are first and we will follow you; the right to start is yours."</t747><t748>"</t748>
<t749>The other added:</t749>
<t750>“A young and strong man; there are kisses for all of us.”</t750> <t751>I lay silently, looking from under my eyelashes with the pain of a sweet anticipation.</t751> <t752>The blonde girl walked over and continued to lean over me until I could feel the movement of her breath.</t752> <t753>In one sense, it was sweet - sweet as honey, I felt the shiver caused by her voice in my nerves, but like the smell of blood, there was a painful, painful ugliness lying beneath the sweetness.</t753>
<t754>I was afraid to lift my eyelids, but I looked from under my eyelashes and saw perfectly.</t754> <t755>The blonde girl knelt down and leaned over me with considerable pleasure.</t755> <t756>There was a conscious lust in her actions that was both exciting and disgusting, and she licked her lips like an animal as she bent her neck backward; until I saw the wetness shining on her red tongue moving over her crimson lips and sharp white teeth in the moonlight.</t756> <t757>Her head descended lower and lower, as if her lips were about to slip under my mouth and chin and sink into my throat.</t757> <t758>Then she stopped, and I could hear the slurping sound her tongue made as she licked her teeth and lips, feeling her hot breath on my neck.</t758> <t759>Then, the skin of my throat began to shiver as it does when a hand approaches to tickle it.</t759> <t760>On the overly sensitive skin of my throat, I could feel the soft, chilling touch of her lips and the touch and wait of her sharp teeth.</t760> <t761>In a state of dizzying ecstasy, I closed my eyes and waited - waited with a pounding heart.</t761>
<t762>But at that very moment, another feeling spread through me with the speed of lightning.</t762> <t763>I felt the presence of the Count and that he was caught in a storm of rage.</t763> <t764>When my eyes involuntarily opened, I saw the Count's strong hand grasping the slender neck of the blonde woman and pulling her back with the strength of a giant, his blue eyes changing with anger, his white teeth clashing with fury, and his pale cheeks burning with passion.</t764> <t765>But the Count! <t771>“With what audacity do any of you dare touch him?</t771> <t772>How dare you look at him when I have forbidden it?</t772> <t773>Step back, I tell you!</t773> <t774>This man belongs to me!</t774> <t775>Do not mess with him or you will have to deal with me.</t775><t776>”</t776>
<t777>The blonde girl, laughing with a suggestive coquetry, replied to the Count:</t777>
<t778>“You never loved yourself; you never love at all!”</t778> <t779>The other women joined in, and such joyless, harsh, soulless laughter echoed in the room that hearing it almost made me faint; it was like the joy of demons.</t779> <t780>After carefully looking at my face, the Count turned and said in a soft whisper:</t780>

<t787>One of them pointed to the bag that the Count had thrown to the ground, which moved as if something alive was inside, and said with a low laugh, "Aren't we going to drink anything tonight?"</t787> <t788>The Count nodded in response, as if to say yes.</t788> <t789>One of the women sprang forward and opened the bag.</t789> <t790>If my ears did not deceive me, I heard sounds of labored breathing and moaning, as if from a half-drowned child.</t790> <t791>While I was frozen with fear, the women gathered around the bag; but when I looked, they had vanished, and the dreadful bag had disappeared with them.</t791> <t792>There was no door nearby, and they could not have passed by me without my noticing.</t792> <t793>They seemed to have flown out through the window among the moonbeams, for outside, I could see faint shapes for a moment before they completely vanished.</t793>
<t794>Then terror overcame me and I lost consciousness.</t794>
<t795>IV</t795>
<t796>Jonathan Harker's journal (continued)</t796>
<t797>I woke up in my own bed.</t797> <t798>If I didn't dream, the Count must have carried me here.</t798> <t799>I tried to find a convincing explanation, but I couldn't reach a definite conclusion.</t799> <t800>Undoubtedly, there were some small pieces of evidence, like my clothes being folded and placed in a manner that is not my habit.</t800> <t801>My watch was not wound, and the last thing I would do before going to bed would certainly be to wind it; many other details like this.</t801> <t802>But these cannot be evidence, as they could be proof that my mind is not as usual and for one reason or another, there is no doubt that I was all mixed up.</t802> <t803>I must be careful to find evidence.</t803> <t804>I am pleased about one thing: If the Count carried me here and undressed me, he must have done it in a hurry because my pockets were untouched.</t804> <t805>I am sure this journal would be an irresistible mystery for him.</t805> <t806>He would have taken and destroyed it.</t806> <t807>Although it is filled with fear for me, as I look at my room now, it seems like a kind of refuge because nothing can be more terrifying than those dreadful women waiting to suck my blood -continuing to wait.</t807>
<t808>May 18.</t808> <t809>- I went down to look at that room again in daylight, because I must learn the truth.</t809> <t810>When I reached the door at the top of the stairs, I saw that it was closed.</t810> <t811>The frame had been pushed with such great force that the wooden joinery in that part was shattered.</t811> <t812>I could see the latch tongue inside, but the door was bolted from the inside.</t812> <t813>I'm afraid what I experienced was not a dream, and I had to act according to this belief.</t813>
<t814>May 19.</t814> <t815>- It is certain that I have fallen into a trap like an animal.</t815> <t816>Last night, the Count, with a pleasant but deceptive demeanor, asked me to write three letters: one stating that my work here is almost finished and that I will be heading home in a few days, another saying that I will leave the day after writing the letter, and the third indicating that I have left the castle and arrived in Bistriţa.</t816> <t817>I wanted to oppose this, but given that I am entirely under his control at the moment, I felt that openly arguing with the Count would be madness, and refusing his request would arouse suspicion and anger him.</t817> <t818>He knows that I know too much and that I must die so that I won't be a danger to him; my only chance is to bide my time.</t818> <t819>Something might come up that will give me a chance to escape.</t819> <t820>A kind of rage, similar to the fury that appeared in his eyes when he threw that blonde woman away from himself, is gathering in his eyes.</t820> <t821>He said that the postal service is sparse and unreliable, and that writing now would put my friends at ease, and he so insistently assured me that if I had the chance to extend my stay here, he would cancel the forward-dated letters to be held in Bistriţa until the time came, that opposing him would have aroused new suspicions.</t821> <t822>So I pretended to agree with him and asked what dates I should put on the letters.</t822> <t823>He calculated for a minute and then said:</t823>
<t824>"The first should be June 12, the second June 19, and the third June 29."</t824><t825></t825>
<t826>Now I know the rest of my life.</t826> <t827>My God, help me!</t827>
<t828>May 28.</t828> <t829>- There is a chance for an escape or at least to send news home.</t829> <t830>A group of Gypsies came to the castle and set up camp in the courtyard.</t830> <t831>I have notes about these Gypsies in my notebook.</t831> <t832>Although they are related to the ordinary Gypsies around the world, they are unique to this part of the world.</t832> <t833>In Hungary and Transylvania, there are thousands of them, almost all of whom are lawless.</t833> <t834>As a rule, they attach themselves to a great noble or boyar and take his name.</t834> <t835>They are fearless, godless except for superstitions, and speak a unique type of the Romanian language.</t835>
<t836>I will try to write a few letters and have these Gypsies mail them.</t836> <t837>I even spoke to them from my window to establish some sort of acquaintance.</t837> <t838>They took off their hats, bowed before me, and made many signs that I couldn't understand, just as I couldn't understand their spoken language...</t838>
<t839>I wrote the letters.</t839> <t840>I wrote Mina’s in shorthand and asked Mr. Hawkins to speak only with Mina.</t840> <t841>I explained my situation to Mina without mentioning the horrors I could only speculate about.</t841> <t842>If I open my heart to her, it would shake her greatly and she would die of fear.</t842> <t843>If the letters do not go, the Count will still learn my secret and the extent of what I know.</t843>
<t844>I gave the letters; I threw them along with a gold coin through the bars of my window and made all the signs I could to ensure they would be mailed.</t844> <t845>The man who received the letters pressed them to his chest, bowed, and placed them under his hat.</t845> <t846>There was nothing more I could do.</t846> <t847>I returned to the study and began to read a book.</t847> <t848>Since the Count did not come, I started to write here...</t848>
<t849>The count arrived.</t849> <t850>He sat next to me and, while opening the two letters, said in the softest voice: “The Gypsies, although I do not know where they came from, gave me these letters which I will of course take an interest in.</t850> <t851>Look!” - He must have looked inside.</t851> <t852>“One is from you to my friend Peter Hawkins; the other,” - here, as soon as he opened the letter and saw the strange symbols, a dark expression settled on his face and his eyes flared sinfully - “the other is something vile, a great insult to friendship and hospitality! <t856>“The letter to Hawkins, since it is yours, I will of course send it.</t856> <t857>Your letters are sacred to me.</t857> <t858>Forgive me, my friend, for breaking the seal unknowingly.</t858> <t859>Aren’t you going to seal it again?” He handed me the letter and, bowing politely, gave me a clean envelope.</t859> <t860>All I could do was rewrite the address and quietly hand the envelope to the Count.</t860> <t861>When he left the room, I heard the key turn slowly.</t861> <t862>A minute later, I looked at the door and tried it; it was locked.</t862>

<t871>May 31.</t871> <t872>- This morning, when I woke up, I thought of taking some paper and envelopes from my bag and keeping them in my pocket so that I could write if I got the chance; but again, a surprise, again a shock!</t872>

<t877>June 17.</t877> <t878>- This morning, while I was sitting on the edge of my bed, straining my mind, I heard the cracking of whips and the pounding of horses' hooves on the stony road beyond the courtyard.</t878> <t879>In high spirits, I ran to the window and saw two large wagons, each pulled by eight sturdy horses, entering the courtyard, with a Slovak at the head of each pair of horses, wearing a wide hat, a studded belt, dirty sheepskin, and high boots.</t879> <t880>They also had long sticks in their hands.</t880> <t881>I ran to the door to join them in the main hall, which I thought might have been opened for them.</t881> <t882>Another shock: My door was locked from the outside.</t882>

<t890>June 24, before sunrise.</t890> <t891>- The Count left my side early last night and locked himself in his room.</t891> <t892>As soon as I gathered my courage, I ran to the spiral staircase and looked out the window facing south.</t892> <t893>I thought of following the Count, because something was going on.</t893> <t894>The Gypsies were settled somewhere in the castle and were doing some kind of work.</t894> <t895>I know this because I occasionally hear the muffled sounds of digging and shoveling from afar, and whatever this is, it must be nearing the end of some cruel evil.</t895>

<t902>I thought, let me wait for Kont's return, and I stubbornly sat by the window for a long time.</t902> <t903>Then, I started to see small strange dots floating in the moonlight.</t903> <t904>They were like tiny dust particles, and I noticed that they were swirling and coming together like a cloud.</t904> <t905>I watched them in peace, and a kind of tranquility settled over me.</t905> <t906>To better enjoy this aerial display, I took a more comfortable position in the window frame and leaned back.</t906>

<t916>After a few hours had passed, I heard something stir in the Count's room, something like a sharp cry that was quickly stifled; then silence - a deep and terrible silence that made my hair stand on end.</t916> <t917>My heart pounding, I tried the door; but I was locked in my cell and there was nothing I could do.</t917> <t918>I sat down and cried.</t918>

<t923>“Monster! Give me my child!”</t923><t924>”</t924>
<t925>He threw himself on his knees and raised his hands, shouting the same words in tones that wrenched my heart.</t925> <t926>Then he tore at his hair and beat his chest, surrendering himself to the intensity of exaggerated emotions.</t926> <t927>Finally, he lunged forward; although I couldn't see him, I could hear him pounding on the door with his bare hands.</t927>

<t934>What will I do?</t934> <t935>What can I do?</t935> <t936>How can I escape and get rid of this terrifying captivity of night, gloom, and fear?</t936>
<t937>June 25, morning.</t937> <t938>- No one knows how sweet and precious the morning can seem to the heart and eyes without bearing the pain of the night.</t938> <t939>This morning, when the sun rose high enough to strike the top of the large door opposite my window, it seemed to me as if the pigeon on the arch was illuminated at the high point it touched.</t939> <t940>My fear flowed off me as if it were a garment made of steam, melting away in the heat.</t940> <t941>I must somehow take action while I have the courage of the day.</t941> <t942>Last night, one of my future-dated letters was mailed; the first in a deadly series that will erase all traces of my existence from the earth.</t942>

<t945>The times I was harassed or threatened or somehow fell into danger or fear were always at night.</t945> <t946>I have not yet seen the Count in daylight.</t946> <t947>Could he be sleeping while others are awake and awake while they are sleeping?</t947>

<t960>The same day, later.</t960> <t961>- I did my best and, with God's help, I returned safely to this room.</t961> <t962>I must write down all the details in order.</t962> <t963>While my courage was still fresh, I went straight to the window on the south side of the castle and immediately stepped out onto the narrow stone ledge that surrounds this side of the building.</t963> <t964>The stones were large and roughly cut, and the mortar between them had worn away over time.</t964> <t965>I took off my boots and embarked on this desperate path.</t965> <t966>So that I wouldn't suddenly see the terrifying depth and succumb to it, I looked down once, but then kept my eyes away from it.</t966> <t967>I knew the direction and the distance to the Count's window quite well, and I aimed there as best as I could to seize the opportunity.</t967> <t968>I didn't get dizzy - I think I was too excited - the time it took until I found myself standing at the window ledge trying to open the sash seemed ridiculously short.</t968> <t969>But I tensed up when I leaned in and my feet first slipped inside the window.</t969> <t970>Then I looked around for the Count but discovered something with surprise and delight.</t970> <t971>The room was empty!</t971> <t972>It was furnished with a few odd items that looked as if they had never been used; <t977>There was a heavy door in one corner of the room.</t977> <t978>I tried this door because I needed to investigate further, having not found the key to the room or the key to the outer door, which were the main subjects of my research, or all my efforts would be in vain.</t978> <t979>The door was open and led to a stone corridor that descended steeply to a spiral staircase.</t979> <t980>Since the steps were dark, illuminated only by the loopholes in the heavy stone walls, I descended carefully, watching my step.</t980> <t981>At the bottom, there was a dark, tunnel-like corridor from which emanated a deadly, nauseating smell, like the scent of old, overturned earth.</t981> <t982>As I progressed down the corridor, the smell grew closer and heavier.</t982> <t983>Finally, I opened the heavy door that was ajar and found myself in an old, abandoned chapel that was evidently used as a cemetery.</t983> <t984>The roof had collapsed, and there were steps leading down to underground tombs in two places, but the ground had been recently dug up, and the soil had clearly been filled into large wooden crates brought by the Slovaks.</t984> <t985>There was no one around, so I searched for another exit but found none.</t985> <t986>Then, to leave no stone unturned, I scanned every square inch of the floor.</t986> <t987>Despite my terror, I even descended into the dimly lit burial chambers where the light flickered.</t987> <t988>I entered two of them but saw nothing except old coffin fragments and piles of dust; however, in the third one, I discovered something.</t988>
<t989>Count was lying on top of a freshly dug mound of earth inside one of the large chests, which were about fifty in total!</t989> <t990>He was either dead or sleeping, I couldn't tell which, because his eyes were open and rigid - but there was no glassy look that comes with death - despite his pallor, there was a warmth of life in his cheeks and his lips were as red as ever.</t990> <t991>However, there was no sign of movement, pulse, breath, or heartbeat.</t991> <t992>I leaned over him and tried to find a sign of life, but it was in vain.</t992> <t993>He couldn't have been lying here for long because the smell of the earth would have dissipated within a few hours.</t993> <t994>Next to the chest, the lid, which had holes drilled here and there, was lying.</t994> <t995>I thought the keys might be on him, but when I started to search, I saw such a look of hatred in his dead eyes - even though they were dead, they were not aware of me or my presence - that I fled from there and left the Count's room through the window, crawling along the castle walls again.</t995> <t996>I returned to my room, threw myself onto the bed, breathless, and tried to think...</t996>
<t997>June 29.</t997> <t998>- Today is the day of my last letter, and the Count has taken the necessary steps to prove it is real because I saw him leaving the castle again through the same window and in my clothes.</t998> <t999>I wished I had a gun or a deadly weapon to destroy him as he descended the wall like a lizard; but I fear that no weapon made by human hands can have any effect on him.</t999> <t1000>I did not dare to wait for the Count's return because I was afraid of seeing those strange sisters.</t1000> <t1001>I returned to the library and read books there until I fell asleep.</t1001>
<t1002>I was awakened by the Count, who was looking at me with the wildest expression a person could have; he said:</t1002>
<t1003>“Tomorrow, my friend, we must part.</t1003> <t1004>You return to your beautiful England, and I will return to some of my affairs which may result in us never meeting again.</t1004> <t1005>The letter you wrote home has been sent; I will not be here tomorrow, but everything will be ready for your journey.</t1005> <t1006>In the morning, Gypsies and Slovaks who have some business here will arrive.</t1006> <t1007>When they leave, my carriage will come to pick you up and take you to the Borgo Pass to meet the coach going from Bistriţa to Bukovina.</t1007> <t1008>But I hope to see you more at Dracula’s Castle.”</t1008> <t1009>I was suspicious of him and decided to test his sincerity.</t1009> <t1010>Sincerity!</t1010> <t1011>It would be disrespectful to write this word in association with such a monster; so I asked him directly: “Why can’t I leave this evening?</t1011><t1012>”</t1012>
<t1013>“Because, dear sir, my coachman and my horses are not here as they have work to do.</t1013><t1014>”</t1014>
<t1015>"But I will walk gladly.</t1015> <t1016>I want to get away as soon as possible.</t1016><t1017>"</t1017>
<t1018>He smiled; it was such a soft, calm, and devilish smile that I knew there was a kind of trick beneath its softness.</t1018> <t1019>He said:</t1019>
<t1020>“What about your suitcases?</t1020><t1021>”</t1021>
<t1022>"I don't care.</t1022> <t1023>I can have them picked up later.</t1023><t1024>"</t1024>
<t1025>The count stood up and, with a sweetness that caused me to rub my eyes and seemed quite real, said:</t1025>
<t1026>“You English have a saying that greatly appeals to me because it governs our boyars: ‘Welcome the arrival of the guest, hasten their departure.’</t1026> <t1027>Come with me, my dear young friend.</t1027> <t1028>Although I am saddened by your departure and your sudden desire for it, do not stay in my home for even an hour against your will.</t1028> <t1029>Come!” With a lamp in hand, he descended the stairs with majestic dignity and proceeded ahead of me down the corridor.</t1029> <t1030>Suddenly, he stopped.</t1030> <t1031>“Listen!</t1031><t1032>”</t1032>
<t1033>The howling of many wolves was heard up close.</t1033> <t1034>The sound had almost begun with the raising of the Count's hand, just like the music of a large orchestra under the direction of a conductor.</t1034> <t1035>After a momentary hesitation, he advanced to the door with his majestic demeanor, pulled the heavy bolts, removed the heavy chains from their hooks, and began to open the door.</t1035>

<t1044>“Close the door; I will wait until morning!” And then, to hide the tears caused by bitter disappointment, I covered my face with my hands.</t1044> <t1045>The Count closed the door with a single movement of his strong arm, the large bolts clanged and settled into place, the sound echoing down the corridor.</t1045>
<t1046>We returned to the library in silence; a minute or two later, I went to my own room.</t1046> <t1047>The last time I saw Count Dracula, he was looking at me with a red glint of triumph in his eyes and a smile that could have made Judas in Hell proud, kissing his own hand.</t1047>

<t1056>I turned around and threw myself onto my knees.</t1056> <t1057>So, this is how close my end is, huh?</t1057> <t1058>Tomorrow! Tomorrow! God, help me and those who love me.</t1058>
<t1059>June 30, morning.</t1059> <t1060>- These might be the last words I write in this journal.</t1060> <t1061>I slept until just before dawn and when I woke up, I threw myself onto my knees because I had decided that if Death were to come, it should find me ready.</t1061>
<t1062>Finally, I felt the slight change in the air and realized that morning had come.</t1062> <t1063>Then, the crowing of the rooster welcoming the morning came, and I felt safe.</t1063> <t1064>With a content heart, I opened my door and ran downstairs to the hall.</t1064> <t1065>I had seen that the door was not locked, and now escape was before me.</t1065> <t1066>With hands trembling with eagerness, I unhooked the chains and pulled the mighty bolts.</t1066>

<t1072>Then, taking every risk, a wild desire to get hold of that key seized me; right there and then, I decided to climb the wall once more and reach the Count's room.</t1072> <t1073>He could kill me, but death was the best option among the evils.</t1073> <t1074>Without wasting any time, I ran to the east window and, as I had done before, crawled along the wall and descended into the Count's room.</t1074> <t1075>It was empty, but I was expecting that.</t1075> <t1076>I couldn't see the key anywhere, but the pile of gold was there.</t1076> <t1077>I passed through the door in the corner, went down the spiral staircase, and walked through the dark corridor leading to the old chapel.</t1077>
<t1078>Now I knew well enough where to find the monster I was looking for.</t1078>
<t1079>The large chest was in the same place, close to the wall, but its lid, though not reinforced, was placed on top; the nails were also ready in their places to be hammered into their slots.</t1079><t1080>I knew I had to search its surface to find the key, so I lifted the lid and leaned it against the wall; <t1097>I kept thinking about what my next move should be, but my mind was like a burning field, and I waited with a growing sense of hopelessness inside me.</t1097> <t1098>While waiting, I heard a Gypsy song sung by cheerful voices coming closer and closer, and amidst the songs, the turning of heavy wheels and the cracking of whips; the Gypsies and Slovaks the Count had mentioned were coming.</t1098> <t1099>After taking one last look around and at the coffin hiding the disgusting body, I decided to dash out as soon as the door opened and escaped to the Count's room.</t1099> <t1100>I listened to the sounds with great care and heard the key turning and the heavy door being pulled back downstairs.</t1100> <t1101>There must have been other entrances, or one of the locked doors had a key.</t1101> <t1102>Then, footsteps making noise and echoing in the corridor were heard, moving away.</t1102> <t1103>I turned to run to the crypt where I could find the new entrance; but at that moment, a violent and sudden wind blew, slamming the door opening to the spiral staircase and scattering the dust on the upper lintel.</t1103> <t1104>When I ran to open the door, I found it desperately jammed.</t1104> <t1105>I was a prisoner again, and fate was weaving its webs around me more tightly.</t1105>
<t1106>As I write these, there are numerous footsteps and the noise of weights being placed heavily on the floor in the corridor below; those being placed are undoubtedly crates filled with soil.</t1106> <t1107>The sound of hammering is heard; this is the crate being nailed shut.</t1107> <t1108>Now, I can hear the sound of heavy footsteps, followed by many other footsteps, echoing along the corridor.</t1108>

<t1110>Listen! <t1116>And then home! To the fastest and nearest train!</t1116> <t1117>Away from this cursed place, this cursed land where the devil and his children still walk with earthly feet!</t1117>

<t1304>May 25.</t1304> <t1305>- Today, there is a decrease in appetite.</t1305> <t1306>Can't eat, can't sleep, so instead of these, a journal.</t1306> <t1307>Since my rejection yesterday, there is a kind of emptiness inside me; nothing in the world seems worth doing.</t1307> <t1308>Knowing that the only cure for this kind of thing is work, I went down to the patients.</t1308> <t1309>I chose someone who is a very interesting subject of study for me.</t1309> <t1310>He has such strange thoughts and is so different from normal mental patients that I decided to understand him as well as I could.</t1310> <t1311>Today, it felt like I got closer to the essence of his mystery than ever before.</t1311>
<t1312>In order to learn the truths about his delusions, I interrogated him in a much more comprehensive manner than I had done before.</t1312> <t1313>Now I see that there was a bit of ruthlessness in the way I did it.</t1313> <t1314>It was as if I wanted to keep him at the peak of his madness - which is something I avoid as much as the mouth of hell in patients.</t1314> <t1315>(Note: Under what conditions would I not avoid the pit of hell?) <t1353>July 24.</t1353> <t1354>Whitby.</t1354> <t1355>- Lucy, looking sweeter and more beautiful than ever, met me at the station and we went by carriage to the house with vacant rooms in Crescent.</t1355> <t1356>This is a very beautiful place.</t1356> <t1357>A small river called Esk flows through a deep valley that widens as it approaches the harbor.</t1357> <t1358>A large bridge on high piers crosses to the other side, and the view between the piers makes it seem farther away than it actually is.</t1358> <t1359>The valley is lush and so steep that, unless you are close enough to look down, you only see the opposite side.</t1359> <t1360>In the old town - the side far from us - all the houses have red roofs and seem to be stacked on top of each other, similar to the pictures we saw in Nuremberg.</t1360> <t1361>Right above the town are the ruins of Whitby Abbey, which was plundered by the Danes and where the part of "Marmion" where the girl is walled up takes place.</t1361> <t1362>An extremely noble, very large, beautiful, and romantic ruin; there is a legend that a white lady has been seen in one of the windows.</t1362> <t1363>There is another church between the town and the abbey; a parish church with a large graveyard full of tombstones around it.</t1363> <t1364>To me, this is the most beautiful spot in Whitby, because it is right above the town and overlooks the entire bay, from the harbor to the headland called Kettleness that stretches out to the sea.</t1364> <t1365>It descends so steeply to the harbor that part of the ground has slipped down, damaging some of the graves.</t1365> <t1366>In one place, the tombstones extend down to the sandy road below.</t1366> <t1367>Along the churchyard, there are walking paths with seats beside them; people go there and sit all day, enjoying the beautiful view and the breeze.</t1367> <t1368>I will often sit and work here too.</t1368> <t1369>In fact, I am writing now with my notebook on my knee, listening to the conversation of three old men sitting next to me.</t1369> <t1370>They seem to do nothing all day but sit here and talk.</t1370>
<t1371>The harbor stretches below, and at the end of the harbor, there is a long granite wall extending into the sea; in the middle of the outward-curving tip, there is a lighthouse.</t1371> <t1372>Outside, a heavy breakwater stretches out.</t1372> <t1373>On the side closer to me, the breakwater makes a reversed elbow, and at its tip, there is also a lighthouse.</t1373> <t1374>Between the two piers, there is a narrow opening leading to the harbor that suddenly widens.</t1374>
<t1375>It's beautiful during the rising tide; but when the waters recede, it looks like nothing and only the Esk remains, flowing here and there between the rocks and the sandy shore.</t1375> <t1376>Outside the harbor, on this side, a wide rocky ridge extends for about eight hundred meters; its steep edge starts right behind the southern lighthouse.</t1376> <t1377>At the end, there is a buoy with a bell that sways in bad weather and sends a mournful sound to the wind.</t1377> <t1378>According to a legend here, whenever a ship is lost at sea, bells are heard.</t1378> <t1379>I should ask the old man about this; he is coming this way.</t1379>
<t1380>A strange old man.</t1380> <t1381>He must be extremely old because his face is entirely gnarled and wrinkled like tree bark.</t1381> <t1382>He tells me that he is almost a hundred years old and that he was a sailor in the Greenland whaling fleet during the Battle of Waterloo.</t1382> <t1383>I'm afraid he's quite skeptical, because when I asked him about the bells at sea and the White Lady of the Monastery, he began to speak with an accent and in a gruff manner:</t1383>
<t1384>“If I were you, I wouldn't bother with these things, young lady.</t1384> <t1385>All of this is outdated.</t1385> <t1386>Look, I'm not saying they never existed, but they didn't exist in my time.</t1386> <t1387>These tales might be good for tourists and such, but not for a lovely young lady like you.</t1387> <t1388>People who come from York and Leeds, constantly eating smoked herring and drinking tea, looking to buy cheap black amber, they believe in this.</t1388> <t1389>I wonder who would go to the trouble of lying to these people - and even to newspapers filled with nonsense.”</t1389> <t1390>I thought this old man might be someone from whom I could learn interesting things, so I asked if he would mind telling me something about whaling in the old days.</t1390> <t1391>He was just about to start when the clock struck six, upon which he struggled to stand up and said:</t1391>
<t1392>"I must get moving to go home now, young lady.</t1392> <t1393>My grandson doesn't like to be kept waiting when the tea is ready because it takes me a while to get down the stairs - there are so many of them; and young lady, when the time comes, I get very hungry.</t1393><t1394>"</t1394>
<t1395>He limped away, down the stairs, and I could see him descending as quickly as he could.</t1395> <t1396>The stairs are one of the important features of this place.</t1396> <t1397>They go from the town to the church; there are hundreds of steps - I don't know how many - and they turn with a gentle curve; the incline is so slight that a horse can easily go up and down.</t1397> <t1398>I think they originally had some connection with the Monastery.</t1398> <t1399>I should go home too.</t1399> <t1400>Lucy had gone to pay visits with her mother, and since these visits were out of duty, I did not go.</t1400> <t1401>They must have returned home by now.</t1401>
<t1402>July 25.</t1402> <t1403>- I came here with Lucy an hour ago; we had a very interesting conversation with my old friend and the other two who always come here and join him.</t1403> <t1404>Clearly, the group's Mr. Prophecy17 is my old friend; I think he was quite a domineering person in his time.</t1404> <t1405>He wouldn't accept anything and would snap at everyone.</t1405> <t1406>If he couldn't prevail in a debate, he would bully, and then he would see the silence of his opponents as a sign of agreement with his thoughts.</t1406> <t1407>Lucy looked very elegant and beautiful in her white, thin linen dress; she has gotten a nice color since she came here.</t1407> <t1408>As soon as we sat down, I noticed that the old men didn't waste any time getting up to sit close to her.</t1408> <t1409>Lucy is so sweet to old people; I think they immediately fell in love with her.</t1409> <t1410>Even my old man couldn't resist and didn't clash with her, but instead doubled my share.</t1410> <t1411>I caught him on the subject of legends and he immediately started a speech-like talk.</t1411> <t1412>I should try to remember what he said and put it down on paper:</t1412>
<t1413>“It's all nonsense, from top to bottom; that's it, nothing else.</t1413> <t1414>All these curses, ghosts, bogeymen, and everything related to them are things suitable for children and foolish women to believe in.</t1414> <t1415>Nothing but soap bubbles!</t1415> <t1416>All these horrors, signs, and warnings are concocted by priests, malicious educated people, and railway barkers to scare half-wits and to make people do things they wouldn't otherwise be inclined to do.</t1416> <t1417>Thinking about them makes me angry.</t1417> <t1418>The lies they print in newspapers, the lies they preach from the pulpit aren't enough; they also want to carve them onto gravestones.</t1418> <t1419>Look around you, all the stones seem to be proudly lifting their heads, but in reality, they are toppling under the weight of the lies written on them; on all of them, it says, ‘Here lies the body of so-and-so’ or, ‘In sacred memory of so-and-so,’ but half of them don't contain any bodies; and they are neither sacred, nor does anyone care about their memory.</t1419> <t1420>It's all lies, all lies in one way or another!</t1420> <t1421>My God, on Judgment Day, what a mess it will be when they try to drag their gravestones, struggling to hold onto them with their slippery hands from being in the sea for so long, to prove how good they were.</t1421><t1422>”</t1422>
