<t2301>I am pleased that I made this decision, and even more pleased that I adhered to it.</t2301> <t2302>I lay tossing and turning; when the guard sent from the ward came to tell me that Renfield had escaped, I had only heard the clock strike twice.</t2302> <t2303>I quickly put on my clothes and ran downstairs; my patient is a man too dangerous to be wandering around.</t2303> <t2304>His thoughts can lead to dangerous outcomes for others.</t2304> <t2305>When I arrived, the nurse was waiting for me.</t2305> <t2306>He said it had not even been ten minutes since he looked through the observation hole in the door and saw him seemingly asleep in his bed.</t2306> <t2307>The sound of the window being opened outward caught his attention.</t2307> <t2308>He turned back and ran to the door, and upon seeing the patient's foot disappear out the window, he immediately called for me.</t2308> <t2309>The patient is only in his nightclothes and cannot have gone far.</t2309> <t2310>The nurse thought it would be more useful to watch where he was going rather than chase after him and risk losing his trail as he exited the building through the door.</t2310> <t2311>The nurse is a burly man and couldn't get out the window.</t2311> <t2312>I am slender, and with the nurse's help, I went out the window feet first and landed on the ground without injury, as we were only a few meters up.</t2312> <t2313>The nurse said the patient turned left and went straight ahead, so I ran as fast as I could.</t2313> <t2314>As I passed through the trees, I saw a white figure climbing the high wall that separates our grounds from the abandoned house's property.</t2314>

<t2342>IX</t2342>
<t2343>From Mina Harker</t2343>
<t2344>Letter to Lucy Westenra</t2344>
<t2345>Budapest, August 24</t2345>
<t2346>Dearest Lucy,</t2346>
<t2347>I know you'll be curious to learn everything that has happened since we parted at the train station in Whitby.</t2347><t2348>Well, my dear, I arrived safely in Hull, caught the ship to Hamburg, and from there, the train that brought me here.</t2348><t2349>I can't remember much about the journey except that I knew I needed to sleep as much as possible since I would need to take care of Jonathan when I arrived.</t2349><t2350>I found my beloved looking so weak, pale, and frail!</t2350><t2351>My dear, all the determination in his eyes, that quiet dignity I told you about on his face, had vanished.</t2351><t2352>He has become a shadow of himself and does not remember what happened to him during that long period.</t2352><t2353>At least, he wants me to believe that, and I will never ask.</t2353><t2354>He has suffered a terrible shock, and I fear that trying to remember it might strain his poor brain too much.</t2354><t2355>Sister Agatha, who is a very good soul and a natural nurse, says that he raved about horrible things when he was acting mad.</t2355><t2356>I asked her to tell me what they were, but she just crossed herself and said she would never tell; because a patient's ravings are considered God's secrets, and if a nun hears them as part of her duty, she must respect the trust placed in her.</t2356><t2357>She is sweet and kind; the next day, when she saw I was distressed, she brought up the subject again and said she could never speak of what my beloved raved about, but added: "I can tell you this much, dear: What he raved about was not something bad he had done, and there is no reason for you to worry as his future wife.</t2357><t2358>He has not forgotten you or what he owes you.</t2358><t2359>His fear is related to things so great and terrifying that no mortal could speak of them."</t2359><t2360>I think this sweet person thought I might be jealous if my poor beloved had fallen in love with another girl.</t2360><t2361>Imagine thinking I could be jealous of Jonathan!</t2361><t2362>But still, my dear, let me whisper that I felt a joyful relief when I learned that another woman was not the cause of his distress.</t2362><t2363>Now, I am sitting by his bed, where I can see his face while he sleeps.</t2363><t2364>He is waking up!..</t2364><t2365>When he woke up, he wanted his coat to get something from his pocket; <t2378>The nun came back and said that the English missionary church pastor had been called.</t2378> <t2379>We will get married within an hour or as soon as Jonathan wakes up...</t2379>
<t2380>Lucy, the moment came and went.</t2380> <t2381>I feel very honored and very, very happy.</t2381> <t2382>Jonathan woke up about an hour after our last conversation; everything was ready, and Jonathan was sitting up in bed, propped up by pillows.</t2382> <t2383>"I accept," he said clearly and strongly.</t2383> <t2384>I could barely speak; my heart was so full that even those words seemed to choke me.</t2384> <t2385>The dear nuns were very considerate.</t2385> <t2386>Please, God, never ever let me forget them or the heavy and sweet responsibilities I have taken on.</t2386> <t2387>I must tell you about my wedding gift.</t2387> <t2388>When the priest and the nuns left my husband and me -Oh, Lucy, this is the first time I write the word "husband"- when they left my husband and me alone, I took the notebook out from under his pillow, wrapped it in white paper, tied it with a light blue ribbon that I wore around my neck, sealed it with wax, and used my wedding ring as the seal.</t2388> <t2389>Then I kissed the package and showed it to my husband, telling him that I would keep the notebook this way, so it would be a visible and clear sign that we trust each other throughout our lives, and that I would never open it unless it was for his own good or an unrelenting duty.</t2389> <t2390>Then he took my hand, and oh, Lucy, it was the first time he held his wife's hand, and he said it was the most beautiful thing in the world and that he would relive the entire past to earn it, if necessary.</t2390> <t2391>My poor darling meant a part of the past, but he can't think about time yet, and I wouldn't be surprised if he mixes up not only months but also years.</t2391>
<t2392>Yes, my love, what could I have said?</t2392> <t2393>I told him only that I was the happiest woman in the world and that I had nothing to give but myself, my life, and my trust, and that these would be accompanied by the love and respect I would feel for him every day of my life.</t2393> <t2394>And my love, when he kissed me and pulled me towards him with his poor, weak hands, it felt as if there was a sacred vow between us.</t2394>

<t2430>August 20.</t2430> <t2431>- The Renfield case is becoming more and more interesting.</t2431> <t2432>He has now become so quiet that there are moments of calm between his bouts of madness.</t2432> <t2433>During the first week after his seizure, he constantly exhibited violent tendencies.</t2433> <t2434>Then one night, just as the moon was rising, he calmed down and began to mutter to himself: "I can wait now; I can wait now."</t2434> <t2435>The nurse came to tell me this, and I immediately rushed downstairs to check on Renfield.</t2435> <t2436>He was still in the padded room with his straitjacket on, but the expression we had seen on his face for so long was gone, and the old pleading - almost "fawning" - soft look had returned to his eyes.</t2436> <t2437>I was pleased with his current state and ordered the straitjacket to be removed.</t2437> <t2438>The nurses hesitated, but eventually complied with my wishes without objection.</t2438> <t2439>It was strange that the patient had enough sense of humor to notice their distrust; because he came up to me and, looking at them slyly, whispered:</t2439>

<t2533>Arthur Holmwood's letter</t2533>
<t2534>2</t2534> <t2535>September</t2535>
<t2536>Dear old friend,</t2536>
<t2537>I can quickly tell you about Miss Westenra's health that, in my opinion, there is no functional disorder or any disease that I know of.</t2537> <t2538>However, I was not at all pleased with her appearance; she looks distressingly changed compared to the last time I saw her.</t2538> <t2539>Of course, you must take into account that I did not have the opportunity for a thorough examination as I would have liked; our friendship creates a difficulty that neither medical science nor traditions can overcome.</t2539> <t2540>The best thing is for me to tell you exactly what happened so that you can come to your own conclusions to some extent.</t2540> <t2541>Then I will tell you what I did and what I suggest should be done.</t2541>
<t2542>I found Miss Westenra seemingly cheerful.</t2542> <t2543>Her mother was there, and after a few seconds, I concluded that she was doing everything to deceive her mother and prevent her from worrying.</t2543> <t2544>Although she wasn't sure what it was, I have no doubt that she sensed precautions needed to be taken.</t2544> <t2545>We had lunch alone, and while we all strove to cheer up, our efforts were somewhat rewarded, and a bit of genuine joy emerged among us.</t2545> <t2546>Then Miss Westenra went to lie down, and Lucy stayed with me.</t2546> <t2547>We went to Lucy's room; her cheerfulness lasted until we entered the room because the servants were coming and going.</t2547> <t2548>But as soon as the door closed, the mask on her face fell, and with a deep sigh, she collapsed into a chair and covered her eyes with her hands.</t2548> <t2549>Seeing her mood change, I immediately took the opportunity to diagnose her reaction.</t2549> <t2550>With great kindness, she said:</t2550>

<t2556>I could easily see that she was somewhat anemic, but there were no usual signs of anemia; by chance, I was able to measure the quality of her blood because a wire snapped while opening a stuck window and she slightly cut her hand with the broken glass.</t2556><t2557>In itself, it was a trivial thing, but it gave me a clear opportunity, and I took a few drops of blood and examined them.</t2557><t2558>The qualitative examination yielded quite normal results, and according to this conclusion, her health seems quite good.</t2558><t2559>I was convinced that there was no need to worry about other physical matters; <t2650>Dr. Seward's journal</t2650>
<t2651>September 4th.</t2651> <t2652>- The zoophagous patient still holds our interest.</t2652> <t2653>He only had one outburst, and that was at an unusual hour yesterday.</t2653> <t2654>He started getting restless just before noon.</t2654> <t2655>The nurse recognized the symptoms and immediately called for help.</t2655> <t2656>Fortunately, the men came running and arrived just in time, because as the clock struck noon, the patient became so aggressive that they had to use all their strength to restrain him.</t2656> <t2657>But within about five minutes, he quieted down and eventually sank into a sort of melancholy that is still ongoing.</t2657> <t2658>The nurse says the screams he let out during the seizure were truly horrifying; when I went in, I found I had a lot of work to do, attending to some of the other patients he had frightened.</t2658>

<t2662>Later.</t2662> <t2663>- There has been a new change in my patient.</t2663> <t2664>I went to see him at five o'clock and found him happy and content as before.</t2664> <t2665>He was catching flies and eating them, and he was keeping a record of his captures by making notches with his fingernail on the protrusions of the door frame.</t2665> <t2666>When he saw me, he came up to me and apologized for his bad behavior, and with great respect and obsequiousness, he asked to be taken back to his room and to be allowed to have his notebook back.</t2666> <t2667>I thought it would be good to humor him; so, he returned to his room and his window is open.</t2667> <t2668>He spread the sugar from his tea on the window sill and is having a good harvest of flies.</t2668> <t2669>He is no longer eating them, but is putting them in a box as before, and has already started looking in the corners of his room for spiders.</t2669> <t2670>I tried to get him to talk about the last few days, because any clue about his thoughts would be of great help to me; but he did not join me in this conversation.</t2670> <t2671>For a second or two, he looked very sad and, in a tone as if he were talking to himself rather than to me, he said:</t2671>

<t2684>Midnight.</t2684> <t2685>- Another change in the patient.</t2685> <t2686>I had just returned to the hospital after visiting Miss Westenra, whom I found much better, and was standing at our door looking at the sunset when I heard Renfield shouting once again.</t2686> <t2687>Since his room is on this side of the building, I could hear him better than in the morning.</t2687> <t2688>Turning from the perfect, misty sunset over London, with its red lights, dark shadows, and all those extraordinary hues coming over the ugly clouds and even uglier waters, to the cold, stony rigidity of my building, breathing in the richness of suffering and my lonely heart that would endure it all, shook me.</t2688> <t2689>As the sun set, I reached the patient and saw the red orb setting from his window.</t2689> <t2690>At the moment the sun set, the patient's madness gradually decreased, and as it completely set, the patient slid to the ground like a heavy lump from the hands holding him.</t2690> <t2691>But the mental healing power that mental patients possess is extraordinary, for within a few minutes, he stood up with great calmness and looked around.</t2691> <t2692>I signaled the attendants not to hold him, as I was curious to see what he would do.</t2692> <t2693>He went directly to the window and swept the sugar crumbs outside; then he took the fly box in his hand, emptied it outside, and threw the box away; then he closed the window, crossed to the other side of the room, and sat on his bed.</t2693> <t2694>All this surprised me, so I asked him, "Won't you keep flies anymore?"</t2694>

<t2717>Letter from Dr. Seward to the Honorable Arthur Holmwood</t2717>
<t2718>September 6</t2718>
<t2719>Dear Art,</t2719>
<t2720>My news today is not very good.</t2720> <t2721>This morning, Lucy's condition deteriorated a bit.</t2721> <t2722>But this situation had a good outcome: naturally, Ms. Westenra was worried about Lucy and consulted me about her in a professional context.</t2722> <t2723>Taking advantage of this opportunity, I told her that my old master, the great master Van Helsing, would be coming to stay with me and that we would take joint responsibility for Lucy; thus, we can come and go without unnecessarily alarming her because a sudden shock could mean her death, and in Lucy's weak condition, such a development could be disastrous for her.</t2723> <t2724>We are all surrounded by difficulties, my poor old friend; but with God's permission, we will overcome them.</t2724> <t2725>I will write if necessary, that is, if you don't hear from me, just understand that I am waiting for news.</t2725>
<t2726>With my love</t2726>
<t2727>JOHN SEWARD</t2727>

<t2729>September 7 - The first thing Van Helsing said to me when we met on Liverpool Street was this:</t2729>
<t2730>“Did you say anything to our young friend, that is, the lady's lover?</t2730><t2731>”</t2731>
<t2732>“No,” I said.</t2732> <t2733>“As I mentioned in my telegram, I waited until I saw you.</t2733> <t2734>I wrote him a letter saying that you would come because Miss Westenra is not very well and that I would inform him if necessary.</t2734><t2735>”</t2735>
<t2736>“True, my friend,” he said, “very true!</t2736> <t2737>It is better that he does not know yet; perhaps he should never know.</t2737> <t2738>I hope it will be so; but if necessary, he must learn everything.</t2738> <t2739>And my good friend John, let me warn you.</t2739> <t2740>You are dealing with madmen.</t2740> <t2741>Everyone is mad in one way or another; be as sensible when dealing with God's madmen - the rest of the world - as you are with your own madmen.</t2741> <t2742>You do not tell your madmen what you are doing to them or why you are doing it; you do not tell them what you are thinking.</t2742> <t2743>So, leave knowledge where it can rest comfortably, gather its kind around it, and propagate.</t2743> <t2744>You and I will keep what we know here and here for now.”</t2744> <t2745>He touched first my chest and forehead and then his own in the same manner.</t2745> <t2746>“I have thoughts that I am keeping to myself right now.</t2746> <t2747>I will explain to you later.</t2747><t2748>”</t2748>

<t2752>“My friend John, when corn is growing, even before it matures - while Mother Nature's milk is still inside and the sun has not yet begun to paint it golden, the farmer pulls the cob and takes it in his rough hands, blows off the green husk, and says to you: ‘Look! <t2926>Dr. Seward's journal (continued)</t2926>
<t2927>September 8 - I sat by Lucy's side all night.</t2927> <t2928>The effect of the narcotic wore off towards twilight and she woke up on her own; she seemed like a different person compared to before the procedure.</t2928> <t2929>Her spirits were even good and she was filled with a happy liveliness, but I could see the traces of the absolute exhaustion she had been subjected to.</t2929> <t2930>When I told Mrs. Westenra that Dr. Van Helsing had ordered me to watch over Lucy, she almost scoffed at the idea, pointing out her daughter's renewed strength and perfect morale.</t2930> <t2931>But I was determined and made preparations for my long night watch.</t2931> <t2932>When her maid prepared her for the night, I went in; meanwhile, I had had my dinner and sat by her bedside.</t2932> <t2933>She did not object and looked at me with gratitude when our eyes met.</t2933> <t2934>After a long time, she seemed to fall asleep, but she struggled to gather herself and shook off sleep.</t2934> <t2935>This situation repeated itself several times with increasing efforts and shorter intervals as time went on.</t2935> <t2936>It was clear that she did not want to sleep, so I immediately addressed the issue:</t2936>

<t2963>I watched him all night.</t2963> <t2964>He didn't move at all and kept sleeping a deep, peaceful, invigorating, and healing sleep.</t2964> <t2965>His lips were slightly parted and his chest rose and fell with the regularity of a pendulum.</t2965> <t2966>There was a smile on his face, and it was clear that he didn't have a single bad dream to disturb his peace of mind.</t2966>
<t2967>Early in the morning, the servant came and I handed Lucy over to her and returned home, because there were many things that worried me.</t2967> <t2968>I sent short telegrams to Van Helsing and Arthur, informing them of the flawless outcome of the procedure.</t2968> <t2969>It took me all day to finish my own tasks - which were many; by the time I managed to get information about my zoophagous patient, it was already dark.</t2969> <t2970>The report was good: He had been quite quiet throughout the past day and night.</t2970> <t2971>While I was having dinner, a telegram arrived from Van Helsing, who was in Amsterdam at the time, saying that it would be good for me to be at Hillingham tonight and that he would join me early in the morning after traveling by the night mail coach.</t2971>
<t2972>September 9.</t2972> <t2973>- When I arrived at Hillingham, I was quite tired and exhausted.</t2973> <t2974>I had barely slept for two nights and my brain was beginning to feel the numbness indicative of fatigue.</t2974> <t2975>Lucy was awake and in good spirits.</t2975> <t2976>As she shook hands with me, she looked sharply at my face and said:</t2976>
<t2977>“Tonight, you won't be sitting up.</t2977> <t2978>You are exhausted.</t2978> <t2979>I'm as good as I used to be, really good; if someone needs to stay up all night, I'll be the one staying up with you.”</t2979> <t2980>I didn't argue about it, I went and had my dinner.</t2980> <t2981>Lucy came with me and I had a perfect meal cheered by her pleasant presence and drank a few glasses of Porto wine that was beyond perfect.</t2981> <t2982>Then Lucy took me upstairs and showed me the room next to hers, where a warm fireplace was burning.</t2982> <t2983>“Now,” she said, “you must stay here.</t2983> <t2984>I will leave this door and my own door open.</t2984> <t2985>You can lie on the couch, because I know that when there is a patient nearby, nothing can convince you doctors to lie in bed.</t2985> <t2986>If I need anything, I will call out and you can come to me immediately.”</t2986> <t2987>I couldn't do anything but accept because I was “dog-tired” and even if I tried to stay up all night, I wouldn't be able to manage it.</t2987> <t2988>So, after making her promise once more that she would call out if she needed anything, I lay down on the couch and forgot everything.</t2988>
<t2989>Lucy Westenra's diary</t2989>
<t2990>September 9.</t2990> <t2991>- Tonight I feel very happy.</t2991> <t2992>I had become so weak that being able to think and walk again feels like sensing the daylight after a long-lasting east wind in a steel-like sky.</t2992> <t2993>Somehow, I feel Arthur very, very close to me.</t2993> <t2994>I feel as if his warm presence is warming me inside.</t2994> <t2995>I think illness and weakness are selfish things; they turn our inner eye and love towards ourselves, whereas health and strength leave the reins to Love, allowing thoughts and feelings to go wherever they please.</t2995> <t2996>I wish Arthur knew this!</t2996> <t2997>My dear, my dear, your ears must be ringing while you sleep, mine ring while I'm awake.</t2997> <t2998>Oh, the delightful sleep of last night!</t2998> <t2999>How well I slept while that dear, good Dr. Seward watched over me.</t2999> <t3000>And tonight I should not be afraid to sleep because he is so close, within calling distance.</t3000> <t3001>Thank you so much to everyone for treating me so well!</t3001> <t3002>Thank God!</t3002> <t3003>Good night, Arthur.</t3003>
<t3004>Dr. Seward's journal</t3004>
<t3005>September 10 - I realized the Professor's hand was on top of my head and woke up instantly.</t3005> <t3006>This is one of the things we learned in the mental hospital, no matter the cost.</t3006>
<t3007>“So, how is our patient?</t3007><t3008>”</t3008>

<t3010>“Come on, let's see,” he said.</t3010> <t3011>And we entered the room together.</t3011>
<t3012>The curtain was drawn, and as Van Helsing quietly moved towards the bed like a cat, I also went to slowly open the curtain.</t3012>
<t3013>As I opened the curtain and the morning sun filled the room, I heard the Professor's sigh, and knowing how rare it was, a deadly fear pierced my heart.</t3013> <t3014>When I approached him, he recoiled, and there was no need for the anguished expression on his face to emphasize his exclamation of "Gott in Himmel!"27, a sign of his horror.</t3014> <t3015>He raised his hand and pointed to the bed; his stern face had fallen and turned ashen.</t3015> <t3016>I felt my knees begin to tremble.</t3016>

<t3093>September 11.</t3093> <t3094>- This afternoon I went to Hillingham.</t3094> <t3095>I found Van Helsing in an excellent mood and Lucy much better.</t3095> <t3096>Shortly after my arrival, a large package arrived for the Professor from abroad.</t3096> <t3097>He opened it, looking very impressed - supposedly, of course - and showed a huge bunch of white flowers.</t3097>

<t3131>We took the flowers with us and entered the room.</t3131> <t3132>The professor's actions were definitely strange, and what we were doing was not something you would find in any medical book I had ever heard of.</t3132> <t3133>First, he closed the windows and tightened the latches; then he took a handful of flowers and rubbed them along the window sashes as if wanting to ensure that any breeze coming in would be filled with the smell of garlic.</t3133> <t3134>Then, with that bunch, he rubbed the entire door frame, the bottom, the top, and both sides, and did the same around the fireplace.</t3134> <t3135>All of this seemed very meaningless to me, and I immediately said:</t3135>

<t3148>"Tonight I can sleep peacefully, and I need sleep - two nights of travel, plenty of reading on the day in between, followed by a day of much worry and a sleepless night.</t3148> <t3149>Come by early tomorrow morning and pick me up, and let's go see our lovely little lady who has become much stronger with the 'magic' I've been working on.</t3149> <t3150>Ho! <t3154>Lucy Westenra's diary</t3154>

<t3229>Lucy Westenra's diary</t3229>
<t3230>September 17.</t3230> <t3231>- Four days and four nights of peace.</t3231> <t3232>Again, I feel so strengthened that I hardly recognize myself.</t3232> <t3233>It’s as if I have just awakened from a long nightmare to see the clean morning air surrounding me with beautiful sunlight.</t3233> <t3234>I have vague, half-formed memories of long, anxious waits and fears, of darkness without even the slightest hope that would make the existing tension even more destructive, of long periods of oblivion, and of returning to life like a diver freed from the heavy pressure of water.</t3234> <t3235>But, with Dr. Van Helsing by my side, all these bad dreams seem like the past; all the sounds that scared me to the point of losing my mind - the flapping wings at the window, the voices that seemed close but were heard from afar, the harsh voices commanding me to do who knows what - seem like the past.</t3235> <t3236>I no longer go to bed afraid to sleep.</t3236> <t3237>I don’t even try to stay awake.</t3237> <t3238>I’ve started to quite like garlic, and every day a box full of it comes for me from Haarlem.</t3238> <t3239>Tonight, Dr. Van Helsing is leaving because he needs to be in Amsterdam for a day.</t3239> <t3240>But there’s no need for anyone to keep watch over me; I am well enough to be left alone.</t3240> <t3241>God bless my mother, dear Arthur, and all our friends who have been so kind!</t3241> <t3242>I don’t even feel alone, because last night Dr. Van Helsing slept in his chair for a long time.</t3242> <t3243>I found him asleep twice when I woke up; but despite the almost angry banging of tree branches, bats, or something else against the windows, I wasn’t afraid to fall asleep again.</t3243>

<t3376>Dr. Seward's journal</t3376>
<t3377>September 17 - After dinner, due to the pressure of other tasks and the numerous visits to Lucy, I unfortunately worked in my room to complete my remaining tasks.</t3377> <t3378>Suddenly, the door opened and my patient, whose face was contorted with anger, burst in.</t3378> <t3379>I was stunned, because it was almost unheard of for a patient to enter the Administrator's room of their own accord.</t3379> <t3380>Without hesitating for even a moment, he came directly at me.</t3380> <t3381>He had a dinner knife in his hand, and seeing that it was dangerous, I tried to keep the table between us.</t3381> <t3382>But he was far too fast and far too strong for me; thus, before I could regain my balance, he struck me with the knife and cut my left wrist quite seriously.</t3382> <t3383>However, before he could attack again, I lunged at him with my right hand and knocked him flat on his back.</t3383> <t3384>My wrist was bleeding heavily, forming a small pool on the carpet.</t3384> <t3385>Seeing that my friend had no intention of further struggle, I busied myself with bandaging my wrist without taking my eyes off the person lying on the ground.</t3385> <t3386>When the nurses rushed in and we turned our attention to him, what he was doing absolutely sickened me.</t3386> <t3387>Lying face down on the floor, like a dog, he was licking the blood that had dripped from my wounded wrist.</t3387> <t3388>He was easily caught and, to my surprise, went quite docilely with the nurses; as he left, he kept repeating these words: "The blood is the life!</t3388> <t3389>The blood is the life!</t3389><t3390>"</t3390>

<t3411>The note left by Lucy Westenra</t3411>
<t3412>September 17.</t3412> <t3413>Night.</t3413> <t3414>- I am writing this and leaving it to be seen so that no one gets into trouble because of me.</t3414> <t3415>This is a complete record of what happened tonight.</t3415> <t3416>I think I am dying of weakness and can barely find the strength to write, but I must write even if I die doing so.</t3416>
<t3417>As usual, I lay down paying attention to whether the flowers were placed in the spots indicated by Dr. Van Helsing, and soon fell asleep.</t3417>
<t3418>I woke up to the sound of wings outside the window, which I now know very well, starting from my sleepwalking episode on the slope in Whitby where Mina had saved me.</t3418> <t3419>I wasn't afraid, but I wished Dr. Seward—or as Dr. Van Helsing suggested—was in the next room so I could call out to him.</t3419> <t3420>I tried to sleep, but I couldn't.</t3420> <t3421>Then, as before, I became afraid to sleep and decided to stay awake.</t3421> <t3422>Ironically, whenever I don't want to sleep, sleep tries to come; so, fearing to be alone, I opened my door and called out, "Is anyone there?"</t3422> <t3423>No response came.</t3423> <t3424>I hesitated to wake my mother, so I closed my door again.</t3424> <t3425>Then, from the bushes outside, I heard a howl that resembled a dog's but was harsher and deeper.</t3425> <t3426>I went to the window and looked out but saw nothing except a large bat clearly hitting the window with its wings.</t3426> <t3427>So I returned to bed but decided not to sleep.</t3427> <t3428>A little later, the door opened, and my mother looked in; she realized I was awake from my movement and came in to sit beside me.</t3428> <t3429>In a voice even sweeter and softer than usual, she said, "I was worried about you, my dear, and came to see if you were alright.</t3429><t3430>"</t3430>

<t3474>XII</t3474>
<t3475>Dr. Seward's journal</t3475>
<t3476>September 18.</t3476> <t3477>- I immediately drove to Hillingham and arrived there early in the morning.</t3477> <t3478>Leaving my car at the garden gate, I walked alone down the tree-lined path to the house.</t3478> <t3479>I knocked on the door slowly and rang the bell as quietly as possible because I was afraid of disturbing Lucy or her mother and hoped to bring only one of the servants to the door.</t3479> <t3480>After a while, when I received no response, I knocked and rang the bell again; still no answer.</t3480> <t3481>At this hour - for it was ten o'clock - I cursed the laziness of the servants who might be in bed and thus knocked and rang the bell more impatiently once again, but still, there was no response.</t3481> <t3482>Until now, I had only blamed the servants, but now a great fear began to fill me.</t3482> <t3483>Was this abandonment a new link in the chain of bad news that was tightening around us?</t3483> <t3484>Was this house, to which I had indeed arrived too late, a house of death?</t3484> <t3485>I knew that being late by even a few minutes, or even seconds, could mean long hours of danger for Lucy if her condition had relapsed; I circled the house hoping to find any possible entrance by chance.</t3485>

<t3687>When she woke up late that afternoon, the first thing Lucy did was to feel her chest and, to my surprise, take out the paper that Van Helsing had given me to read from her chest.</t3687><t3688>The careful Professor had put it back where it came from so she wouldn't worry when she woke up.</t3688><t3689>Then, her eyes shifted to Van Helsing and me, and she felt relieved.</t3689><t3690>Then, she looked around the room and shuddered when she realized where she was; she screamed loudly and covered her pale face with her poor, thin hands.</t3690><t3691>We both understood what this meant - that she fully comprehended her mother's death; so we did our best to comfort her.</t3691><t3692>Undoubtedly, the empathy comforted her a bit, but she was very weak mentally and spiritually; she cried silently and feebly for a long time.</t3692><t3693>We told her that one or both of us would always stay with her; this seemed to comfort her a little.</t3693><t3694>She fell into a light sleep towards twilight.</t3694><t3695>During this time, a very strange thing happened.</t3695><t3696>In her sleep, she took the paper out of her chest and tore it up.</t3696><t3697>Van Helsing went to her and took the pieces of paper from her hand.</t3697><t3698>However, despite this, Lucy continued the tearing motion as if the paper was still in her hand; finally, she raised her hands and opened them as if scattering the pieces.</t3698><t3699>Van Helsing seemed surprised, and his eyebrows furrowed as if deep in thought, but he said nothing.</t3699>
<t3700>September 19.</t3700> <t3701>- Throughout last night, he slept fitfully, always fearing sleep and growing somehow weaker with each awakening.</t3701> <t3702>The Professor and I took turns watching over him, never leaving him alone for a moment.</t3702> <t3703>Quincey Morris said nothing about his plan, but I knew he patrolled around the house all night long.</t3703>
<t3704>When it was daytime, the sunlight revealed how badly his poor strength had been damaged.</t3704> <t3705>He could barely turn his head, and the small amount of food he could consume didn't seem to benefit him.</t3705> <t3706>He slept from time to time, and Van Helsing and I could see the difference between when he was asleep and awake.</t3706> <t3707>While he appeared weaker and his breathing was lighter when sleeping, he seemed stronger; his open mouth revealed his drawn, pale gums, making his teeth look definitely longer and sharper; when he woke up, the softness in his eyes clearly changed his expression, because even though he was dying, he looked like himself.</t3707> <t3708>In the afternoon, he asked for Arthur and sent him a telegram.</t3708> <t3709>Quincey went to the station to meet him.</t3709>
<t3710>When Arthur arrived, it was almost six o'clock; the sun was setting, red light was streaming in through the window, giving a bit more color to his pale cheeks.</t3710> <t3711>When he saw him, Arthur was almost choked with excitement, none of us could speak.</t3711> <t3712>In the hours that passed, healthy sleeps or what were considered coma-like states became more frequent, and thus the intervals where conversation was possible shortened.</t3712> <t3713>But Arthur's presence acted as a stimulant; Lucy had somewhat come to herself and was more lively while talking to him than she had been since we arrived here.</t3713> <t3714>Arthur had also pulled himself together, speaking as cheerfully as possible, so everything was going as well as it could.</t3714>
<t3715>It was almost one o'clock and Arthur and Van Helsing were sitting beside Lucy.</t3715> <t3716>In fifteen minutes, I will take over their watch, and I am making this record on Lucy's phonograph.</t3716> <t3717>They will try to rest until six o'clock.</t3717> <t3718>I fear tomorrow will end our watch, for this shock was too great; the poor child will not recover.</t3718> <t3719>God help us all.</t3719>
<t3720>Letter from Mina Harker to Lucy Westenra (Unopened by the recipient.</t3720><t3721>)</t3721>
<t3722>September 17</t3722>
<t3723>Dearest Lucy</t3723>
<t3724>It feels like a century has passed since I last heard from you or actually wrote to you.</t3724> <t3725>I know you will forgive me for my mistakes once you read all my news.</t3725> <t3726>Well, I safely received my husband; when we arrived in Exeter, a car was waiting for us, and despite suffering from gout, Mr. Hawkins was in the car.</t3726> <t3727>He took us to his home, where all the rooms allocated to us were very nice and comfortable, and we had dinner together.</t3727> <t3728>After dinner, Mr. Hawkins said:</t3728>
<t3729>“My dears, I want to drink to your health and happiness; I wish all the best for you.</t3729> <t3730>I have known both of you since your childhood and watched you grow with love and pride.</t3730> <t3731>Now I want you to build your home here beside me.</t3731> <t3732>I have neither wife nor child left; they are all gone and I have left everything to you in my will."</t3732> <t3733>As Jonathan and the old man shook hands, I cried, my dear Lucy.</t3733> <t3734>Our evening was very, very, very happy.</t3734>
<t3735>So here we are, settled in this beautiful old house, and from both my bedroom and the living room, I can see the nearby cathedral, with the great black bodies of the elm trees standing against the old yellow stones of the cathedral; I can hear the crows making noise all day, cawing and gossiping about the behaviors of crows and people.</t3735> <t3736>Needless to say, I am busy making arrangements concerning work and household management.</t3736> <t3737>Jonathan and Mr. Hawkins work all day long; because Jonathan is now a partner.</t3737> <t3738>Mr. Hawkins wants to tell him everything about the clients.</t3738>
<t3739>How is your dear mother doing?</t3739> <t3740>I wish I could come to town for a day or two to see you, dear, but with so much burden on my shoulders, I still don't have the courage; Jonathan still needs care as well.</t3740> <t3741>A bit of flesh has started to cover his bones, but he was terribly weakened by the long illness; even now, sometimes he suddenly jumps up in his sleep and wakes up trembling until I can soothe him back to his usual docility with sweet words.</t3741> <t3742>Still, thank God, these episodes are becoming less frequent as days go by, and I believe they will completely disappear in time.</t3742> <t3743>So, I've given you my news, let me ask about yours.</t3743> <t3744>When and where will you get married, who will conduct the wedding, and what will you wear, will it be an open wedding for the guests or will it be just among yourselves?</t3744> <t3745>Tell me everything, dear; tell me everything about it because there is nothing that concerns you that is not important to me.</t3745> <t3746>Jonathan asked me to convey his "deepest respects" to you, but I don't think that's enough for a greeting from the junior partner of Hawkins & Harker; so, since you love me, and he loves me, and I love you in all tenses and meanings of the word, I am sending you his "love" instead.</t3746> <t3747>Goodbye dear Lucy, and may all goodness be upon you.</t3747>
<t3748>With my love,</t3748>
<t3749>MINA HARKER</t3749>

<t3763>September 20</t3763>
<t3764>Dear Sir,</t3764>
<t3765>In line with your requests, I am sending the report regarding the items left under my responsibility as an attachment.</t3765> <t3766>There are more things to be said about the patient, Renfield.</t3766> <t3767>He had another fit that could have had a terrible ending, but fortunately, it did not.</t3767> <t3768>This afternoon, a transport cart with two men on it arrived at the empty house adjacent to our property - you remember, the house the patient escaped to twice.</t3768> <t3769>Since the men were strangers to the area, they stopped at our door to ask the porter for directions.</t3769> <t3770>I was looking out the window of my study while smoking my cigarette after dinner and saw one of the men approaching the house.</t3770> <t3771>As he passed in front of Renfield's room window, the patient began to scold him from inside and shouted all kinds of obscenities at him.</t3771> <t3772>The man, who seemed quite gentlemanly, simply replied, "Shut up, you foul-mouthed beggar," upon which our man accused him of robbing and killing him and said he would stop him even if he were to be hanged for it.</t3772> <t3773>I opened the window and signaled to the man not to mind, so he, after taking a look around and deciding what kind of place he had come to, simply said, "God bless you, sir, I don't care what is said to me in a damn madhouse.</t3773> <t3774>I pity you and the director for having to live in this house with such a wild animal," and then politely asked for directions; I told him where the door of the empty house was; he walked away with our man's threats, curses, and swearing trailing behind him.</t3774> <t3775>Wondering if I could understand why he got so angry, I went downstairs, because he is usually very well-mannered and nothing like this had ever happened outside of his wild fits.</t3775> <t3776>To my great surprise, I found him quite calm and moderate in his demeanor.</t3776> <t3777>I tried to get him to talk about the incident, but he kept sweetly asking what I meant and made me think he was completely unaware of the matter.</t3777> <t3778>Regrettably, I must report that this was just another display of his devilishness, because half an hour later, I received another report about him.</t3778> <t3779>This time, he had climbed out of his room window and was running down the tree-lined path.</t3779> <t3780>I told the attendants to follow me and ran after the patient because I was afraid he might harm someone.</t3780> <t3781>My fear was justified when I saw the cart that had passed by earlier moving down the road with several large wooden crates on it.</t3781> <t3782>The men were wiping their foreheads as if they had been exercising vigorously, and their faces were flushed.</t3782> <t3783>Before I could reach him, the patient lunged at the men, pulled one of them off the cart, and started banging his head on the ground.</t3783> <t3784>If I hadn't caught him in time, I think he would have killed the man right there.</t3784> <t3785>The other man jumped down and hit the patient on the head with the blunt end of his whip.</t3785> <t3786>It was a terrible blow, but he didn't seem to care and fought with all three of us, pulling us back and forth as if we were kittens.</t3786> <t3787>You know, I am not light, and the other two were hefty men as well.</t3787> <t3788>At first, he was silent while fighting; but when we started to subdue him and the attendants put a straitjacket on him, he began to shout: "I will stop them!</t3788> <t3789>They will not rob me!</t3789> <t3790>They will not slowly kill me!</t3790> <t3791>I will fight for my master!" He said this and other such nonsensical things.</t3791> <t3792>With considerable difficulty, they took him back to the house and put him in the padded room.</t3792> <t3793>One of the attendants, Hardy, had a broken finger.</t3793> <t3794>But I have sorted everything out, and he is now in good condition.</t3794>
<t3796>The two carriers initially shouted their threats regarding the legal measures to be taken for the damage caused, saying they would rain down all the punishments the law could give upon us.</t3796> <t3797>But their threats were intertwined with an indirect defense relating to both of them being defeated by a feeble madman.</t3797> <t3798>They said they could have dealt with the man quickly if their strength hadn't been spent carrying the heavy chests and lifting them onto the cart.</t3798> <t3799>As another reason for their defeat, they cited the unusual thirst they had fallen into due to the dusty nature of their profession and the deplorable distance of their work from any place of amusement.</t3799> <t3800>I understood their purpose very well; after one or more glasses of rum and a gold coin placed in each of their hands, they began to disregard the attack and swore they would encounter a worse madman to have the pleasure of meeting such a "damn good fellow" who writes these lines to you.</t3800> <t3801>I took their names and addresses in case it might be necessary in the future.</t3801> <t3802>The information is as follows: Jack Smollet from Dudding Houses, King George Road, Great Walworth, and Thomas Snelling from Peter Parley Houses, Guide Square, Bethnal Green.</t3802> <t3803>Both work at Harris & Sons Transport and Haulage Company located at Orange Master's Yard, Soho.</t3803>
<t3804>I will write to you about every topic that occurs here and might attract interest, and if something important happens, I will send a telegram as soon as possible.</t3804>
<t3805>Believe me, Sir.</t3805>
<t3806>Yours sincerely,</t3806>
<t3807>PATRICK HENNESSEY</t3807>

<t3810>September 18</t3810>
<t3811>Dearest Lucy</t3811>
<t3812>We experienced such a great disaster! Mr. Hawkins died suddenly.</t3812> <t3813>Some might think that this is not very sad for us, but we both loved him so much that it truly feels like we have lost our father.</t3813> <t3814>Since I never knew my mother or father, the death of this dear old man was a great shock to me.</t3814> <t3815>Jonathan is quite distressed.</t3815> <t3816>Not only does he feel great sorrow for this good man who had been his companion throughout his life and finally treated him like his own son, leaving him a fortune beyond our humble means, but Jonathan is also troubled by something else.</t3816> <t3817>He says that the amount of responsibility placed upon him with this situation makes him uneasy.</t3817> <t3818>He is starting to doubt himself.</t3818> <t3819>I try to cheer him up, and my faith in him helps him believe in himself.</t3819> <t3820>But this heavy shock he has experienced affects him the most in this matter.</t3820> <t3821>Oh, it is so hard that such a sweet, simple, noble, strong nature - a nature that, with the help of our dear, good friend, elevated him from a legal consultant to mastery within a few years - has been wounded in a way that destroys the essence of its strength.</t3821> <t3822>If I am troubling you with my worries in the midst of your own happiness, forgive me, dear; but dear Lucy, I must tell someone because trying to appear brave and cheerful in front of Jonathan is exhausting me, and there is no one here with whom I can share my secret.</t3822> <t3823>We have to go to London tomorrow, but I am hesitant about it; Mr. Hawkins stated in his will that he wanted to be buried in the same grave as his father.</t3823> <t3824>Since he has no other relatives, Jonathan has to take on the role of the funeral owner.</t3824> <t3825>Even if just for a minute or two, I will come to see you, dear.</t3825> <t3826>Forgive me for troubling you.</t3826> <t3827>With all my best wishes.</t3827>
<t3828>The one who loves you</t3828>
<t3829>MINA HARKER</t3829>
<t3830>Dr. Seward's journal</t3830>
<t3831>September 20 - Only determination and habit can allow me to make a note here tonight.</t3831> <t3832>I am in such a pitiable state, so sad, so tired of the world and everything in it, including life itself, that if I were to hear the flutter of the angel of death's wings right now, I wouldn't care.</t3832> <t3833>And recently, those merciless wings have been flapping for a certain purpose - Lucy's mother, Arthur's father, and now...</t3833> <t3834>Let me get back to my work.</t3834>
<t3835>I took over the duty of keeping watch over Lucy from Van Helsing just in time.</t3835><t3836>We also wanted Arthur to go and rest, but he initially refused.</t3836><t3837>However, when I told him that we would need his help during the day and that we shouldn't be exhausted from lack of rest if Lucy's condition worsened, he agreed to go.</t3837><t3838>Van Helsing was very kind to him.</t3838><t3839>"Come, my child," he said; "come with me.</t3839><t3840>You are sick and weak, and in addition to the burden we know of, you have also experienced great sorrow and mental anguish.</t3840><t3841>You should not be alone; for to be alone is to be filled with fear and dread.</t3841><t3842>Come to the sitting room where there is a large fire burning and two couches.</t3842><t3843>You lie on one, I on the other, and even if we do not talk or even sleep, our companionship will comfort each other." Arthur, looking longingly at Lucy's face, which was almost whiter than the linen on her pillow, left the room with the Professor.</t3843><t3844>Lucy was lying quite still, and I looked around the room to see that everything was as it should be.</t3844><t3845>I could see that the Professor maintained his determination to use garlic in this room as well as in the other; all the window frames smelled of garlic, and around Lucy's neck, over the silk handkerchief that Van Helsing wanted her to wear, there was a rough garland made of the same scented flowers.</t3845><t3846>Lucy's breathing was a bit raspy, and her face was in a terrible state because her pale gums were exposed through her open mouth.</t3846><t3847>In the dim and uncertain light, her teeth seemed longer and sharper than they had in the morning.</t3847><t3848>Especially, by some trick of the light, her canine teeth appeared longer and sharper than the others.</t3848><t3849>I sat down beside her, and she immediately moved restlessly.</t3849><t3850>At that very moment, monotonous wing sounds were heard at the window.</t3850><t3851>I slowly went to the window and looked outside from the corner of the curtain.</t3851><t3852>There was a full moon, and I could see that the noise was being made by a large bat, which, though very dim, was undoubtedly attracted by the light and occasionally struck the window with its wings.</t3852><t3853>When I returned to my seat, I noticed that Lucy had slightly moved and had torn off the garlic flowers from her throat.</t3853><t3854>I placed them back as best as I could and sat down to watch her.</t3854>
<t3855>She woke up a little later and I gave her the meal prescribed by Van Helsing.</t3855> <t3856>She ate very little and was reluctant.</t3856> <t3857>There seemed to be no sign of the struggle for life and strength that had been indicative of her illness until now.</t3857> <t3858>It struck me as odd that as soon as she regained consciousness, she pressed the garlic flowers to her chest.</t3858> <t3859>It was certainly strange that whenever she fell into that state of sleep with labored breathing, she pushed the flowers away, but when she woke up, she clung to them tightly.</t3859> <t3860>There was no possibility of making a mistake in this matter, because she went through many periods of sleep and wakefulness over the long hours that followed, and she repeated these two actions many times.</t3860>
<t3861>At six o'clock, Van Helsing came to take over the watch from me.</t3861> <t3862>During this time, Arthur had fallen asleep, and the Professor, out of compassion, had allowed him to continue sleeping.</t3862> <t3863>When he saw Lucy's face, I could hear the hiss in his breathing, and he said harshly in a whisper: "Open the curtain; I want light!" Then he leaned in and examined her carefully, his face almost touching Lucy's.</t3863> <t3864>He removed the flowers and the silk handkerchief from her neck.</t3864> <t3865>As he did so, he flinched, and I heard him say, as if choking, "Mein Gott!"</t3865> <t3866>I also leaned in and felt a strange shiver when I saw what had startled Van Helsing.</t3866> <t3867>The wounds on Lucy's neck had completely disappeared.</t3867> <t3868>For a full five minutes, Van Helsing stood there, looking at Lucy with the sternest expression on his face.</t3868> <t3869>Then he turned to me and said calmly:</t3869>
<t3870>“He is dying.</t3870> <t3871>It won't take long now.</t3871> <t3872>Be careful; whether he dies while conscious or in his sleep will change many things.</t3872> <t3873>Wake that poor child up, let him come and see him one last time; he trusts us and we promised him.</t3873><t3874>”</t3874>
<t3875>I went to the dining room and woke Arthur up.</t3875> <t3876>For a moment he was dazed, but when he saw the daylight streaming through the edges of the shutters, he thought he was late and expressed his fear.</t3876> <t3877>I convinced him that Lucy was still asleep, but as gently as I could, I told him that both Van Helsing and I feared the end was near.</t3877> <t3878>He covered his face with his hands and fell to his knees at the foot of the couch; there he remained for perhaps a minute, praying with his head bowed and his shoulders shaking with sorrow.</t3878> <t3879>I took his hand and lifted him up.</t3879> <t3880>"Come," I said, "my dear old friend, gather all your courage; this will be the best and easiest for her.</t3880><t3881>"</t3881>
<t3882>When we came to Lucy's room, I could see that Van Helsing, with his usual prudence, had fixed everything and made it as pleasant as possible.</t3882> <t3883>He had even brushed Lucy's hair, so that it lay on her pillow in its usual sunny waves.</t3883> <t3884>When we entered the room, she opened her eyes and, upon seeing him, slowly whispered:</t3884>
<t3885>“Arthur! Ah, my love.</t3885> <t3886>I am so happy you came!” He was just about to lean in to kiss Lucy when Van Helsing pulled him back.</t3886> <t3887>“No,” he whispered, “not yet!</t3887> <t3888>Hold her hand; this will comfort her more.</t3888><t3889>”</t3889>
<t3890>Thus, Arthur held her hand and knelt beside her; Lucy looked more beautiful than ever with the soft lines that matched the angelic beauty of her eyes.</t3890> <t3891>Then her eyes slowly closed and she fell asleep.</t3891> <t3892>For a short while, her chest rose and fell gently, her breathing like that of a tired child.</t3892>
<t3893>And then, in a vague manner, the strange change I noticed at night occurred.</t3893> <t3894>His breathing began to take on a wheezing quality, his mouth opened, and his receded pale gums made his teeth appear longer and sharper than ever.</t3894> <t3895>As if waking from sleep, vaguely, unconsciously, he opened his eyes that suddenly became dull and rigid, and in a soft, sensual voice I had never heard from his lips before, he said:</t3895>
<t3896>“Arthur! Ah, my darling.</t3896> <t3897>I am so happy that you came!</t3897> <t3898>Kiss me!” Arthur eagerly leaned in to kiss her, but at that very moment, Van Helsing, who was startled by Lucy’s voice just like I was, pounced on Arthur and grabbed him by the neck with a strength I never thought he possessed, pulling him back - or rather, almost throwing him to the other side of the room.</t3898>
<t3899>"Not in a million years!" he said, "not for your living soul or his!" And he stood between them like a tiger.</t3899>
<t3900>Arthur was so stunned that for a moment he didn't know what to do or say; before any impulse of violence could take hold of him, he perceived the place and situation, and remained silent, waiting.</t3900>
<t3901>My eyes, just like Van Helsing's, were fixed on Lucy; like a shadow, we saw an angry spasm pass over her face; her sharp teeth clashed together.</t3901> <t3902>Then, her eyes closed and she took a deep breath.</t3902>
<t3903>Shortly after, with all her tenderness, she opened her eyes and reached out her own poor, pale, thin hand to take Van Helsing's large, brown hand; pulling it towards her and kissed it.</t3903> <t3904>“My true friend,” she said, with a voice so weak and a tenderness beyond words, “the true friend of me and Arthur!</t3904> <t3905>Oh, protect him and bring me peace!</t3905><t3906>”</t3906>
<t3907>Van Helsing said solemnly, "I promise!" while raising his hand like someone taking an oath, kneeling beside Lucy.</t3907> <t3908>Then he turned to Arthur and said to him, "Come, my son, take her hand in yours and kiss her on the forehead, just once.</t3908><t3909>"</t3909>
<t3910>Their eyes met instead of their lips, and thus they parted.</t3910>
<t3911>Lucy’s eyes closed; Van Helsing, who was watching them closely, took Arthur’s arm and moved him away.</t3911>
<t3912>And then, Lucy's breathing became raspy again and suddenly stopped.</t3912>
<t3913>“Everything is over,” said Van Helsing.</t3913> <t3914>“She is dead!</t3914><t3915>”</t3915>
<t3916>I grabbed Arthur by the arm and took him to the living room, where he sat down and, upon seeing it, almost broke my heart as he covered his face with his hands, sobbing uncontrollably.</t3916>
<t3917>I returned to the room; I found Van Helsing looking at poor Lucy, the Professor's face was more stern than ever.</t3917> <t3918>There had been some changes in Lucy's body.</t3918> <t3919>Death had given back some of her beauty, as her forehead and cheeks had regained some of their flowing lines; even her lips had lost their deathly pallor.</t3919> <t3920>It was as if the blood, no longer needed to keep her heart working, had gone there to make the cruelty of death as little harsh as possible.</t3920>
<t3921>We thought he was dying while sleeping,</t3921>
<t3922>And when he dies, he sleeps.</t3922> <t3923>33</t3923>
<t3924>I stood next to Van Helsing and said, "Ah, poor girl, finally at peace."</t3924> <t3925>"The end has come!"</t3925> <t3926>He turned to me and replied with grave seriousness, "No; alas, it is not so.</t3926> <t3927>This is only the beginning!" When I asked what he meant, he just shook his head and said:</t3927>
<t3928>“We can't do anything for now.</t3928> <t3929>Wait and see.</t3929><t3930>”</t3930>
<t3931>Thirteen</t3931>
<t3932>Dr. Seward's journal (continued)</t3932>
<t3933>The funeral was arranged for the day after tomorrow so that Lucy and her mother could be buried together.</t3933> <t3934>I dealt with all the horrible official paperwork, and the polite funeral director proved that his entire staff was either cursed or blessed with his own excessive courtesy.</t3934> <t3935>Even the woman who performed the final duties for the dead said to me in a secret and friendly professionalism as she left the mortuary:</t3935>

<t4160>Mina Harker's journal</t4160>
<t4161>September 22 - Exeter train.</t4161> <t4162>Jonathan is sleeping.</t4162> <t4163>So much has happened since the last time I wrote here, which feels like it was just yesterday, when I was in Whitby and the whole world was ahead of me, when Jonathan was far away and I had no news from him; now, I am married to Jonathan, Jonathan has become a legal advisor, a partner, wealthy, and the owner of his own business, Mr. Hawkins has died and been buried; Jonathan had another fit that could harm him.</t4163> <t4164>One day he might ask me something about it.</t4164> <t4165>I am writing everything down.</t4165> <t4166>My shorthand has gotten rusty - see what unexpected happiness does to us - but it would be good to revive my shorthand by practicing in one way or another...</t4166>

<t4217>Dr. Seward's journal</t4217>
<t4218>September 22 - Everything is over.</t4218> <t4219>Arthur returned to the Ring and took Quincey Morris with him.</t4219> <t4220>Quincey is such a good man!</t4220> <t4221>I truly believe that he suffered as much as we did because of Lucy's death; <t4241>‘Ah, you don't understand, my friend John.</t4241><t4242>Even if I laugh, don't think that I'm not sad.</t4242><t4243>Look, I cried even while choking with laughter.</t4243><t4244>Always remember that the laughter knocking on your door and asking, ‘May I come in?’ is not real laughter.</t4244><t4245>No! <t4291>And now we are all in a wretched state; for long days, loneliness will sit with its wings deep in thought above our roofs.</t4291> <t4292>Lucy lies in the grand house of the dead in the deserted churchyard, far from the crowded London, among the graves of her relatives; here the air is clean, the sun rises over Hampstead Hill, and wildflowers grow on their own.</t4292>

<t4295>SON</t4295>
<t4296>"Westminster" newspaper, September 25</t4296>
<t4297>THE HAMPSTEAD MYSTERY</t4297>
<t4298>The Hampstead area is currently experiencing exciting days due to a series of developments similar to the events known as the "Kensington Horror" or the "Stabbing Woman" or the "Woman in Black" in the headlines.</t4298> <t4299>In the last two or three days, there have been numerous incidents involving small children who have wandered away from home or gone to play on the Heath and not returned.</t4299> <t4300>In all these cases, the children were too young to properly express themselves, but the common point in their supposed explanations was that they were with a "beautiful" lady.</t4300> <t4301>They all disappeared late at night, and in two cases, the children were not found until the early hours of the next day.</t4301> <t4302>There was a widespread belief that the first of the missing children used the excuse that "the beautiful lady said she wanted to take a walk with him," and the others followed this example as an excuse.</t4302> <t4303>These days, it is very understandable since the favorite thing of the little ones is to distract each other with small games.</t4303> <t4304>One of the reporters writes that it is extremely funny to see the little children playing "beautiful lady."</t4304> <t4305>He adds that some of our cartoonists could take lessons from these children on the fine satire of the grotesque that emerges when reality is compared to representation.</t4305> <t4306>The fact that the "beautiful lady" is the favorite role in these alfresco games is in harmony with the general principles of human nature.</t4306> <t4307>Our reporter naively states that even Ellen Terry could not have the charming appeal of some of these dirty-faced little children who are acting - and even believe themselves to be - the "beautiful lady."</t4307>
<t4308>But maybe the problem has a serious side because some of the children -actually all of those who disappeared at night- have small tears and wounds on their throats.</t4308> <t4309>The wounds seem to have been made by rats or small dogs, and although they are not very significant on their own, whatever animal made them shows that it has its own unique system or method.</t4309> <t4310>The local police were ordered to pay close attention to children wandering around Hampstead Heath and its surroundings, especially very young ones, and to any stray dogs that might be roaming the area.</t4310>

<t4322>September 23.</t4322> <t4323>- We had a bad night, but Jonathan is better now.</t4323> <t4324>I'm glad he has a lot of work to do because it keeps his mind off the dreadful things; I'm happy that he's not overwhelmed by the responsibilities that come with his new position.</t4324> <t4325>I knew he would return to his old self, and now seeing my Jonathan climb to the peak of his promotion and adapt to the responsibilities on his shoulders in every way makes me so proud.</t4325> <t4326>He will be out all day, until late, because he said he couldn't have lunch at home.</t4326> <t4327>My housework is done, so I can take the journal he kept abroad and lock myself in my room to read it...</t4327>
<t4328>September 24.</t4328> <t4329>- Last night, I didn't have the heart to write; Jonathan's horrifying journal upset me so much!</t4329> <t4330>Poor dear!</t4330> <t4331>Whether what he wrote was real or entirely a figment of his imagination, who knows how much he suffered!</t4331> <t4332>I wonder if there is any truth in what was written.</t4332> <t4333>Did he first contract brain fever and then write all these horrifying things; <t4352>(Confidential)</t4352>
<t4353>Dear Madam,</t4353>
<t4354>Forgive me for writing to you about the sad news of Miss Lucy Westenra's death.</t4354><t4355>Due to the kindness of Lord Godalming, I have the authority to read the young lady's letters and documents, as I have deep concerns about some matters of vital importance.</t4355><t4356>Among these papers, I found some of your letters showing how close friends you were and how much you loved her.</t4356><t4357>Oh, Madam Mina, I beg you, for the sake of that love, help me.</t4357><t4358>I ask this for the good of others - to correct a great mistake and to eliminate great and terrible troubles - which may be greater than you can even imagine.</t4358><t4359>Is it possible for me to see you?</t4359><t4360>You can trust me.</t4360><t4361>I am a friend of Dr. John Seward and Lord Godalming (who was Miss Lucy's Arthur).</t4361><t4362>For now, I must keep this from everyone.</t4362><t4363>If you tell me when and where I should be, I will come to Exeter immediately to see you, if I may have the privilege of doing so.</t4363><t4364>I have read the letters you wrote to poor Lucy, and I know the pains you and your husband have suffered; therefore, I beg you, if possible, do not inform him about this matter to avoid causing him harm.</t4364><t4365>Once again, I beg your pardon, forgive me.</t4365>

<t4373>September 25 - As Dr. Van Helsing's visit approaches, I can't help but feel an overwhelming excitement because somehow, I hope this visit will shed light on Jonathan's distressing experience; since he took care of Lucy during her last illness, he can tell me everything about her.</t4373> <t4374>The reason for his visit is this; it is not about Jonathan, but about Lucy and her sleepwalking.</t4374> <t4375>Then, I can never learn the truth now!</t4375> <t4376>How foolish I am!</t4376> <t4377>That dreadful journal has captured my imagination and is slowly coloring everything in its own hue.</t4377> <t4378>Of course, this visit is about Lucy.</t4378> <t4379>Poor thing, she had reverted to her old habit and that dreadful night on the hill must have made her sick.</t4379> <t4380>She must have told Dr. Van Helsing about the sleepwalking adventure on the hill and that I knew about it; and now the Doctor wants me to tell him about it so he can understand the situation.</t4380> <t4381>I hope I did the right thing by not mentioning this to Mrs. Westenra; if any of my actions, or even inactions, have harmed poor dear Lucy, I will never forgive myself.</t4381> <t4382>I also hope Dr. Van Helsing will not blame me; I have been subjected to such distress and anxiety lately that I feel I can no longer bear any more.</t4382>
<t4383>I think crying from time to time does us a lot of good - it clears the air like rain.</t4383> <t4384>Perhaps what upset me was reading the journal yesterday and Jonathan not being by my side for the first time since the beginning of our marriage, for an entire day and night.</t4384> <t4385>I hope my dear husband takes care of himself and that nothing happens to upset him.</t4385> <t4386>It is now two o'clock, the doctor will be here soon.</t4386> <t4387>Unless he asks me something about it, I will not tell him anything about Jonathan's journal.</t4387> <t4388>I am very glad that I am typing my own journal, so that if he asks about Lucy, I can give him the journal; this will save us from many questions.</t4388>

<t4539>Letter from Van Helsing to Ms. Harker (handwritten)</t4539>

<t4553>letter from Ms. Harker to Van Helsing</t4553>

<t4567>Jonathan Harker's journal</t4567>
<t4568>September 26 - I thought I would never write in this journal again, but the time has come.</t4568> <t4569>When I came home last night, Mina had prepared dinner; after the meal, she told me about Van Helsing's visit and that she had given him copies of two journals, expressing her deep concern for me.</t4569> <t4570>She showed me a letter from the Doctor, stating that everything written in my journal was true.</t4570> <t4571>This made me feel like a completely new man.</t4571> <t4572>What was breaking me down was the doubt about the reality of all these events.</t4572> <t4573>I felt inadequate, in the dark, and insecure.</t4573> <t4574>But now that I know the truth, I am not afraid - not even of the Count!</t4574> <t4575>So, he had finally succeeded in his plan to come to London, and the person I saw was him.</t4575> <t4576>He had rejuvenated, but how?</t4576> <t4577>If he was as Mina described, Van Helsing would be the one to unmask the Count and track him down.</t4577> <t4578>Mina and I stayed up late discussing this matter from beginning to end.</t4578> <t4579>Mina is getting dressed, and in a minute or two, I will stop by the hotel to bring Van Helsing here...</t4579>

<t4633>Dr. Seward's journal</t4633>

<t4754>For a while, I was under the influence of pure anger; it felt as if the Doctor had struck Lucy's face while she was alive.</t4754> <t4755>I slammed the table hard and stood up, saying: "Dr. Van Helsing, are you mad?" He looked up at me, and somehow the kindness on his face immediately calmed me.</t4755> <t4756>"I wish I were!" he said.</t4756> <t4757>"Madness is much easier to bear than such a truth.</t4757> <t4758>Oh, my friend, why do you think I beat around the bush, why did it take me so long to tell you something so simple?</t4758> <t4759>Because I hated you and have hated you all my life?</t4759> <t4760>Because I wanted to make you suffer?</t4760> <t4761>Because I wanted to take revenge, albeit late, for the time you saved my life, rescuing me from a horrific death?</t4761> <t4762>Oh, no!</t4762><t4763>"</t4763>
<t4764>“Forgive me,” I said.</t4764> <t4765>He continued speaking: “My friend, because I wanted to be gentle while giving you this bad news, because I know you love that very sweet lady.</t4765> <t4766>But even now, I don't expect you to believe it.</t4766> <t4767>It is so difficult to immediately accept an abstract truth that we always doubt the possibility of such a thing when we have believed it to be ‘impossible’; accepting such a concrete truth, especially when it concerns Miss Lucy, is even harder.</t4767> <t4768>I will go to prove it tonight.</t4768> <t4769>Will you dare to come with me?</t4769><t4770>”</t4770>
<t4771>This surprised me.</t4771> <t4772>A person does not want to prove such a truth; Byron had excluded the class of jealousy from this.</t4772>
<t4773>And he is proving the fact he despises the most.</t4773> <t4774>42</t4774>
<t4775>Seeing my hesitation, he said:</t4775>
<t4776>“The logic is simple: This time, it's not the logic of a madman jumping from one tuft of grass to another in a foggy swamp.</t4776> <t4777>If it's not true, then proving it will be a relief; at worst, it won't cause any harm.</t4777> <t4778>If it's true! <t4792>My heart was sinking because I felt that there was a terrifying exam ahead of us.</t4792> <t4793>But there was nothing I could do, so I gathered all my courage and said that we needed to act quickly because the afternoon was approaching...</t4793>
<t4794>We found the child awake.</t4794> <t4795>He had slept and eaten a little; his condition was entirely improving.</t4795> <t4796>Dr. Vincent removed the bandage from his neck and showed us the punctures on his skin.</t4796> <t4797>There was no doubt about the similarity with those on Lucy's neck.</t4797> <t4798>They were smaller and the edges looked fresher; that was all.</t4798> <t4799>We asked Vincent what he attributed these to; he said it must be an animal bite, perhaps a rat bite; but for his part, he tended to think it was one of the bats that are found in large numbers in the northern heights of London.</t4799> <t4800>“Among so many harmless species,” he said, “it could be a wild type from the more harmful species of the South.</t4800> <t4801>A sailor might have brought it home and it managed to escape; or a young bat might have been freed from the zoo or mated with a vampire bat there and caused a breeding.</t4801> <t4802>Such things happen, you know.</t4802> <t4803>Just ten days ago, a wolf escaped from the zoo and I believe it was tracked in this direction.</t4803> <t4804>A week later, children in all the alleys around here were playing nothing but Little Red Riding Hood in Heath until the fear of this ‘beautiful lady’ emerged.</t4804> <t4805>Even this little child, when he woke up this morning, asked the nurse, ‘Can I go?’</t4805> <t4806>When the nurse asked him why he wanted to go, he said he wanted to play with the ‘beautiful lady’.</t4806><t4807>”</t4807>

<t4834>Van Helsing began to work with a certain system.</t4834> <t4835>He found Lucy's grave by holding the candle so that he could read the plaques on the graves, and holding the spermaceti in such a way that it dripped in white pieces and solidified the moment it touched the metal.</t4835> <t4836>He searched his bag once more and took out his screwdriver.</t4836>

<t4838>“I will open the coffin.</t4838> <t4839>You still need to be convinced.”</t4839> <t4840>He immediately started unscrewing the bolts and finally lifted the lid to reveal the lead lining underneath.</t4840> <t4841>The sight affected me almost unbearably.</t4841> <t4842>This situation seemed like an insult to the dead, as if stripping someone of their clothes while they slept; in fact, I held Van Helsing's hand to stop him.</t4842> <t4843>The only thing he said was, “You will see,” and rummaged through his bag again to take out a fine wire saw.</t4843> <t4844>With a swiftness that frightened me, he brought the screwdriver down on the lead and made a small hole, just large enough for the tip of the saw to enter.</t4844> <t4845>I had expected gas to escape from the week-old corpse.</t4845> <t4846>We doctors, who have to be aware of the risks of our work, are accustomed to such things, so I stepped back towards the door.</t4846> <t4847>But the Professor did not stop for a moment; he cut a slit about sixty centimeters long along one side of the lead coffin with the saw, then cut the opposite side of the coffin, and then one of the other sides.</t4847> <t4848>He tilted the lifted part towards the foot of the coffin, holding it, and signaled for me to look by holding the candle towards the opened part.</t4848>

<t4999>September 27</t4999>
<t5000>My friend John,</t5000>
<t5001>I am leaving this note in case something happens.</t5001><t5002>I am going alone to keep watch in that churchyard.</t5002><t5003>I am pleased that Miss Lucy, who is Undead, will not leave tonight and thus will be more eager tomorrow night.</t5003><t5004>Therefore, I will place some things she will not like - garlic and a cross - and thus seal the door of the tomb.</t5004><t5005>As an Undead, she is still young and will avoid these.</t5005><t5006>Moreover, these are only to prevent her from getting out; if she wants to get in, they may not work; for then the Undead are desperate and must encounter the least resistance, no matter what.</t5006><t5007>I will be nearby from sunset to after sunrise and will learn whatever there is to be learned.</t5007><t5008>I am not afraid for Miss Lucy or of her; but the other one who turned her into an Undead now has the power to seek her grave and take refuge.</t5008><t5009>From mr Jonathan's experiences and from how cunningly he played with us for Miss Lucy's life and made fools of us all that time, I know that the Undead are strong in many ways.</t5009><t5010>They always have the strength of twenty people; within Miss Lucy is the combined strength of us four who gave her our power.</t5010><t5011>He can also gather his wolves and who knows what else.</t5011><t5012>Therefore, if he comes there tonight, he will find me; but no one else - until it is too late.</t5012><t5013>But he may not try here.</t5013><t5014>There is no reason for him to come; there would be more to hunt in the churchyard where the Undead woman sleeps and an old man keeps watch than in this hunting ground.</t5014>
<t5015>That's why, just in case, I'm writing this letter.</t5015> <t5016>Take the papers next to it, Harker's journal and the other papers; read them and then find this great Undead, cut off his head and burn his heart or stake him so that the world may be rid of him.</t5016>
<t5017>If we don't meet again, goodbye.</t5017>

<t5019>Dr. Seward's journal</t5019>
<t5020>September 28 - How a good night's sleep does wonders for a person.</t5020> <t5021>Yesterday, I was almost willing to accept Van Helsing's monstrous thoughts; but now these thoughts stand before me, horrifically, as an insult to common sense.</t5021> <t5022>I have no doubt that he believes in all this.</t5022> <t5023>I wonder if he might have lost his mind in some way.</t5023> <t5024>Surely, there must be some logical explanations for all these mysterious things.</t5024> <t5025>Is it possible that the Professor himself has done this?</t5025> <t5026>He has such an extraordinary mind that if he has gone mad, he would perfectly carry out his purpose related to a fixed idea.</t5026> <t5027>I don't want to think about it, and indeed, seeing Van Helsing as mad would be almost as astonishing as the other situation; but in any case, I will observe Van Helsing carefully.</t5027> <t5028>Maybe, I can find something that will shed light on the mystery.</t5028>
<t5029>September 29, morning.</t5029> <t5030>- Last night, just before ten o'clock, Arthur and Quincey came to Van Helsing's room; he told us everything he wanted us to do, but while doing so, he was particularly addressing Arthur, as if all our wills were concentrated on him.</t5030> <t5031>He began his words by saying that he hoped all of us would come with him, "Because," he said, "there is a serious duty to be fulfilled there.</t5031> <t5032>Surely you were surprised by my letter, weren't you?”</t5032> <t5033>This question was directly addressed to Lord Godalming.</t5033>
