<t5143>Dr. Seward's journal (continued)</t5143>
<t5144>When we climbed over the low wall and entered the churchyard, it was only a quarter past twelve.</t5144> <t5145>Despite the moonlight occasionally shining through the cracks between the heavy clouds drifting across the night sky, it was dark.</t5145> <t5146>In some way, we all walked close to each other; Van Helsing was a bit ahead of us, showing us the way.</t5146> <t5147>As we approached the grave, I looked at Arthur carefully, because I feared that approaching a place filled with such sorrowful memories would upset him; but he was holding up well.</t5147> <t5148>I concluded that the mystery of the task at hand somehow prevented his grief.</t5148> <t5149>The professor unlocked the door and, seeing that we all had a natural hesitation for various reasons, resolved the issue by entering first himself.</t5149> <t5150>We others followed him and he closed the door behind us.</t5150> <t5151>Then he lit a dim light and pointed to the coffin.</t5151> <t5152>Arthur advanced hesitantly; Van Helsing said to me: "You were here with me yesterday.</t5152> <t5153>Was Miss Lucy's body in the coffin yesterday?</t5153><t5154>"</t5154>
<t5155>“Yes.” The Professor turned to the others, saying: “You hear, and yet there is someone who still does not believe me.”</t5155> <t5156>Then, he took his screwdriver and lifted the lid of the coffin.</t5156> <t5157>Arthur watched with a very pale face but silently; when the lid was lifted, he stepped forward.</t5157> <t5158>It was clear that he did not know the coffin was lead, or at least he had not thought about it.</t5158> <t5159>When he saw the crack in the lead, blood rushed to his face for a moment, but then it withdrew just as quickly; so much so that he remained pale and white as a sheet; he was still silent.</t5159> <t5160>Van Helsing threw back the lead flap and we all recoiled as we looked inside the coffin.</t5160>
<t5161>The coffin was empty!</t5161>
<t5162>For a few minutes, no one spoke.</t5162> <t5163>The silence was broken by Quincey Morris:</t5163>
<t5164>"Professor, I vouched for you.</t5164> <t5165>The only thing I want is what you have to say; normally, I wouldn't ask for such a thing - I wouldn't cast doubt on your honor; but this is a mystery beyond all honor and dishonor.</t5165> <t5166>Is this your work?</t5166><t5167>"</t5167>
<t5168>“I swear by everything I hold sacred that I neither carried it nor touched it.</t5168> <t5169>This is what happened: Two nights ago, my friend Seward and I came here - with good intentions, believe me.</t5169> <t5170>We opened that sealed coffin and found it empty, just as it is now.</t5170> <t5171>Then we waited and saw something white coming through the trees.</t5171> <t5172>The next day, we came again during the day and there it was lying.</t5172> <t5173>Isn't that right, my friend John?</t5173><t5174>”</t5174>
<t5175>“Yes.</t5175><t5176>”</t5176>
<t5177>“We arrived just in time that night.</t5177> <t5178>A small child had gone missing again, and thank God, we found him unharmed among the graves.</t5178> <t5179>Yesterday, I came here before sunset because the Undead move at sunset.</t5179> <t5180>I waited here all night until the sun rose, but I saw nothing.</t5180> <t5181>This was very reasonable because I had covered the edges of the door with garlic, which the Undead cannot stand, and other things they avoid.</t5181> <t5182>No one came out last night, so before sunset tonight, I removed my garlic and other things from there.</t5182> <t5183>And thus, we found this coffin empty.</t5183>
<t5184>But listen to me patiently.</t5184> <t5185>So far, very strange things have happened.</t5185> <t5186>Wait with me outside, unseen and unheard, much stranger things will happen.</t5186> <t5187>Therefore,” -here he closed the cover of his lamp- “now outside.”</t5187> <t5188>He opened the door, walked behind us, closed the door behind him, and we went out in single file.</t5188>
<t5189>Ah! After the grave, the night air felt fresh and pure.</t5189> <t5190>How sweet it was to see the passing clouds and the moonlight filtering through the swiftly moving clouds - like the joys and sorrows in human life; how sweet it was to breathe the clean air untouched by death and decay; how humanizing it was to see the red glow in the sky behind the hill and to hear that muffled hum, a sign of the great city's life.</t5190> <t5191>Everyone was very serious in their own way and was coping with what had happened.</t5191> <t5192>Arthur was silent, trying to grasp the purpose and spiritual meaning of this mystery.</t5192> <t5193>I was quite patient and seemed half-inclined to set aside doubt and accept the conclusions Van Helsing had reached.</t5193> <t5194>Quincey Morris was in a calm state of someone who accepts everything and accepts everything with a cool courage, along with the things he must risk.</t5194> <t5195>Since he couldn't smoke, he had cut himself a large piece of chewing tobacco and was chewing it.</t5195> <t5196>As for Van Helsing, he was busy with a special task.</t5196> <t5197>First, he took out a thin, biscuit-like thing carefully wrapped in a white napkin from his bag; then he took two handfuls of a white substance that looked like dough or paste.</t5197> <t5198>He crumbled the biscuit finely and mixed it with the substance in his hand.</t5198> <t5199>Then he took this and, after rolling it into thin strips, began to place them in the gaps between the door and the door frame of the grave.</t5199> <t5200>I was a bit surprised by this and, being close to him, asked what he was doing.</t5200> <t5201>Arthur and Quincey had also come close to us because they were curious too.</t5201> <t5202>The professor replied:</t5202>
<t5203>“I am closing the grave so that the Not Dead cannot enter.</t5203><t5204>”</t5204>
<t5205>“And is this thing you put here going to provide it?” asked Quincey.</t5205> <t5206>“Oh my God! Is this a game?</t5206><t5207>”</t5207>
<t5208>“Yes.</t5208><t5209>”</t5209>
<t5210>"What is it that you are using?"</t5210> <t5211>This time the question came from Arthur.</t5211> <t5212>Van Helsing answered, lifting his hat respectfully:</t5212>
<t5213>“Communion bread.</t5213> <t5214>I brought it from Amsterdam.</t5214> <t5215>I had my sins forgiven.”</t5215> <t5216>This was a response that surprised even our most skeptical member, and each of us individually felt that it was impossible to display distrust in the face of such a serious purpose as the Professor's, a purpose that could use even the most sacred objects.</t5216> <t5217>In a respectful silence, we took our places near the grave, but in spots where we could hide from the eyes of any approaching person.</t5217> <t5218>I pitied the others, especially Arthur.</t5218> <t5219>Due to my previous visits, my inexperience in this vigil of horror had ended; but still, even I, who had rejected the evidence until an hour ago, felt my heart sinking.</t5219> <t5220>The graves had never seemed so terrifyingly white to me; the cypress, yew, or juniper had never appeared so much like the embodiment of funeral sorrow; the trees or grass had never rustled and swayed so ominously; a tree branch had never creaked so mysteriously, and the howling dogs in the distance had never sent such mournful signals into the night.</t5220>
<t5221>There was a long silence, a great, painful void, and then a sharp "shh" sound came from the Professor.</t5221> <t5222>He pointed to a spot, and below, from the direction of the distant badger-tree road, we saw a white figure approaching - a barely discernible white figure holding something black on its chest.</t5222> <t5223>The figure stopped, and at that moment, a beam of moonlight filtered through the passing clouds; we were astonished to see a woman with dark hair, shrouded in burial clothes, revealed before our eyes.</t5223>
<t5224>We couldn't see his face because he was bent over something we understood to be a fair-haired child.</t5224><t5225>There was a pause, and then a sharp, short scream was heard, like that of a small child in sleep or a dog dreaming by the fire.</t5225><t5226>We were just about to leap forward when we stopped at the warning hand of the Professor, whom we could see because he was standing behind the yew tree; then, as we watched him, the white figure began to move forward again.</t5226><t5227>It was now close enough for us to see clearly, and the moonlight was still in place.</t5227><t5228>My heart turned to ice, and I could hear Arthur breathing heavily, for we had recognized the figure of Lucy Westenra.</t5228><t5229>What we saw was Lucy Westenra, but how she had changed.</t5229><t5230>Her sweetness had turned into diamond-like hardness, heartless cruelty, and her purity into wanton lust.</t5230><t5231>Van Helsing stepped forward, and following his movement, we also advanced; we lined up at the entrance of the tomb.</t5231><t5232>Van Helsing raised his lamp and lifted its cover; thanks to the intense light falling on her face, we could see that Lucy's lips were crimson with fresh blood and that the blood had trickled down her chin, staining her shroud of fine linen.</t5232>
<t5233>We shuddered with horror.</t5233> <t5234>I could see that even Van Helsing's nerves were frayed in the flickering light.</t5234> <t5235>Arthur was standing beside me, and if I hadn't held his arm for support, he would have fallen.</t5235>
<t5236>Lucy -I call this thing in front of us "Lucy" because it had taken her shape- retreated with an angry growl like a cat caught off guard when she saw us; then her eyes roamed over us.</t5236> <t5237>These were Lucy's eyes in shape and color; but instead of the pure, gentle pupils we knew, there were sinful and hellfire-filled eyes.</t5237> <t5238>At that moment, what remained of my love turned into hatred and disgust; if she needed to be killed then, I could have done it with ruthless pleasure.</t5238> <t5239>When she looked, her eyes sparkled with malevolent light and her face was crowned with a lascivious smile.</t5239> <t5240>Oh God! How it made my hair stand on end to see this!</t5240> <t5241>With a careful movement, she threw the child she had been diligently holding to her chest to the ground with a heartless motion reminiscent of a demon, and as she did so, she growled at him like a dog growling at a bone.</t5241> <t5242>The child let out a high-pitched scream and lay on the ground moaning.</t5242> <t5243>There was a cold-bloodedness in the act itself that caused Arthur to groan; when Lucy approached him with open arms and a wanton smile, Arthur retreated and hid his face behind his hands.</t5243>
<t5244>But she was still moving forward with a seductive and sensual grace:</t5244>
<t5245>"Come to me, Arthur."</t5245> <t5246>"Leave the others and come to me."</t5246> <t5247>"My arms are open to you."</t5247> <t5248>"Come and let us find peace together."</t5248> <t5249>"Come, my husband, come!"</t5249><t5250>"</t5250>

<t5255>But about half a meter from the door, he stopped as if caught by an irresistible force.</t5255> <t5256>Then he turned, and his face was revealed in the light of the clearly shining moon and the lamp whose light did not waver with Van Helsing's iron nerves.</t5256> <t5257>I had never seen such a malevolent astonishment on a face before, and I believe that such a sight will never again be seen by mortal eyes.</t5257> <t5258>The beautiful color of his skin came to life, his eyes seemed to spark with the fires of hell; his forehead wrinkled as if the folds of his flesh were Medusa's snakes, and his beautiful, bloody mouth opened squarely like the masks used by the Greeks and Japanese in religious plays.</t5258> <t5259>If it is possible for a human face to mean death -if looks could kill- we saw it at that moment.</t5259>
<t5260>And thus, for what seemed like an eternity of a full half minute, he remained between the cross held aloft and the sacred barrier at the entrance.</t5260> <t5261>Van Helsing turned to Arthur and broke the silence:</t5261>
<t5262>"Answer me, oh my friend!</t5262> <t5263>Shall I continue with my work?</t5263><t5264>"</t5264>
<t5265>Arthur threw himself onto his knees and responded, hiding his face in his hands:</t5265>
<t5266>“Do what you want, my friend; do what you want.</t5266> <t5267>Such a horror can never be seen again!” And he groaned with all his soul.</t5267> <t5268>Quincey and I moved towards him at the same time and held him by the arms.</t5268> <t5269>We heard the sound of the lamp being extinguished in Van Helsing’s hand; approaching the tomb, he took some of the holy symbols he had previously placed there from the gaps.</t5269> <t5270>When the professor stepped back, we stared in horror and amazement as we saw the woman's material body, which at that moment seemed as real as ours, pass through a crack only a knife's edge could fit through.</t5270> <t5271>We all sighed with relief when we saw the professor calmly placing the paste on the edges of the door again.</t5271>
<t5272>When this task was completed, the Professor lifted the child from the ground and said:</t5272>
<t5273>“Now come, my friends; we can't do anything else until tomorrow.</t5273> <t5274>There is a funeral here at noon, so we will come here shortly after the ceremony.</t5274> <t5275>The friends of the deceased will have left by two o'clock, and when the sexton locks the door, we will stay here.</t5275> <t5276>Then, there will be other tasks to do; but not like tonight.</t5276> <t5277>As for this little one, he hasn't been harmed much and will be healed by tomorrow evening.</t5277> <t5278>Let's leave him here, where the police will find him, just like last night, and then let's go home.” Approaching Arthur, he said:</t5278>
<t5279>“My friend Arthur, you have gone through a bitter trial, but later, when you look back, you will see how necessary it was.</t5279> <t5280>Now you are in bitter waters, my child.</t5280> <t5281>By this time tomorrow, with God's permission, you will have passed these trials and tasted sweet waters; so do not mourn too much.</t5281> <t5282>Until then, I will not ask you to forgive me.</t5282><t5283>”</t5283>
<t5284>Arthur and Quincey came home with me, and we tried to cheer each other up along the way.</t5284> <t5285>We had left the child in a safe place and were tired; therefore, we slept in a manner that was almost like real sleep.</t5285>
<t5286>September 29, night.</t5286> <t5287>- Just before midnight, the three of us - Arthur, Quincey Morris, and I - visited the Professor.</t5287> <t5288>It was strange to notice that we were all dressed in black unanimously.</t5288> <t5289>Of course, Arthur was dressed in black because he was in deep mourning; but the rest of us had dressed this way instinctively.</t5289> <t5290>We arrived at the churchyard at half-past one and wandered around, staying out of sight of the officials, so that when the gravediggers finished their work and the sexton, believing everyone had left, locked the door, the entire place was left to us.</t5290> <t5291>Instead of his small black bag, Van Helsing had a leather bag that resembled a long cricket bag; it was evidently very heavy.</t5291>
<t5292>After being left alone and hearing the last footsteps leaving the churchyard fade away on the road, we silently, as if commanded for this purpose, followed the Professor to the grave.</t5292> <t5293>He unlocked the door, and we entered, closing the door behind us.</t5293> <t5294>Then he took a lamp out of his bag and lit it; then he took out two candles from his bag, which he lit and melted the ends to stick them on the other coffins so they could provide enough light to work.</t5294> <t5295>When he lifted the lid of Lucy's coffin again, we all looked inside -Arthur was trembling like a leaf- and saw the corpse lying there with all its dead beauty.</t5295> <t5296>But there was no love in my heart; in my heart, there was no feeling other than disgust for that horrible Thing that took the shape of Lucy without her soul.</t5296> <t5297>I could even see Arthur's face hardening as he looked into the coffin.</t5297> <t5298>After a while, he said to Van Helsing:</t5298>
<t5299>“Is this really Lucy's body or just a demon that has taken her form?</t5299><t5300>”</t5300>
<t5301>“It is his body, but still not him.</t5301> <t5302>But wait a little; you will see what he was in the past and what he is now.</t5302><t5303>”</t5303>
<t5304>What we saw, lying there, was like Lucy's nightmare; sharp teeth, bloody, lustful lips - which sent shivers down one's spine - all that sexual and non-spiritual appearance that seemed like a diabolical imitation of Lucy's sweet innocence.</t5304> <t5305>Van Helsing, with all his usual methodicalness, began to take various things out of his bag and prepare them for use.</t5305> <t5306>First, a soldering iron and some solder, then a small gas lamp that burned with fierce blue flames and emitted gas when lit in a corner of the grave, then his surgical knives which he left within reach, and finally a round wooden stake about seven or eight centimeters wide and approximately ninety centimeters long.</t5306> <t5307>The tip of the stake had been hardened and sharpened by being roasted in the fire.</t5307> <t5308>Along with this stake came a heavy hammer, similar to those used in homes to break large pieces in the coal shed.</t5308> <t5309>To me, the Doctor's preparation for any task is enlightening and invigorating, but the effect on Arthur and Quincey was to throw them into a kind of horror.</t5309> <t5310>But both of them kept their courage and stood quietly.</t5310>
<t5311>When everything was ready, Van Helsing began to speak:</t5311>
<t5312>"Before we start, let me tell you this; what we are about to do comes from the knowledge and experience of everyone who has studied the power of the ancients and the Undead.</t5312> <t5313>When they transform into the Undead, the curse of immortality comes with it; <t5344>The thing in the coffin writhed in agony; from the open, red lips came a disgusting, blood-curdling scream.</t5344><t5345>Its body shook and trembled, twisting and contorting wildly; its sharp white teeth clashed together, cutting its lips until its mouth filled with red foam.</t5345><t5346>But Arthur did not hesitate.</t5346><t5347>As his arm rose and fell without trembling, he drove the merciful stake deeper, even as blood spurted from the shattered heart.</t5347><t5348>His face was resolute, and the expression of holy duty on his face shone; this sight gave us courage, so that our voices seemed to echo in the small tomb chamber.</t5348>

<t5359>Now in the coffin, it was not that repulsive Thing we so despised and left to the person most authorized to destroy it, but Lucy as we had seen her in life, with her unique sweetness and purity.</t5359> <t5360>It was true that there were traces of anxiety, pain, and exhaustion as we had seen in life; but all of these were precious to us because they indicated the reality of her as we had once known her.</t5360> <t5361>We all felt that the holy calmness extending over that ravaged face and body like daylight was the earthly sign and symbol of the eternal calm that would reign forever.</t5361>

<t5423>After the usual bustle on the arrival platform, the crowd dispersed; I was starting to get anxious that I might have missed my guest, when a cute, petite-looking girl came up to me and, after a brief look, said, "Doctor Seward, isn't it?"</t5423>

<t5428>We arrived on time.</t5428> <t5429>Of course, she knew this was a mental hospital, but I could see that she couldn't help but shiver slightly when we entered.</t5429>

<t5438>September 29 - After tidying myself up, I went down to Dr. Seward's study.</t5438> <t5439>I paused for a moment at the door because I thought I heard him talking to someone.</t5439> <t5440>But since he was urging me to be quick, I knocked on the door, and upon hearing him say "Come in," I entered the room.</t5440>

<t5500>29 September.</t5500> <t5501>- I was so engrossed in the dreadful journals of Jonathan Harker and his wife that I allowed time to pass without thinking.</t5501> <t5502>When the servant came and announced that dinner was ready, Ms. Harker had not yet come down, so I said, "She is probably tired; let dinner wait for an hour," and continued with my work.</t5502> <t5503>When Ms. Harker came in, I had just finished her journal.</t5503> <t5504>She was in a sweet beauty, but she looked sad and her eyes were red from crying.</t5504> <t5505>For some reason, this affected me greatly.</t5505> <t5506>God knows, I have had many reasons to shed tears lately!</t5506> <t5507>But the soothing effect of tears was denied to me, and now the sight of those sweet eyes glistening with recently shed tears touched my heart directly.</t5507> <t5508>Therefore, I said as gently as I could:</t5508>

<t5539>29 September.</t5539> <t5540>- After dinner, I went to the study with Dr. Seward.</t5540> <t5541>He brought the phonograph back from my room, and I took my typewriter.</t5541> <t5542>He seated me in a comfortable chair, adjusted the phonograph so I wouldn't have to stand up to touch it, and showed me how to stop it if I wanted to take a break.</t5542> <t5543>Then, with great thoughtfulness, he pulled a chair to sit with his back to me so I could be as free as possible, and started reading.</t5543> <t5544>I placed the fork-shaped metal piece in my ears and listened.</t5544>

<t5551>"With your permission, I will write all this down.</t5551> <t5552>We must be ready for Dr. Van Helsing when he arrives.</t5552> <t5553>I sent a telegram to Jonathan, telling him to come here as soon as he arrives in London from Whitby.</t5553> <t5554>In this matter, dates mean everything, and if we prepare all our materials and arrange all the items in chronological order, we will have done a lot of work.</t5554> <t5555>You said that Lord Godalming and Mr. Morris would also be coming.</t5555> <t5556>When they arrive, we should be in a position to explain all this to them."</t5556> <t5557>For this, I set the phonograph to slow speed and began typing from the beginning of the seventh cylinder.</t5557> <t5558>I was using carbon paper, and thus made three copies of the journal, just like all the other documents.</t5558> <t5559>When I finished the work, it was late, but Dr. Seward had gone to visit his patients; when he finished his work, he came back and sat close to me reading, so I wouldn't feel too lonely while working.</t5559> <t5560>What a good and thoughtful person he is; the world seems full of good men - despite the monsters.</t5560> <t5561>Before leaving his side, I remembered what Jonathan wrote in his journal about the Professor being disturbed by something he read in the evening newspaper at the Exeter station; therefore, when I saw that Dr. Seward kept his newspapers, I borrowed the files of the Westminster and Pall Mall Gazettes and took them to my room.</t5561> <t5562>I remembered how much the clippings I cut from the Dailygraph and Whitby Gazettes helped us understand the terrible events that occurred in Whitby when Count Dracula came ashore; so, I will look through all the evening newspapers that have been published since then, hoping to find a new clue.</t5562> <t5563>I am not sleepy, and working will soothe me.</t5563>
<t5564>Dr. Seward's journal</t5564>
<t5565>September 30 - Mr. Harker arrived at nine o'clock.</t5565> <t5566>He received his wife's telegram just before setting off.</t5566> <t5567>If it's possible to judge by looking at his face, he is an exceptionally intelligent and energetic person.</t5567> <t5568>If what is written in his journal is true - and judging by my astonishing personal experiences, it must be - he is also someone with very strong nerves.</t5568> <t5569>Descending into the tomb chamber for the second time is a considerable act of courage.</t5569> <t5570>After reading what he wrote about the events, I was prepared to meet a good example of manliness, but I was not quite ready to meet the calm, businessman-like gentleman who arrived here today.</t5570>

<t5590>I found Renfield in his room, sitting quietly with his hands clasped, laughing harmlessly.</t5590> <t5591>At that moment, he looked as sane as anyone I had ever seen.</t5591> <t5592>I sat down and talked with him about many subjects, all of which he approached naturally.</t5592> <t5593>Then he spontaneously began to talk about returning home—a topic he had never mentioned during his stay here, as far as I knew.</t5593> <t5594>In fact, he spoke quite confidently about being released immediately.</t5594> <t5595>If I had not spoken with Harker and read the letters detailing the dates of his sudden outbursts, I would have been ready to sign off after a short observation.</t5595> <t5596>In this situation, I am quite suspicious.</t5596> <t5597>All those outbursts are somehow connected to the Count's proximity to here.</t5597> <t5598>Then, what does this absolute calmness mean?</t5598> <t5599>Could it mean that his instinct is pleased with the vampire's certain victory?</t5599> <t5600>Wait; he is a zoophagous, and in his wild ramblings at the chapel door of the abandoned house, he always spoke of "my Master."</t5600> <t5601>All this seems to confirm our thoughts.</t5601> <t5602>Still, after a while, I left him; my friend is currently too sane for me to examine deeply with questions.</t5602> <t5603>He might start thinking, and then!..</t5603> <t5604>Thus, I walked away from him.</t5604> <t5605>I do not trust his calm demeanor; therefore, I told the nurse to watch him carefully and to have a straitjacket ready if necessary.</t5605>
<t5606>Jonathan Harker's journal</t5606>
<t5607>29 September, on the train to London.</t5607><t5608>- When I received Mr. Billington's kind letter, in which he said he would give me all the information he could, I thought it best to go to Whitby and conduct my desired research on site.</t5608><t5609>My aim now was to trace the Count's dreadful cargo to its location in London.</t5609><t5610>Then, we could deal with him.</t5610><t5611>His pleasant son, Billington, met me at the station and brought me to his father's house, where they had decided I should stay the night.</t5611><t5612>They showed true Yorkshire hospitality: giving the guest everything and leaving him free to do as he pleased.</t5612><t5613>They all knew I was busy and that my visit would be short, and Mr. Billington had prepared all the documents related to the transport of the crates in his study.</t5613><t5614>Seeing one of the letters I had previously seen on the Count's desk before learning of his diabolical plans almost caused me to have a fit.</t5614><t5615>Everything was done carefully, systematically, and with sensitivity.</t5615><t5616>He seemed prepared for any accidental obstacle that might arise on the path to achieving his goals.</t5616><t5617>In modern terms, he "left nothing to chance," and the absolute precision with which his instructions were carried out was merely the logical result of his meticulousness.</t5617><t5618>I saw and noted the invoice: "Fifty crates of ordinary soil for experimental purposes." <t5625>September 30.</t5625> <t5626>- The station master was kind enough to give me a note to take to his old friend, the station master at King’s Cross, so that when I arrived there the next morning, I could ask him questions about the arrival of the crates.</t5626> <t5627>He immediately introduced me to the clerks who were handling the matter, and I saw that the cargo lists matched the original invoice.</t5627> <t5628>Here, the opportunities for extraordinary thirst were limited; but they had been taken advantage of in a more noble manner, and once again I had to deal with the result in an expostfacto manner.</t5628>

<t5647>Mina Harker's diary</t5647>
<t5648>September 30 - I am so happy that I almost don't know how to control myself.</t5648> <t5649>I think I am reacting this way to the fear that won't leave me: the fear that this terrible event and the reopening of the old wound could harm Jonathan.</t5649> <t5650>I watched his departure to Whitby with as much courage as I could muster, but I felt as if I were sick with worry.</t5650> <t5651>But this effort did him good.</t5651> <t5652>He has never been as determined, as strong, or possessed such fierce energy as he does now.</t5652> <t5653>Just as dear kind-hearted Professor Van Helsing said: It was a true example of courage, and he is getting better while experiencing a tension that could kill someone of weaker constitution.</t5653> <t5654>When he returned, he was full of life, hope, and determination; we have arranged everything for tonight.</t5654> <t5655>I feel like I am going mad with excitement.</t5655> <t5656>One must pity something that hunts like the Count.</t5656> <t5657>Here it is: This Thing is not human - not even an animal.</t5657> <t5658>Reading Dr. Seward's writings about Lucy's death and what happened afterwards is enough to dry up the source of compassion in one's heart.</t5658>

<t5841>Mina Harker's diary</t5841>
<t5842>September 30 - When we met in Dr. Seward's study two hours after the six o'clock dinner, we had unconsciously formed a sort of committee or council.</t5842> <t5843>When Professor Van Helsing entered the room, he took the seat at the head of the table, as indicated by Dr. Seward.</t5843> <t5844>He seated me to his right and asked me to take on the role of secretary; Jonathan sat next to me.</t5844> <t5845>Opposite us were Lord Godalming, Dr. Seward, and Mr. Morris - Lord Godalming sat next to the Professor and Dr. Seward took the middle seat.</t5845> <t5846>The Professor said:</t5846>

<t5852>There are beings called vampires; some of us have evidence that they truly exist.</t5852> <t5853>Even if we don't have proof from our own unhappy experience, the teachings and records of the past provide enough evidence for sane people.</t5853> <t5854>I admit that I approached this with skepticism at first.</t5854> <t5855>If I hadn't trained myself to be open-minded over the years, I wouldn't have believed it until the truth roared in my ear at such a time, 'Look! still, with the help of necromancy and as the root of the word indicates, it means seeing the future through the dead and that the dead it can approach come under its command, it is a ruthless and more than ruthless, a heartless demon, and it has no emotion in its heart, within certain limits, it can appear at any time, in any place, and in any form it desires, within a certain distance, it can control the air: it can create storms, mist, lightning, it can command lesser creatures - rats, owls, and bats - moths, foxes, and wolves; <t5877>While the professor was speaking, Jonathan had held my hand.</t5877> <t5878>When I saw his hand reaching out, I was very afraid that the terrifying nature of the danger we were facing would weaken him once again, but feeling his touch meant life to me - so strong, so confident, and so determined.</t5878> <t5879>The hand of the brave man can speak for him, and there is no need for a woman's love to hear his music.</t5879>

<t5891>Van Helsing continued his words with a kind of cheerfulness that indicated serious work had begun.</t5891> <t5892>As with any other matter in life, the issue had to be approached with seriousness and common sense.</t5892>
<t5893>“Alright, you know what we are fighting against, but we are not powerless either.</t5893> <t5894>We have the power of unity on our side - a power spared from the vampire kind, we have the resources of science, the freedom to act and think, and the hours of day and night are equally ours.</t5894> <t5895>In fact, as our powers grow, they become more unrestrained and we are free to use them.</t5895> <t5896>We have a dedication to a purpose and an unselfish end to achieve.</t5896> <t5897>These are important things.</t5897>

<t5900>The only thing we can rely on is traditions and superstitions.</t5900> <t5901>When it comes to matters of life and death - even more than life and death - these may not seem very apparent at first glance.</t5901> <t5902>Nevertheless, we should be glad about it, because firstly, we are compelled to - we have nothing else under our control - and secondly, because ultimately these - tradition and superstition - mean everything.</t5902> <t5903>For others - but not for us - isn't the belief in vampires based on these?</t5903> <t5904>A year ago, in the midst of the scientific, realistic nineteenth century, which of us would have accepted such a possibility?</t5904> <t5905>We even rejected the belief confirmed right before our eyes.</t5905> <t5906>Then, assume for a moment that the belief in the vampire, its boundaries, and its cure are also based on this foundation.</t5906> <t5907>Because, let me tell you, it is recognized wherever mankind exists.</t5907> <t5908>It shines in ancient Greece, ancient Rome, all of Germany, in France, India, even in the Thracian Peninsula, in China, in places far from us under any circumstances, and even today people fear it.</t5908>

<t5992>Dr. Seward's journal</t5992>
<t5993>October 1, 4 AM.</t5993> <t5994>- Just as I was about to leave the house, I received an urgent message from Renfield asking if I could see him as soon as possible because he had something extremely important to tell me.</t5994> <t5995>I told the messenger to inform him that I would attend to his request in the morning and that I was currently busy.</t5995> <t5996>The nurse added:</t5996>

<t6106>Nineteen</t6106>
<t6107>Jonathan Harker's journal</t6107>

<t6294>“I agree with you wholeheartedly,” I replied sincerely, because I did not want him to soften on this matter.</t6294> <t6295>“It is better for Ms. Harker to stay out of this issue.</t6295> <t6296>Things are bad enough for us, who have seen and experienced a lot and have been in very difficult places in our time, but this is no place for a woman and if she had anything to do with this, it would undoubtedly destroy her over time.</t6296><t6297>”</t6297>
<t6298>Thus, Van Helsing went to meet with Ms. Harker and Mr. Harker; Quincey and Art are doing their best to track down the soil boxes.</t6298> <t6299>I will finish my work and meet with them tonight.</t6299>
<t6300>Mina Harker's diary</t6300>
<t6301>October 1st.</t6301> <t6302>- It feels strange to me not to be informed as I was today; after Jonathan's endless trust over the years, to avoid certain topics and the most crucial ones so openly!</t6302> <t6303>After yesterday's exhaustion, I slept in late this morning, and although Jonathan got up late as well, he was up earlier than me.</t6303> <t6304>Before leaving, he spoke to me in a sweeter and softer manner than ever before, but did not say a single word about what happened during the visit to the Count's house.</t6304> <t6305>But still, he must have known how worried I was.</t6305> <t6306>Poor dear man!</t6306> <t6307>I think this situation must have upset him even more than it upset me.</t6307> <t6308>They all decided together that I should not be drawn further into this dreadful matter, and I did not oppose it.</t6308> <t6309>But to think that he is hiding something from me!</t6309> <t6310>And now, even though I know it stems from my husband's great love and the good, good intentions of those other strong men, I am crying like a fool...</t6310>
<t6311>This did me good.</t6311> <t6312>One day Jonathan will tell me everything, and so that he doesn't think I'm hiding anything from him for even a moment, as always, I'm keeping my journal.</t6312> <t6313>Then, if he doubts my trust, I will show him every thought that comes from my heart written down, so that his dear eyes can read them.</t6313> <t6314>Today, I feel strangely sad and listless.</t6314> <t6315>It must be a reaction to that horrific excitement.</t6315>
<t6316>Last night, when the men left, I went to bed just because they told me to do so.</t6316><t6317>I wasn't sleepy and I felt a consuming anxiety.</t6317><t6318>Since the day Jonathan came to London to see me, I kept reviewing everything that happened, and everything seems like a horrifying tragedy, as if fate is relentlessly pushing towards a predetermined end.</t6318><t6319>Everything done, no matter how right, seems to cause the very thing we find the worst.</t6319><t6320>If I hadn't gone to Whitby, perhaps dear poor Lucy could be here with us today.</t6320><t6321>If she hadn't gone to visit the churchyard until I came, and if she hadn't gone there with me during the day, she wouldn't have walked there in her sleep, and if she hadn't gone there in her sleep at night, that monster couldn't have destroyed her like this.</t6321><t6322>Oh, why did I go to Whitby?</t6322><t6323>Here I am, crying again!</t6323><t6324>I don't know what happened to me today.</t6324><t6325>I must hide this from Jonathan, because if he learns that I cried twice this morning - I, who never cry on my own and Jonathan has never caused me to shed a single tear - the poor man would be devastated with worry.</t6325><t6326>I must put on a brave face, and if I feel like crying, he must never know.</t6326><t6327>I think this is one of the lessons we poor women must learn...</t6327>
<t6328>I can't remember how I fell asleep last night.</t6328> <t6329>I remember suddenly hearing dogs barking and a lot of strange noises coming from Mr. Renfield's room somewhere below this room, as if someone was praying very loudly.</t6329> <t6330>And then, silence fell over everything, a silence so deep that it frightened me, and I got up to look out the window.</t6330> <t6331>Everything was dark and quiet, and the dark shadows cast by the moonlight seemed filled with their own mystery.</t6331> <t6332>Not a single thing was moving, everything seemed as terrible and still as death or fate; so much so that the thin line of white mist that seemed to be crawling towards the house across the grass at an almost imperceptible speed seemed to have a consciousness and life of its own.</t6332> <t6333>I think it did me good to get away from the subject because when I returned to bed, a heaviness had settled over me.</t6333> <t6334>I lay down for a while, but I couldn't sleep much, so I got up again and looked out the window.</t6334> <t6335>The mist was spreading and had now come very close to the house, so much so that I could see it clinging to the wall in a thick layer as if it were secretly reaching for the windows.</t6335> <t6336>The poor man was making more noise than ever, and although I couldn't distinguish a single word he was saying, I could detect a peculiar passionate plea in his voice.</t6336> <t6337>Then, the sound of a struggle came; I knew the nurses were attending to him.</t6337> <t6338>I was so scared that I crawled into bed and covered my head with the blankets, plugging my ears with my fingers.</t6338> <t6339>At that moment, I wasn't sleepy at all, or at least I thought so; but I must have fallen asleep because I don't remember anything until Jonathan woke me up in the morning, except for the dreams I had.</t6339> <t6340>I think it took me some effort and time to understand where I was and to realize that it was Jonathan leaning over me.</t6340> <t6341>My dream was quite unusual and was almost an example of thoughts conceived while awake blending into or continuing in the dream.</t6341>
<t6342>I thought I was asleep and waiting for Jonathan to arrive.</t6342> <t6343>I was very worried about him and had no strength to move; my feet, hands, and mind were heavy, so nothing could progress at its usual pace.</t6343> <t6344>Because of this, I slept a troubled sleep and thought.</t6344> <t6345>Then, it occurred to me that the air was heavy, humid, and cold.</t6345> <t6346>I covered my face with the blankets again and, in astonishment, saw that my surroundings were dim.</t6346> <t6347>The gas lamp I had left on for Jonathan but then dimmed, clearly appeared like a tiny red dot in the thickening mist seeping into the room.</t6347> <t6348>Then, I remembered that I had closed the window before getting into bed.</t6348> <t6349>Actually, I would have gotten up to be sure, but a kind of leaden weight seemed to chain my arms, legs, and even my will.</t6349> <t6350>I lay still and endured it; that was all; I closed my eyes but could still see through my eyelids.</t6350> <t6351>(How marvelous are the tricks our dreams play on us and our ability to imagine accordingly.</t6351><t6352>)</t6352> <t6353>As the mist thickened more and more, I could now see how it was entering because it was seeping in not from the window but from the joints of the door, like smoke - or the white steam of boiling water.</t6353> <t6354>It continued to thicken until it seemed to form a column of cloud in the room, at the top of which I could see the gas lamp glowing like a red eye.</t6354> <t6355>The things in my head were swirling around just like the cloudy column in the room; among this, the phrase "Pillar of cloud by day, pillar of fire by night" from the Holy Bible came to mind.</t6355> <t6356>Was it really a kind of spiritual guide coming to me in my sleep?</t6356> <t6357>But this column was composed of both the guidance of night and day, because the fire, which gained a new allure for me upon reflection, was in the red eye; until, as I watched, the fire split and shone through the mist above me, just like the two red eyes Lucy mentioned during her momentary mental lapse when the setting sun's light hit the windows of Saint Mary Church on the slope.</t6357> <t6358>Suddenly, I was terrified, remembering that Jonathan had seen those dreadful women transform from mist into reality in the moonlight.</t6358> <t6359>The last conscious effort of my imagination was a very angry white face emerging from the mist and leaning over me.</t6359> <t6360>I must be careful of such dreams, for if they become numerous, they can take one's mind.</t6360> <t6361>If I weren't afraid of worrying them, I would ask Dr. Van Helsing or Dr. Seward to prescribe me a sleeping aid.</t6361> <t6362>Such a dream right now would be woven into the fears they have for me.</t6362> <t6363>Tonight, I will try to sleep naturally.</t6363> <t6364>If I can't sleep, I will have them give me a dose of chloral tomorrow night; using it once won't harm me, and it will give me a good night's sleep.</t6364> <t6365>Last night tired me so much that I wouldn't be this exhausted even if I hadn't slept at all.</t6365>
<t6366>2</t6366> <t6367>October, 10 PM.</t6367> <t6368>- I slept last night, but I didn't dream.</t6368> <t6369>I must have slept deeply; I didn't wake up when Jonathan came to bed; but the sleep didn't refresh me, because today I feel terribly weak and unwell.</t6369> <t6370>Yesterday, I spent the whole day either trying to read or lying down and dozing.</t6370> <t6371>In the afternoon, Mr. Renfield asked if he could see me.</t6371> <t6372>The poor man was very kind and kissed my hand, wishing God's protection upon me as he left.</t6372> <t6373>This affected me greatly in some way; whenever I think of him, I cry.</t6373> <t6374>This is a new weakness I need to be careful about.</t6374> <t6375>If Jonathan knew I was crying, he would be devastated.</t6375> <t6376>He and the others were out until dinner and they all returned tired.</t6376> <t6377>I did my best to cheer them up and I think this effort did me good, because I forgot how tired I was.</t6377> <t6378>After dinner, they sent me to bed and said they were all going out to smoke together, but I knew they wanted to tell each other what had happened to them during the day; from Jonathan's demeanor, I could see he had something important he wanted to share.</t6378> <t6379>I wasn't as sleepy as I should have been; therefore, before they left, I asked Dr. Seward to give me some kind of sleeping medicine because I hadn't slept well the previous night.</t6379> <t6380>He kindly prepared a sleeping draught for me, assuring me it was very mild and wouldn't harm me...</t6380> <t6381>I took the medicine and am still waiting for the distant sleep to come.</t6381> <t6382>I hope I haven't made a mistake because when sleep starts to court me, a new fear arises: I hope I haven't been foolish by depriving myself of the power to wake up.</t6382> <t6383>I might want to wake up.</t6383> <t6384>Here comes sleep.</t6384> <t6385>Good night.</t6385>
<t6386>XX</t6386>
<t6387>Jonathan Harker's journal</t6387>
<t6388>October 1, evening.</t6388> <t6389>I found Thomas Snelling at his home in Benthal Green, but unfortunately, he was in no condition to remember anything.</t6389> <t6390>Knowing that I would go there and give him beer money had tempted him, and he had gotten drunk early.</t6390> <t6391>However, from his wife, who seemed to be an honest, poor woman, I learned that the man carried the boxes together and that the authoritative Smollet was merely his assistant.</t6391> <t6392>Therefore, I went by carriage to Walworth and found Mr. Joseph Smollet at home, with his jacket off, drinking tea from a saucer.</t6392> <t6393>An honest and intelligent man, evidently a good and reliable worker, with a mind of his own.</t6393> <t6394>He remembered the entire incident regarding the boxes and gave the destinations of the boxes from a perfect notebook with curled corners, which he took out from a mysterious pocket at the back of his trousers, containing thick, semi-faded hieroglyph-like notes written with a pencil.</t6394> <t6395>He said there were six boxes he picked up from Carfax and loaded into the carriage, which he left at 197 Chicksand Street, Mile End New Town, and another six boxes he left at Jamaica Road, Bermondsey.</t6395> <t6396>If the Count intends to distribute these hideous refuges all over London, these places were chosen as the first delivery points, so that he could complete the distribution in more detail later.</t6396> <t6397>This systematic approach in the execution of this task made me think that he did not intend to limit himself to the two sides of London.</t6397> <t6398>Now he had settled at the eastern end of the north shore and the eastern end of the south shore and to the south.</t6398> <t6399>The north and west were never meant to be excluded from his diabolical plan - especially not the very center of the city and the favored parts of London, the southwest, and the southern hub.</t6399> <t6400>I started talking to Smollet again and asked him if he could tell me whether there were any other boxes taken from Carfax.</t6400>
<t6401>He answered like this:</t6401>
<t6402>"Well boss, you treated me very well," -I had given him half a gold coin- "and I will tell you everything I know.</t6402> <t6403>I heard a man named Bloxam telling his friend at the Hare and Hounds Tavern in Pincher’s Alley about four nights ago that he did a very dusty job at the old house in Purfleet.</t6403> <t6404>There aren't many such jobs around here, and I think maybe Sam Bloxam can tell you something."</t6404> <t6405>I asked him where I could find this man.</t6405> <t6406>I told him that if he could find the address for me, it would be worth another half gold coin.</t6406> <t6407>So, he finished the rest of his tea in one gulp and stood up, saying he would start investigating right away.</t6407> <t6408>He stopped at the door and said:</t6408>
<t6409>“Listen, boss, there's no point in keeping you here.</t6409> <t6410>I might find Sam soon or I might not, but in any case, he won't be able to tell you much tonight.</t6410> <t6411>When Sam starts drinking, he becomes quite a rare character.</t6411> <t6412>If you can give me an envelope with a stamp and your address on it, I can find out where Sam might be tonight and mail it to you.</t6412> <t6413>But you'd better start looking for him early in the morning or you might not catch him, because Sam gets up early no matter how much he drank the night before.</t6413><t6414>”</t6414>
<t6415>This was very convenient; thus, one of the children went to get an envelope and a sheet of paper with a penny and kept the change for themselves.</t6415> <t6416>When the girl came back, I wrote the address on the envelope and stuck the stamp, and after Smollet once again promised to mail it when he found the address, I headed home.</t6416> <t6417>One way or another, we are on the trail.</t6417> <t6418>I am tired tonight and want to sleep.</t6418> <t6419>Mina is in a deep sleep and looks a bit too pale; her eyes look as if she has been crying.</t6419> <t6420>Poor darling, I have no doubt that the thought of secrets being kept from her worries her; this might cause her to worry twice as much for me and the others.</t6420> <t6421>But this is for the best.</t6421> <t6422>Experiencing disappointment and worry in this way is better than having her nerves shattered.</t6422> <t6423>I must be resolute as I carry this special burden of silence on my shoulders.</t6423> <t6424>Under no circumstances should I discuss this matter with her.</t6424> <t6425>To be honest, this might not be a difficult task, as she has been reticent about this matter for a while and has not spoken about the Count or his actions since we explained our decision to her.</t6425>
<t6426>2</t6426> <t6427>October, evening.</t6427> <t6428>- A long, challenging, and exciting day.</t6428> <t6429>With the first mail, an envelope arrived with a dirty piece of paper stuffed inside, previously addressed; on the paper, written with a carpenter's pencil and in large handwriting, it said:</t6429>

<t6454>“Well, boss, I forget the numbers, but it was only a few buildings past a big white church or something like that.</t6454> <t6455>It was also an old, dusty house, though not as dusty as the damn house where we picked up the crates.”</t6455> <t6456>“If both were vacant at the time, how did you get into the houses?” “There was an old man waiting for me at the house in Purfleet.</t6456> <t6457>He helped me lift the crates and load them into the car.</t6457> <t6458>By God, even though he was a thin old man with a white mustache, he was the strongest man I've ever met.</t6458><t6459>”</t6459>
<t6460>How these words frightened me.</t6460>
<t6461>“The man lifted one end of the chests as if he were carrying tea, but I had already started huffing and puffing before I could lift the end I was holding - and I'm no weakling either.</t6461><t6462>”</t6462>

<t7300>“Without a doubt, God will repair all the mistakes made by the world and the children He placed there on Judgment Day, so it is possible that you may have to bear this stain until the time He deems appropriate.</t7300> <t7301>And oh, Madam Mina, dear, dear, we who love you hope to be there to see that the red scar, which is a sign that God knows what has happened, has passed and left your forehead as clean as the heart we know.</t7301> <t7302>Because we know as well as our own lives that when God finds it right to lift the great burden from us, that scar will also pass.</t7302> <t7303>Until then, we will carry our Cross just as His Son obeyed His will.</t7303> <t7304>Perhaps we are the instruments chosen for His sweet joy, and just as the other rose with blows and shame, with tears and blood, with doubts and fears, and with everything that separates man from God, we too will rise by His command.</t7304><t7305>”</t7305>

<t7310>Then, the time came to get to work.</t7310> <t7311>Therefore, I bid farewell to Mina; it was a departure we would not forget until the day of our death, and we set off.</t7311>
<t7312>I was determined about one thing: If we were to find out that Mina had to become a vampire in the end, she would not go to that unknown and terrifying place alone.</t7312> <t7313>I think this is why, in the past, a single vampire meant many vampires; just as their disgusting bodies could only rest on consecrated ground, the most sacred love also recruits soldiers into their vile ranks.</t7313>
<t7314>We entered Carfax without any trouble and found everything in its place on the first try.</t7314> <t7315>In such an ordinary environment of neglect, dust, and decay, it was hard to believe that such a familiar horror could have a foothold.</t7315> <t7316>If we were not determined and if it were not for the terrifying memories that spurred us on, we might have struggled to make progress in our task.</t7316> <t7317>We found no documents or any indication of the house's use, and the boxes in the old chapel stood as they did the last time we saw them.</t7317> <t7318>As we stood in front of the boxes, Dr. Van Helsing said solemnly:</t7318>
<t7319>“And now, my friends, we have a duty here.</t7319> <t7320>We must cleanse this soil, which he brought from afar for such a dreadful purpose, of its sacred memories.</t7320> <t7321>He chose this soil because it is blessed.</t7321> <t7322>Thus, we will defeat him with his own weapon, for we will make this soil even more sacred.</t7322> <t7323>It was blessed for man to use in this way, now we are blessing it for God.”</t7323> <t7324>As he spoke, he took a screwdriver and a wrench out of his bag, and shortly after, the lid of one of the chests was opened.</t7324> <t7325>The soil smelled musty; but somehow we didn't seem to mind, because all our attention was on the Professor.</t7325> <t7326>He took a piece of blessed bread from its box and respectfully placed it on the soil, then began to screw the lid back on; as he worked, we were helping him.</t7326>
<t7327>We performed the same operation on each of the large chests one by one and left them, from the outside, as we found them; but inside each of them was a piece of blessed bread.</t7327>
<t7328>When we closed the door behind us, the Professor said solemnly:</t7328>
<t7329>"We have done this much already.</t7329> <t7330>If we can be as successful with the others, tonight's sunset may shine on Madam Mina's forehead as white and spotless as ivory!</t7330><t7331>"</t7331>
<t7332>As we crossed the grassy area on the way to the station to catch our train, we could see the front facade of the mental hospital.</t7332> <t7333>I eagerly looked in that direction and saw Mina at the window of my room.</t7333> <t7334>I waved to her and nodded to indicate that our task there had been successfully completed.</t7334> <t7335>She also nodded in response to show that she understood.</t7335> <t7336>The last I saw of her, she was waving goodbye.</t7336> <t7337>We barely reached the station and only just caught the train as it was hissing steam on the platform.</t7337>
<t7338>I wrote this on the train.</t7338>
<t7339>Piccadilly, 12:30.</t7339> <t7340>- As we were about to reach Fenchurch Street, Lord Godalming said to me:</t7340>
<t7341>“Quincey and I will find a locksmith.</t7341> <t7342>It would be better if you didn't come with us in case there's any trouble, because under these circumstances, it wouldn't look too bad for us to break into an empty house.</t7342> <t7343>But you are a lawyer, and the United Law Society might tell you that you shouldn't do this.”</t7343> <t7344>Since I hadn't yet shared any risk of reproach, I objected, but he continued: “Besides, if we are not too many, we will attract less attention.</t7344> <t7345>My title will help us deal with the locksmith and any police that might come.</t7345> <t7346>The best thing for you is to go with Jack and the Professor, stay somewhere in Green Park where you can see the house, and when you see the door open and the locksmith leave, come together.</t7346> <t7347>We will keep watch for you and let you in.</t7347><t7348>”</t7348>

<t7361>After searching inside for a while, he took out some tools and arranged them neatly beside him.</t7361> <t7362>Then, he stood up, looked through the keyhole, blew into it, and turned to his employers to say something.</t7362> <t7363>Lord Godalming smiled, and the man took a large bunch of keys in his hand, selected one, and began to test the lock as if trying to feel his way with it.</t7363> <t7364>After trying and failing for a while by feel, he tried a second one, then a third.</t7364> <t7365>Suddenly, the door opened with a slight push, and he and the locksmith entered the hall.</t7365> <t7366>We waited without moving; my cigar was burning brightly, but Van Helsing's had completely gone out.</t7366> <t7367>We waited patiently when we saw the worker go out and bring his bag inside.</t7367> <t7368>Then he kept the door ajar and steadied it with his knee while placing the key in the lock.</t7368> <t7369>Finally, he handed this key to Lord Godalming, who took out his wallet and gave him something.</t7369> <t7370>The man touched his hat, took his bag, put on his coat, and left; not a single person saw this entire process.</t7370>
<t7371>When Adam had gone quite a distance, the three of us crossed the street and knocked on the door.</t7371> <t7372>The door was immediately opened by Quincey Morris, behind whom stood Lord Godalming lighting his cigar.</t7372>
<t7373>As we entered, "This place smells disgusting," said Lord Godalming.</t7373> <t7374>Indeed, it smelled disgusting -like the old chapel at Carfax- and based on our past experience, we clearly understood that the Count had been using this place freely.</t7374> <t7375>We set out to explore the house; we moved together in case of an attack, because we knew we had a strong and cunning enemy to deal with, and we did not yet know if the Count was at home.</t7375> <t7376>In the dining room at the back of the hall, we found eight boxes of earth.</t7376> <t7377>Only eight of the nine boxes we were looking for! Our work was not finished, and it would never be until we found that missing box.</t7377> <t7378>First, we opened the shutters of a window overlooking a narrow courtyard with stone paving, on the empty side of a barn painted to look like the front of a small house.</t7378> <t7379>There were no windows in the barn, so we had no fear of being watched.</t7379> <t7380>We did not waste time examining the boxes.</t7380> <t7381>With the tools we had brought, we opened them one by one and did to them what we had done to the boxes in the old chapel.</t7381> <t7382>At that moment, it was clear that the Count was not at home, and we began to search for his personal belongings.</t7382>
<t7383>After quickly glancing through all the rooms from the basement to the attic, we concluded that everything that might belong to the Count was found in the dining room, and thus we began to carefully examine them.</t7383> <t7384>The items were arranged in a neat disorder on the large dining table.</t7384> <t7385>The deeds to the house in Piccadilly were in a large bundle, along with the purchase documents for the houses in Mile End and Bermondsey, letter papers, envelopes, pens, and ink.</t7385> <t7386>All of them were covered with a thin wrapping paper to protect them from dust.</t7386> <t7387>Additionally, there was a clothes brush, a brush and comb, a jug, and a bowl - the latter containing dirty water that appeared red, as if stained with blood.</t7387> <t7388>Finally, there was a bundle of keys of various types and sizes, likely belonging to the other houses.</t7388> <t7389>After examining this last finding, Lord Godalming and Quincey Morris, who were taking notes on the various addresses of the houses in the east and south, took a large bunch of keys and set out to destroy the boxes in those places.</t7389> <t7390>The rest of us are waiting as patiently as we can for their return - or for the Count's arrival.</t7390>
<t7391>XXIII</t7391>
<t7392>Dr. Seward's journal</t7392>
<t7393>October 3.</t7393> <t7394>- Time seemed to pass terribly slowly while waiting for the arrival of Godalming and Quincey Morris.</t7394> <t7395>The Professor tried to keep our minds constantly engaged to keep them active.</t7395> <t7396>From his occasional sideways glance at Harker, I could see his good intentions.</t7396> <t7397>The poor man was crushed under a pain that was terrible to witness.</t7397> <t7398>Last night, he was a man with a strong, young face, full of energy and with dark brown hair, looking sincere and happy.</t7398> <t7399>Today, however, he is a weary, grim-faced man with white hair, sunken, burning eyes, and deep lines of pain etched into his face.</t7399> <t7400>His energy is still intact; in fact, he is like a living flame.</t7400> <t7401>This might still be his salvation, because if everything goes well, it will help him in this desperate situation; then, somehow, he will awaken again to the realities of life.</t7401> <t7402>Poor man, I thought my own troubles were bad enough, but his!</t7402> <t7403>The Professor knows this very well and is doing his best to keep Harker's mind occupied.</t7403> <t7404>The things he was saying were interesting under these circumstances.</t7404> <t7405>As far as I can remember, it went like this:</t7405>
<t7406>“Since the day they came into my hands, I have repeatedly examined all the documents related to this monster, and the more I worked on them, the greater the necessity of its complete destruction seemed.</t7406> <t7407>In all of them, there are indicators of how it progressed; not only of its power but also of its knowledge of that power.</t7407> <t7408>From the research of my friend Arminius in Budapest, I learned that he was a perfect man while alive.</t7408> <t7409>A soldier, statesman, and alchemist - the latter being the greatest advancement in the science of his time.</t7409> <t7410>He had a great mind, an education incomparable to anyone else, and a heart that knew neither fear nor remorse.</t7410> <t7411>He even dared to enter Scholomance and there was no branch of knowledge he did not engage in during his lifetime.</t7411> <t7412>Well, his mental powers survived physical death; although, his memory seemed incomplete.</t7412> <t7413>In some aspects of the mind, he was like a child, and still is, but he is growing now, and some traits that were initially childish have now become fitting for a man.</t7413> <t7414>He is conducting experiments and doing it well, and if we had not stood in his way, he could have been the father or supporter of a new species whose path lies through Death, not Life - if we fail, he still might be.”</t7414> <t7415>Harker groaned and said: “And all this is plotted against my beloved!</t7415> <t7416>But how is he conducting experiments?</t7416> <t7417>This knowledge could help us defeat him!</t7417><t7418>”</t7418>
<t7419>"From the beginning, since his arrival, he has been slowly but surely testing his own strength; that great, childlike mind is at work.</t7419> <t7420>This is good for us because it is still a childlike mind; because if he had dared to attempt certain things at the very start, he would have surpassed our strength long ago.</t7420> <t7421>Nevertheless, he aims for success and a man with centuries ahead of him can afford to wait and progress slowly.</t7421> <t7422>His principle might be festina lente64.</t7422>
<t7423>“I don't understand,” said Harker wearily.</t7423> <t7424>“Oh, please speak more plainly with me!</t7424> <t7425>Perhaps sorrow and troubles are dulling my mind.</t7425><t7426>”</t7426>
<t7427>The professor gently placed his hand on Harker's shoulder as he spoke: "Ah, my child, I will speak plainly.</t7427> <t7428>Don't you see how this monster has recently been infiltrating knowledge in an experimental manner?</t7428> <t7429>How he used the zoophagous patient to enter our friend John's house; because your Vampire, although he could enter whenever and however he wanted later, could only enter initially when invited by someone from inside.</t7429> <t7430>But these are not the most important experiments.</t7430> <t7431>Don't we see how these large boxes were initially carried by others?</t7431> <t7432>At that time, he didn't know it had to be that way.</t7432> <t7433>But that great, childlike mind of his kept evolving, and then he thought about whether he could carry the box himself.</t7433> <t7434>So, he started helping the carriers, and then, seeing there was nothing to it, he tried to carry them alone.</t7434> <t7435>And thus he made progress and distributed his graves; now no one but him knows where they are hidden.</t7435> <t7436>He might have intended to bury them deep.</t7436> <t7437>Thus, he would only use them at night or when he could change form, both of which would suit his purpose, and no one would know these were his hiding places!</t7437> <t7438>But my child, do not despair; this knowledge came to him far too late!</t7438> <t7439>We have already purified all but one of his sanctuaries, and this will be dealt with before sunset.</t7439> <t7440>Then, he will have no place to move and hide.</t7440> <t7441>I did not allow us to act hastily this morning so that we could be sure.</t7441> <t7442>Don't we have much more at stake compared to him?</t7442> <t7443>Then why shouldn't we act more cautiously than him?</t7443> <t7444>According to my watch, it is one o'clock, and if all is well, our friends Arthur and Quincey have already set out towards us.</t7444> <t7445>Today is our day, and we must proceed with sure steps, even if slowly, and not miss any opportunity.</t7445> <t7446>Look! When those who are not with us now return, we will be five.</t7446><t7447>"</t7447>
<t7448>While he was speaking, we were startled by the knocking on the hall door, the double knock of the telegraph boy.</t7448> <t7449>With a single impulse, we all went out into the hall, and Van Helsing, raising his hand to signal us to be silent, went to the door and opened it.</t7449> <t7450>The boy handed over the delivery.</t7450> <t7451>The professor closed the door again, and after looking at the address, he opened the telegram and read it aloud:</t7451>
<t7452>Pay attention to D.</t7452> <t7453>Now, 12:45, he came hurriedly from Carfax and went quickly south.</t7453> <t7454>He seems to be turning back and may want to see you: Mina.</t7454>
<t7455>There was a silence broken by Jonathan Harker's voice: "Thank God, we will meet soon!" Van Helsing quickly turned to him and said:</t7455>

<t7476>"Everything is fine.</t7476> <t7477>We found both places; each had six chests and we destroyed them all!</t7477><t7478>"</t7478>
<t7479>"Did you get rid of it?" asked the Professor.</t7479>
<t7480>"From his perspective!" We remained silent for a minute, and then Quincey said:</t7480>
<t7481>“There is nothing to do here but wait.</t7481> <t7482>If he doesn't come back by five o'clock, we will need to set off; because it wouldn't be right to leave Ms. Harker alone after sunset.</t7482><t7483>”</t7483>
<t7484>“He will be here soon,” said Van Helsing, who was looking at his pocket notebook at the time.</t7484> <t7485>“Nota bene, Madam’s telegram says he went south of Carfax, which means he will cross the river and can only do so when the tide is low, which should be before one o’clock.</t7485> <t7486>His going south has significance for us.</t7486> <t7487>He is still only suspicious and went first to the place where he would encounter the least obstacles from Carfax.</t7487> <t7488>You must have been in Bermondsey just a little before him.</t7488> <t7489>The fact that he hasn’t come here yet indicates that he then went to Mile End.</t7489> <t7490>This must have taken some of his time, because after that, he must have been transported by some means on the river.</t7490> <t7491>Believe me, my friends, we won’t have to wait much longer from now on.</t7491> <t7492>We need to have an attack plan ready so that we don’t miss any opportunity.</t7492> <t7493>Shh! <t7525>“You think you can stop me, you - with your pale faces lined up like sheep for the slaughter.</t7525> <t7526>But in the end, you will regret it, each one of you!</t7526> <t7527>You think you have deprived me of places where I can rest and relax; but there are others.</t7527> <t7528>My revenge is just beginning!</t7528> <t7529>I have spread it over centuries, and time is working in my favor.</t7529> <t7530>Your beloved girls are already mine, and through them, you and others will also be mine - my creatures to do my bidding and my jackals when I need to feed.</t7530> <t7531>Bah!” With a contemptuous laugh, he quickly passed through the door, and we heard the rusty bolt creak as he locked it behind him.</t7531> <t7532>A door opened and closed further ahead.</t7532> <t7533>Realizing the difficulty of following him into the stable, the Professor was the first to speak as we moved towards the hall.</t7533>
<t7534>“We learned something - actually, a lot!</t7534> <t7535>Despite his brave words, he is afraid of us; he fears time, he fears deprivation!</t7535> <t7536>If that were not the case, why would he be in such a hurry?</t7536> <t7537>His tone of voice gives him away, or my ears are deceiving me.</t7537> <t7538>Why would he take that money?</t7538> <t7539>You go after him quickly.</t7539> <t7540>You are wild animal hunters, and think of him as such.</t7540> <t7541>As for me, I will ensure that nothing here will be of use to him if he happens to return.”</t7541> <t7542>While speaking, he put the remaining money in his pocket, took the deeds in the bundle as Harker had left them, and swept the rest towards the fireplace, setting them all on fire with a match.</t7542> <t7543>Godalming and Morris ran out into the courtyard, Harker had climbed out of the window to follow the Count.</t7543> <t7544>But the Count had bolted the stable door, and when they forced it open, there was no trace of him.</t7544> <t7545>Van Helsing and I tried to search the back of the house, but the narrow streets were empty and no one had seen the Count leave.</t7545>
<t7546>It was almost evening and there was not much time left until sunset.</t7546> <t7547>We had to accept that our plan had fallen through, with sorrowful hearts, we agreed with the Professor's words: "Come, let us return to Madam Mina - poor, poor, dear Madam Mina.</t7547> <t7548>For now, everything that could be done has been done, and there, at least we can protect her.</t7548> <t7549>But we must not fall into despair.</t7549> <t7550>There is only one more box of earth left, and we must try to find it; once that is done, everything will be alright." <t8491>Dr. Seward's journal</t8491>

<t8587>Jonathan Harker's journal</t8587>

<t8602>This simplicity, a mixture of superstitious cunning and commercial logic, spurred Van Helsing into action, and he said: "My friend, that Devil is smarter than some think, and when he meets his match, he knows it!" <t8665>Research foundation.</t8665> <t8666>- Count Dracula's problem is returning to his place.</t8666>
<t8667>(a) Must be taken back by someone.</t8667> <t8668>This is obvious; because if a person could act as they wished, they could transform into a wolf, bat, or another form and leave.</t8668> <t8669>Clearly, in the desperation I am sure he is in -trapped in a wooden box between dawn and sunset- he fears being discovered or having his work interfered with.</t8669>
<t8670>(b) How will it be transported?</t8670> <t8671>- Here, the elimination method might be useful for us.</t8671> <t8672>By road, by rail, or by waterway?</t8672>
<t8673>1.</t8673> <t8674>By road.</t8674> <t8675>- There are endless difficulties that can be encountered, especially when leaving a city.</t8675>
<t8676>(x) There are people; people are curious and they ask questions.</t8676> <t8677>A hint, guess, or doubt about what might be in the chest will ruin it.</t8677>
<t8678>(y) There are or may be customs officers or tax officials to pass through.</t8678>
<t8679>(z) Those who chase him can follow.</t8679> <t8680>This is his greatest fear; to avoid being caught, he even repelled his victim - that is, me - as much as he could!</t8680>
<t8681>2.</t8681> <t8682>By railroad.</t8682> <t8683>- There will be no one responsible for the chest.</t8683> <t8684>He will have to risk the possibility of delay, and with enemies on his trail, a delay would be fatal.</t8684> <t8685>Sure, he could escape at night, but what if he ends up in a foreign place without a refuge to run to?</t8685> <t8686>This is not what he intends, and he does not want to jeopardize his goal.</t8686>
<t8687>3.</t8687> <t8688>By water.</t8688> <t8689>- Indeed, in one sense the safest, but in another sense the most dangerous route.</t8689> <t8690>While in the water, powerless except at night; even then, it can only summon mist, storm, snow, and its wolves.</t8690> <t8691>But if there is a shipwreck, the living water leaves it helpless and swallows it, and it truly disappears.</t8691> <t8692>It can bring the vessel to shore, but if it is in enemy territory without freedom of movement, its situation remains hopeless.</t8692>
<t8693>From the records, we know that it is on the water; therefore, what we need to do is determine which water it is.</t8693>
<t8694>First of all, we need to fully understand what you have done so far; then, we can find some insight into what your next step should be.</t8694>
<t8695>First of all, during a period when he had to manage his time and do his best under tight constraints, we must recognize what he did in London as part of the overall movement plan.</t8695>
<t8696>Secondly, we need to understand what he is doing here, as much as we can infer from the facts we know.</t8696>
<t8697>Regarding the first one, it is clear that he aimed to reach Galaţi and sent an invoice to Varna to deceive us so that we wouldn't learn the real reason for his departure from England; at that time, his sole purpose was to escape.</t8697> <t8698>The proof of this is the instruction letter sent to Immanuel Hildesheim, telling him to receive the crate before sunrise.</t8698> <t8699>There are also instructions given to Petrov Skinski.</t8699> <t8700>Here, we can only speculate; but since Skinski arrived at Hildesheim, there must have been a letter or a message.</t8700>
<t8701>We know that their plans so far have been successful.</t8701> <t8702>Czarina Catherine made an astonishingly fast journey - so much so that it aroused Captain Donelson's suspicion; but his superstition, combined with his shrewdness, played into the Count's hands on his behalf, and he sped rapidly through the mists with a protective wind until he reached Galaţi blindly.</t8702> <t8703>It has been proven that the Count's arrangements were well made.</t8703> <t8704>Hildesheim took the chest and delivered it to Skinski.</t8704> <t8705>Skinski took it - and we lost track of it there.</t8705> <t8706>All we know is that the chest is moving somewhere over the water.</t8706> <t8707>Customs and tax officers, if there were any, must have been avoided.</t8707>
<t8708>Now, we come to what the Count might have done after disembarking in Galaţi.</t8708>
<t8709>The chest was delivered to Skinski before sunrise.</t8709> <t8710>At sunrise, the Count could appear in his own form.</t8710> <t8711>Here, we must ask why Skinski was chosen to assist in these matters.</t8711> <t8712>In my husband's journal, Skinski is mentioned as someone who goes down the river to the port and does business with the Slovaks; a man's comment there that the murder was the work of the Slovaks shows his general feelings towards this class.</t8712> <t8713>The Count wanted to be alone.</t8713>
