<t8832>October 31.</t8832> <t8833>- We are still progressing rapidly.</t8833> <t8834>Dawn has broken and Lord Godalming is sleeping.</t8834> <t8835>I am on watch.</t8835> <t8836>In the morning, there is a bitter cold; despite our heavy fur coats, the fire in the stove feels good.</t8836> <t8837>So far, only a few open boats have passed, but none had anything resembling the crate or package we are looking for on their decks.</t8837> <t8838>The men, each time we shone the electric sailor's lantern on them, got scared and fell to their knees, praying.</t8838>
<t8839>November 1, evening.</t8839> <t8840>- No news all day; we found nothing of the sort we were looking for.</t8840> <t8841>We have now moved on to Bistriţa, and if we are wrong in our guess, it means we have lost our chance.</t8841> <t8842>We checked all the boats, big and small.</t8842> <t8843>Early this morning, one of the crew mistook us for a government boat and acted accordingly.</t8843> <t8844>We saw something in this that would make things easier; thus, we obtained a Romanian flag now conspicuously waving at Fundu, where the Bistriţa merges with the Seret.</t8844> <t8845>Since then, this trick has worked on all the boats we have inspected; we are shown every respect and not once have we been opposed in what we ask or want to do.</t8845> <t8846>Some of the Slovaks said that a large boat, which was going faster than usual due to double crew on deck, passed by them.</t8846> <t8847>This was before they reached Fundu, so they couldn't tell if the boat returned to Bistriţa or proceeded up along the Seret.</t8847> <t8848>We heard nothing about such a boat at Fundu; it must have passed there during the night.</t8848> <t8849>I am very sleepy; perhaps the cold is starting to affect me badly, and even nature needs to rest at times.</t8849> <t8850>Godalming insists on taking the first watch.</t8850> <t8851>Thank God for the kindness Godalming has shown to poor Mina and me.</t8851>
<t8852>2</t8852> <t8853>November, morning.</t8853> <t8854>- The weather has brightened up completely.</t8854> <t8855>The kind-hearted man did not wake me up.</t8855> <t8856>He says it would be a sin to wake me up because I slept so peacefully and forgot my troubles.</t8856> <t8857>It feels very selfish to sleep so much and let him keep watch all night, but he was quite right about it.</t8857> <t8858>This morning, I have become a brand new man; sitting here watching Godalming sleep, I can do everything related to looking at the engine, steering, and keeping watch.</t8858> <t8859>I can feel my strength and vigor returning.</t8859> <t8860>I wonder where Mina and Van Helsing are now.</t8860> <t8861>They must have arrived in Veresti by noon on Wednesday.</t8861> <t8862>It will take them some time to find a carriage and horses; so, if they have set off and traveled quickly, they are at Borgo Pass by now.</t8862> <t8863>May God guide and help them!</t8863> <t8864>I am afraid to think of what might happen to them.</t8864> <t8865>I wish we could go faster!</t8865> <t8866>But we cannot; the engines are working hard and doing their best.</t8866> <t8867>I wonder how Dr. Seward and Mr. Morris are progressing.</t8867> <t8868>There are countless streams flowing from the mountains into this river, but none of them are very wide - although they are undoubtedly terrifying in winter and when the snow melts, for now, they are in this state - so the riders must not have encountered too many obstacles.</t8868> <t8869>I hope we can see them before reaching Strasba, because if we haven't caught the Count by then, we may need to come together and discuss what to do next.</t8869>
<t8870>Dr. Seward's journal</t8870>
<t8871>November 2.</t8871> <t8872>- Three days on the road.</t8872> <t8873>No news; even if there were news, there is no time to write it down as every moment is precious.</t8873> <t8874>We only took breaks necessary for the horses; but we both are enduring this very well.</t8874> <t8875>It turns out that our adventure-filled days have been beneficial.</t8875> <t8876>We must speed up; we will never be happy again until we see the steamship once more.</t8876>
<t8877>November 3.</t8877> <t8878>- In Fundu, we learned that the boat was going up the Bistriţa.</t8878> <t8879>I wish the weather wasn't so cold.</t8879> <t8880>There are signs that snow is coming, and if there is heavy snowfall, it will stop us.</t8880> <t8881>In such a case, we would need to get a sled and continue like the Russians.</t8881>
<t8882>November 4.</t8882> <t8883>- Today, we heard that the boat was delayed by an accident while trying to pass a spot where the current sped up.</t8883> <t8884>Slovak boats can navigate against the current without issues with the help of ropes and those who know how to use the rudder.</t8884> <t8885>Some of them set off just a few hours ago.</t8885> <t8886>Godalming himself is an amateur plumber and apparently, he was the one who fixed the boat.</t8886> <t8887>Eventually, with local help, they passed the fast current without issues and returned to tracking.</t8887> <t8888>I'm afraid the boat is not in very good condition due to the accident; the villagers said it stopped occasionally while it remained in sight when it re-entered calm waters.</t8888> <t8889>We must go faster than ever; our help may be needed soon.</t8889>
<t8890>Mina Harker's diary</t8890>
<t8891>October 31.</t8891> <t8892>- We arrived in Veresti at noon.</t8892> <t8893>The Professor said that he had great difficulty hypnotizing me at dawn this morning and that all I could say was, "dark and silent."</t8893> <t8894>Now he is outside to get a carriage and horses.</t8894> <t8895>He says he will also try to get spare horses so that we can change them on the road later.</t8895> <t8896>We have more than a hundred kilometers ahead of us.</t8896> <t8897>The region is very beautiful and very interesting; how delightful it would have been to see all this if we had come under different circumstances.</t8897> <t8898>What a great pleasure it would have been if Jonathan and I were passing through here alone.</t8898> <t8899>Stopping to see the people, learning something about their lives, filling our minds and memories with all the colors and impressiveness of these wild, beautiful lands and interesting people!</t8899> <t8900>But alas!</t8900>
<t8901>Later.</t8901> <t8902>- Dr. Van Helsing returned.</t8902> <t8903>He got the carriage and horses; we will have dinner and set off within an hour.</t8903> <t8904>Our hostess prepared a huge basket full of provisions for us; it looks like enough to feed an army.</t8904> <t8905>The professor supports the woman and whispers to me that we might not find food for maybe a week.</t8905> <t8906>He also went shopping and sent home a lot of excellent coats and blankets and all kinds of materials to keep warm.</t8906> <t8907>There will be no chance of us getting cold.</t8907>
<t8908>We will be setting off soon.</t8908> <t8909>We are truly in God's hands.</t8909> <t8910>Only He knows what might happen; with all the strength of my sad and humble spirit, I pray that He watches over my dear husband and ensures that, no matter what, Jonathan knows that I love and respect him far more than I can say, and that my last and truest thought will always be of him.</t8910>

<t8912>Mina Harker's journal</t8912>
<t8913>November 1st.</t8913> <t8914>- We were on the road all day and made good progress.</t8914> <t8915>The horses seem to know they are being treated kindly, as they run at their best speed of their own accord.</t8915> <t8916>We have changed so many horses so far and have seen the same thing consistently that we dare to think the journey will be easy.</t8916> <t8917>Dr. Van Helsing speaks briefly and to the point; he tells the farmers that he is in a hurry to get to Bistriţa and pays them well to change the horses.</t8917> <t8918>We drink soup, coffee, or tea and immediately set off again.</t8918> <t8919>It is a very beautiful country; filled with all imaginable beauties, and the people seem brave, strong, simple, and pleasant.</t8919> <t8920>They are very, very superstitious.</t8920> <t8921>At the first house we stopped at, the woman who served us crossed herself when she saw the scar on my forehead and extended two fingers towards me to ward off the evil eye.</t8921> <t8922>I think they have taken the trouble to put extra garlic in our food, and I cannot stand garlic.</t8922> <t8923>Since then, I have been careful not to take off my hat or veil, thus avoiding their suspicions.</t8923> <t8924>We are traveling fast, and since we do not have a driver who carries gossip with him, we are ahead of the gossip; but I can say that the fear of the evil eye follows us all along the way.</t8924> <t8925>The professor seems tireless; despite forcing me to sleep for long periods, he has not rested at all throughout the day.</t8925> <t8926>At sunset, he hypnotized me, and as usual, he says I responded, "Darkness, rushing water, and creaking wood."</t8926> <t8927>I am afraid to think of Jonathan, but somehow I am no longer afraid for him or myself.</t8927> <t8928>I am writing these lines while we wait for the horses to be prepared at a farmhouse.</t8928> <t8929>Dr. Van Helsing is sleeping.</t8929> <t8930>Poor thing, he looks very tired, old, and troubled, but his mouth is set as firmly as that of a conqueror; even in his sleep, he is full of determination.</t8930> <t8931>When we set off, I must ensure he rests while I drive the carriage.</t8931> <t8932>I will tell him that there are still days ahead of us and that he must not be exhausted when his full strength is needed.</t8932> <t8933>Everything is ready, we are setting off shortly.</t8933>
<t8934>2</t8934> <t8935>November, morning.</t8935> <t8936>- I made it and we drove the car in turns all night; morning came, the weather is bright but cold.</t8936> <t8937>There is a strange heaviness in the air - I call it heaviness because I can't find a better word; what I mean is, the air is bothering both of us.</t8937> <t8938>It's very cold and only our warm furs are keeping us comfortable.</t8938> <t8939>At dawn, Van Helsing hypnotized me; he said I responded with “Darkness, creaking wood, and roaring water,” so it means there are changes in the river as they move upstream.</t8939> <t8940>I hope, my dear, that you do not face any danger -more than necessary- but we are in God's hands.</t8940>
<t8941>2</t8941> <t8942>November, night.</t8942> <t8943>- We drove all day.</t8943> <t8944>As we progressed, the region became wilder, and the great peaks of the Carpathian Mountains, which seemed very far from us and very low on the horizon in Veresti, now appear to be coming together and rising before us.</t8944> <t8945>We both seem to be in good spirits; I think we are both trying to cheer each other up, and in doing so, we are cheering ourselves up.</t8945> <t8946>Dr. Van Helsing says we will reach the Borgo Pass by morning.</t8946> <t8947>There are very few houses here now, and the Professor says that the last horses we took will have to stay with us because we might not have the opportunity to change them.</t8947> <t8948>In addition to the two horses we changed, we have two more, so we have roughly four horses.</t8948> <t8949>Dear horses are patient and good-natured, they do not cause us any trouble.</t8949> <t8950>The other travelers do not worry us, and thus even I can drive the carriage.</t8950> <t8951>We will reach the Pass in daylight; we do not want to arrive earlier.</t8951> <t8952>So we are taking it slow and both of us are taking long rests in turns.</t8952> <t8953>Oh, I wonder what tomorrow will bring us?</t8953> <t8954>We will search for the place where my poor beloved suffered greatly.</t8954> <t8955>God, help us to be rightly guided, and may my husband and our loved ones, who are in mortal danger, be watched over by God.</t8955> <t8956>As for me, I am not worthy in His eyes.</t8956> <t8957>Ah! I am a sinner in His eyes, and I will remain so until He allows me to stand before Him as one who has not aroused His wrath.</t8957>
<t8958>Abraham Van Helsing's notes</t8958>
<t8959>November 4th.</t8959> <t8960>- This, in case I cannot see him, to my old and true friend, Doctor John Seward of Purfleet, London.</t8960> <t8961>This may explain everything.</t8961> <t8962>Morning has come, and I am writing by the fire I kept alive all night with the help of Madam Mina.</t8962> <t8963>The weather is cold, cold; so cold that the heavy, gray sky is filled with snow that will spend the entire winter on the ground because the earth has hardened to meet it.</t8963> <t8964>The weather seems to have affected Madam Mina; all day her mind appeared so heavy that she seemed not herself.</t8964> <t8965>Sleeping, sleeping, and sleeping!</t8965> <t8966>Normally very brisk, Madam Mina did literally nothing all day; she even lost her appetite.</t8966> <t8967>Madam Mina, who usually writes with great dedication at every break, did not record anything in her little journal.</t8967> <t8968>Something whispers to me that not everything is alright.</t8968> <t8969>But tonight she is more lively.</t8969> <t8970>Her long sleep has revived and refreshed her, for she is now as sweet and radiant as ever.</t8970> <t8971>At sunset, I try to hypnotize her, but alas!</t8971> <t8972>It doesn’t work; the power has diminished more and more each day, and today it failed me completely.</t8972> <t8973>Well, God’s will be done - whatever it is and wherever it leads us!</t8973>
<t8974>Now, let's come to the historical records, because since Madam Mina does not write in shorthand, I must write using my old cumbersome method, so that not a single day passes without being recorded.</t8974>
<t8975>Yesterday morning, just after sunrise, we arrived at the Borgo Pass.</t8975> <t8976>When I saw the signs of dawn, I prepared for hypnosis.</t8976> <t8977>We stopped our carriage and got out so we wouldn't be disturbed.</t8977> <t8978>I made a bed from furs, and Madam Mina, as usual but slower and for a shorter duration than before, surrendered herself to hypnotic sleep.</t8978> <t8979>The response was the same as before: "Darkness and violently flowing waters."</t8979> <t8980>Then she woke up lively and cheerful, and we continued on our way, soon reaching the Pass.</t8980> <t8981>Right there and then, Madam Mina was seized by a fervent enthusiasm; surely a new guiding force was manifesting itself because she pointed to one of the roads and spoke:</t8981>
<t8982>"From here!"</t8982><t8983>”</t8983>
<t8984>"How do you know?" I asked.</t8984>
<t8985>“Of course I know,” he replied and after pausing for a moment, added: “Didn’t my Jonathan travel and document his journey?</t8985><t8986>”</t8986>
<t8987>At first, it struck me as a bit odd, but soon I thought that there could be only this one side road.</t8987> <t8988>It is used very little; it is very different from the wider, harder, and more practical Bukovina-Bistriţa road.</t8988>
<t8989>Thus, we embarked on this path; when other paths appeared before us - we were not always sure they were paths because they were neglected and lightly covered with snow - the horses knew where to go, in fact, only they knew.</t8989><t8990>I left the reins to them, and they proceeded with great patience.</t8990><t8991>Soon, we found everything Jonathan had noted in his astonishing journal.</t8991><t8992>Then we progressed for long, long, long hours.</t8992><t8993>At first, I told Madam Mina to sleep; she tried and succeeded.</t8993><t8994>She kept sleeping until I became suspicious and tried to wake her.</t8994><t8995>But she continued to sleep, and despite my efforts, I couldn't wake her.</t8995><t8996>I didn't want to push too hard to avoid hurting her because I knew she was suffering greatly and that sleep was everything to her at times.</t8996><t8997>I think I must have fallen asleep too, because suddenly I felt guilty as if I had done something wrong; I found myself sitting upright with the reins in my hands, and the good-natured horses were trotting along slowly as usual.</t8997><t8998>I looked down and saw that Madam Mina was still asleep.</t8998><t8999>There wasn't much time left until sunset, and the sunlight was streaming over the snow like a great yellow flood, casting huge, long shadows where the mountain rose steeply.</t8999><t9000>Because we kept going up, up without stopping, and everything was so wild and rocky as if we had reached the end of the world!</t9000>
<t9001>Then I wake Madam Mina.</t9001> <t9002>This time she wakes up without much trouble, and then I try to put her into a hypnotic sleep.</t9002> <t9003>It's as if she's not trying to sleep.</t9003> <t9004>Still, I keep trying, trying; until suddenly I find both of us in the dark; so I look around and see that the sun has set.</t9004> <t9005>Madam Mina laughs; I turn and look at her.</t9005> <t9006>She is now quite awake and looks better than I have seen her since the night we first entered the Count's house in Carfax.</t9006> <t9007>I am surprised and feel uneasy at that moment; but she is so lively, so gentle and thoughtful towards me that I forget all fears.</t9007> <t9008>Since we brought wood with us, I make a fire; she prepares food while I untie, rest, secure, and feed the horses.</t9008> <t9009>Then, when I return to the fire, my meal is ready.</t9009> <t9010>I go to help her; but she laughs and says she has already eaten - she was so hungry that she couldn't wait.</t9010> <t9011>I don't like this, I have great doubts, but I am afraid of alarming her and so I say nothing.</t9011> <t9012>She helps me, and I eat my meal alone; then we wrap ourselves in furs and lie down by the fire, and I tell her to sleep while I keep watch.</t9012> <t9013>But I immediately forget that I am keeping watch, and when I suddenly remember, I find Madam Mina lying quietly but awake, looking at me with shining eyes.</t9013> <t9014>The same thing happened a couple more times, and I got quite a bit of sleep until morning.</t9014> <t9015>When I woke up, I tried to hypnotize her, but alas!</t9015> <t9016>Even though she obediently closed her eyes, she couldn't sleep.</t9016> <t9017>The sun rose higher and higher, her sleep came very late, but it was such a heavy sleep that she wouldn't wake up.</t9017> <t9018>When I had harnessed the horses and prepared everything, I had to lift her and place her in the carriage.</t9018> <t9019>Madam is still sleeping, sleeping, and in her sleep, she looks healthier and redder than before.</t9019> <t9020>And I don't like this.</t9020> <t9021>And I am afraid, afraid, afraid!</t9021> <t9022>(I am afraid of everything.</t9022><t9023>)</t9023> <t9024>I am even afraid to think, but I must continue on my way.</t9024> <t9025>This task we have undertaken is a matter of life and death, even more, and we must not retreat.</t9025>
<t9026>November 5, morning.</t9026> <t9027>- Let me write everything down completely, because even though you and I have seen some strange things together, you might think at first that I - Van Helsing - have gone mad, that after so much horror and tension in the nerves, my mind has become clouded.</t9027>
<t9028>Yesterday, we were on the road all day and we are getting closer and closer to the mountains, advancing towards wilder and more desolate lands.</t9028><t9029>There are alarming steep cliffs with waterfalls, and it seems as if Nature occasionally holds a carnival here.</t9029><t9030>Madam Mina is still sleeping, sleeping; despite getting hungry and feeding myself, I couldn't wake her up - not even for food.</t9030><t9031>Since she is tainted by the vampire's baptism, I began to fear that the deadly enchantment of this place might take hold of her.</t9031><t9032>"Well!" I said to myself, "If she is going to sleep all day, then I will not sleep all night."</t9032><t9033>As we progressed on the rugged road - because the road was very old and broken - I bowed my head and slept.</t9033><t9034>I woke up again with a feeling of guilt and a sense that a lot of time had passed; I saw that Madam Mina was still sleeping and the sun had considerably lowered.</t9034><t9035>But actually, everything had changed; the angry mountains seemed farther away, and we were in the high regions of a steep hill with a castle on its summit similar to the one described in Jonathan's journal.</t9035><t9036>At the same time, I was both happy and scared; because now, for better or worse, the end was near.</t9036><t9037>I woke Madam Mina and tried to hypnotize her again, but alas!</t9037><t9038>I couldn't succeed until it was too late.</t9038><t9039>Then, before the great darkness fell upon us - because even after sunset, the sky continued to reflect the setting sun on the snow, and everywhere was enveloped in a great twilight for a while - I untied the horses and fed them in a shelter I could find.</t9039><t9040>Then I lit a fire, and made Madam Mina, who was now awake and looking more attractive than ever, sit comfortably among her blankets.</t9040><t9041>I prepared the meal, but she didn't eat, merely saying she wasn't hungry.</t9041><t9042>Knowing it would be of no use, I didn't force her.</t9042><t9043>But I ate, because now I must be strong for everyone.</t9043><t9044>Then, fearing what might happen, I drew a wide circle around the place where Madam Mina was sitting for her comfort; I sprinkled some blessed bread over the circle and crumbled it well so that everywhere would be well protected.</t9044><t9045>Madam Mina sat all this time - motionless like the dead; her color turned white, white until she looked paler than the snow, and not a single word came out of her mouth.</t9045><t9046>But when I approached her, she clung to me, and I knew the poor thing was trembling from head to toe with great, painful terror.</t9046><t9047>When she became even quieter, I immediately said:</t9047>
<t9048>“Aren't you going to come near the fire?” Because I wanted to see what he could do.</t9048> <t9049>He stood up obediently, but when he took a step, he stopped and remained as if struck.</t9049>
<t9050>“Why don't you continue?” I asked.</t9050> <t9051>He shook his head from side to side and quietly returned to his seat.</t9051> <t9052>Then, like someone who had just woken up, he opened his eyes and looked at me, saying:</t9052>
<t9053>“I can't!” And he fell silent.</t9053> <t9054>I was relieved because I knew the things he couldn't do, and he couldn't do the things we were afraid he would.</t9054> <t9055>Even if his body was in danger, his soul was still safe!</t9055>
<t9056>At that moment, the horses began to neigh and tug at their reins; until I went to them and calmed them down.</t9056> <t9057>When they felt my hands on them, they whinnied softly as if they were happy, licked my hands, and stood still for a while.</t9057> <t9058>Throughout the night, until that cold hour when all of nature slowed down, I went to them many times, and each time my presence calmed them.</t9058> <t9059>At that cold hour, the fire began to die, and I was about to step out of the circle to revive it; because the snow was sweeping everything with an icy mist.</t9059> <t9060>Even in the darkness, there was light on the snow; it was as if the snowstorm and mist rings were turning into women wearing dresses with fluttering skirts.</t9060> <t9061>Everything was in deathly silence; only the horses were whimpering and cowering as if fearing the worst.</t9061> <t9062>I began to be afraid - terrifying fears; but then I felt the safety within the circle I stood in.</t9062> <t9063>I started to think that the night, the gloom, the unease I felt, and all those dreadful anxieties were causing me to dream.</t9063> <t9064>It was as if my memories of Jonathan's terrible experience were deceiving me, because the snowflakes and mist began to form circles, until the shadowy figures of those women who might have kissed Jonathan appeared.</t9064> <t9065>And then the horses cowered even more in fear, whimpering with terror like people in agony.</t9065> <t9066>They were not even in a state to escape from there in the madness of fear.</t9066> <t9067>When these strange shapes came closer and began to circle around, I feared for dear Madam Mina.</t9067> <t9068>I looked at her, but she was sitting calmly and smiling at me; I was about to take a step to stoke the fire when she caught me and pulled me back, whispering softly like one hears in dreams:</t9068>
<t9069>“No! No! Don't go out! You are safe here!” I turned to him and said, looking into his eyes:</t9069>
<t9070>"Well, what about you?</t9070> <t9071>I'm afraid for you!" When he heard this, he laughed, it was a low and surreal laugh, and he said:</t9071>
<t9072>“Are you afraid for me?</t9072> <t9073>Why are you afraid for me?</t9073> <t9074>There is no one in the whole world who is safer than I am against them.”</t9074> <t9075>While I was wondering about the meaning of his words, a sudden gust of wind flared the fire and I saw the red scar on his forehead.</t9075> <t9076>That was when, ah! I understood! If I hadn’t understood then, I would soon learn, because the shapes of swirling mist and snow approached but always kept away from the sacred circle.</t9076> <t9077>Then they began to materialize, until -if God hasn’t taken my mind- I saw with my own eyes the same three women Jonathan had seen in the room, trying to kiss his throat, standing before me in flesh and blood.</t9077> <t9078>I recognized their swaying round forms, their gleaming hard eyes, their white teeth, their red cheeks, and their lustful lips.</t9078> <t9079>They laughed at poor dear Madam Mina, and as their laughter pierced the silence of the night, they entwined their arms and pointed at her, speaking in those sweet ringing voices that Jonathan compared to the unbearable sweetness of clinking water glasses:</t9079>
<t9080>"Come, my brother.</t9080> <t9081>Come to us.</t9081> <t9082>Come! Come!" <t9091>We stayed like that until the redness of dawn began to fall upon the gloom of the snow.</t9091> <t9092>I was in a state of misery and fear, filled with sorrow and dread, but once that beautiful sun began to climb the horizon again, a surge of life energy filled me.</t9092> <t9093>With the first arrival of dawn, those dreadful shapes melted away into the swirling mist and snow; crowns of transparent gloom advanced towards the castle and disappeared from sight.</t9093>
<t9094>With the breaking of dawn, I instinctively turned to Madam Mina to hypnotize her, but she had fallen into a deep and sudden sleep, and I couldn't wake her.</t9094> <t9095>I tried to hypnotize her in her sleep, but she didn't respond at all, and morning came.</t9095> <t9096>I am still afraid to move.</t9096> <t9097>I lit my fire and saw the horses; they were all dead.</t9097> <t9098>I have a lot of work to do here today, and I am waiting until the sun rises fully, because although the snow and mist obscure it, I may need to go to some places where daylight will be my assurance.</t9098>
<t9099>I will gather my strength with breakfast and then set to my dreadful task.</t9099> <t9100>Madam Mina is still sleeping, and thank God she is calm in her sleep.</t9100>
<t9101>Jonathan Harker's journal</t9101>
<t9102>4</t9102> <t9103>November, evening.</t9103> <t9104>- The accident that happened to the steamship was very bad for all of us.</t9104> <t9105>If it hadn't happened, we would have caught the other ship much earlier and by now dear Mina would have been free.</t9105> <t9106>I am afraid to think that she is in the steppes near that dreadful place.</t9106> <t9107>We have horses and we are on the trail.</t9107> <t9108>I am writing these lines while Godalming is preparing.</t9108> <t9109>We have weapons.</t9109> <t9110>If the Gypsies intend to fight, they need to be very careful.</t9110> <t9111>Oh! <t9114>Dr. Seward's journal</t9114>
<t9115>November 5th.</t9115> <t9116>- At dawn, we saw the Gypsy caravan speeding away from the river in a car.</t9116> <t9117>They were surrounding the car and moving swiftly.</t9117> <t9118>It was lightly snowing, and there was a strange excitement in the air.</t9118> <t9119>This could be our own excited feelings, but the anxiety is peculiar.</t9119> <t9120>I hear the wolves howling in the distance; the snow carries these sounds down from the mountains, and there is danger for all of us from every direction.</t9120> <t9121>The horses are almost ready, and we will set off very soon.</t9121> <t9122>We are heading towards someone's death.</t9122> <t9123>Only God knows who, where, when, or how someone will die...</t9123>
<t9124>Dr. Van Helsing's notes</t9124>
<t9125>November 5, late afternoon.</t9125> <t9126>- At least my sanity is intact.</t9126> <t9127>Though proving it was horrifying, I still thank God for His mercy.</t9127> <t9128>I left Madam Mina sleeping within the holy circle and set off towards the castle.</t9128> <t9129>The blacksmith's hammer I took from the carriage in Veresti came in handy; despite all the doors being open, I broke them off their rusty hinges so that no ill will or bad luck could close them and trap me inside.</t9129> <t9130>Here, Jonathan's painful experience helped me.</t9130> <t9131>Remembering his journal, I found the way to the old chapel, for I knew where my task lay.</t9131> <t9132>The air was very oppressive; from time to time, it seemed to emit a sulfurous gas that made my head spin.</t9132> <t9133>Either there was a ringing in my ears, or I was hearing the howling of wolves from afar.</t9133> <t9134>Then I reminded myself of dear Madam Mina and felt very distressed.</t9134> <t9135>This dilemma pressed upon me.</t9135> <t9136>I dared not bring her here, but I left her safe from the Vampire within the holy circle; yet even there, there could be wolves!</t9136> <t9137>I decided that my task was here and if it was God's will, we must surrender to the wolves.</t9137> <t9138>Beyond this, there was death and salvation.</t9138> <t9139>Thus, I made the choice on her behalf.</t9139> <t9140>If it were for myself, the choice would be easy; better to lie in the belly of the wolf than in the Vampire's grave!</t9140> <t9141>Thus, I decided to continue with my task.</t9141>
<t9142>I knew there were at least three graves to be found, used graves; so, I searched, searched, and found one.</t9142> <t9143>The vampire was in its sleep; it had such a beauty so full of life and bodily desire that I shuddered as if I had come to commit murder.</t9143> <t9144>Ah! In the old days, when such things happened, I have no doubt that many men who set out to fulfill a duty like mine eventually realized that their hearts and then their nerves failed them halfway.</t9144> <t9145>Thus, they would keep postponing their duty until the frivolous Undead hypnotized them, and they would wait, wait there until sunset and the Vampire’s sleep ended.</t9145> <t9146>Then, the beautiful eyes of that charming woman would open, look lovingly, and offer her lustful lips for a kiss; the man would be powerless.</t9146> <t9147>Thus, another victim would join the vampire horde; the merciless and terrifying ranks of the Undead would increase by one more.</t9147> <t9148>There is undoubtedly an enchantment; even while lying in a grave decayed over time and heavy with the dust of centuries, accompanied by that dreadful smell similar to the one in the Count’s secret lair, I am affected by the presence of such a being.</t9148> <t9149>Yes, I was affected -I, Van Helsing, despite my entire purpose and reason for hatred- I was affected by a desire to delay that paralyzed my faculties and hindered my soul.</t9149> <t9150>My need for natural sleep and the strange pressure in the air might be taking hold of me.</t9150> <t9151>Undoubtedly, I was falling into sleep -the open-eyed sleep of someone who desires sweet enchantment- when a long, low moan full of great sorrow and pain, cutting through the air silenced by the snow, woke me like a trumpet sound.</t9151> <t9152>For this was the voice of my dear Madam Mina that I heard.</t9152>
<t9153>Then, I gathered strength for my dreadful task and, by forcibly lifting the tomb lids, I found another of the sisters, the other brunette.</t9153> <t9154>So that I would not begin to be enchanted once more, I did not dare to stop to look at her as I had done with the other sister, but continued my search until I found her in a large, high tomb that seemed made for that dear blonde sister who materialized from the atoms of the mist as Jonathan had seen.</t9154> <t9155>She had such a pure appearance, such dazzling beauty, such graceful sensuality that the masculine instinct within me, which calls my kind to love and protect one of her kind, caused my head to spin with a new feeling.</t9155> <t9156>But thank God, the cry of my dear Madam Mina's soul had not yet faded from my ears, and before the spell could further take hold of me, I gathered my courage for my savage duty.</t9156> <t9157>By this time, I had searched all the tombs I could find in the chapel; since there were only two Undead specters around us at night, I concluded that there were no other active Undead at the moment.</t9157> <t9158>There was a single tomb more magnificent than all the other tombs; it was giant and had noble proportions.</t9158> <t9159>On it was inscribed a single word:</t9159>
<t9160>DRACULA</t9160>
<t9161>So, this was the "Undead Lair of the Vampire King," to which many things were connected.</t9161> <t9162>The empty grave meaningfully told me that something I already knew was true.</t9162> <t9163>Through my dreadful task, before sending these women to their own deaths, I placed some blessed bread in Dracula's grave, thus banishing him from that grave forever while he was in his Undead state.</t9163>
<t9164>Then, my dreadful task began, I was afraid of this.</t9164> <t9165>If there had been only one, it would have been relatively easy.</t9165> <t9166>But three! To start twice more after committing a horrifying act; if it was dreadful with sweet Miss Lucy, who knows how it would be with these strangers who have survived for centuries and grown stronger over the years, who would fight for their vile lives if they could...</t9166>
<t9167>Ah, my friend John!</t9167> <t9168>This is butchery!</t9168> <t9169>If I hadn't gathered my courage by thinking of other dead and those living with such a shroud of fear over them, I wouldn't have been able to continue my work.</t9169> <t9170>Even after it all ended, I keep trembling, thank God my nerves endured it.</t9170> <t9171>If I hadn't seen the peace indicating the soul was reclaimed, the satisfaction spreading across the face before the final dissolution, I couldn't have continued my butchery.</t9171> <t9172>I couldn't bear that horrifying scream heard as the stake was driven in, the lunges of the writhing form, and the blood-filled frothy lips.</t9172> <t9173>I would flee in terror and leave my work unfinished.</t9173> <t9174>But it's all over!</t9174> <t9175>And thinking that in that brief moment before their annihilation, each of them appeared docile in their true death sleep, I can pity them and shed tears for them.</t9175> <t9176>Because, my friend John, it was as if the death that should have come centuries ago finally appeared and suddenly declared loudly, "I am He!" before each of their heads was freshly severed, and their entire body crumbled and merged back into the soil from which it came.</t9176>
<t9177>Before leaving the castle, I arranged the entrances so that the Count could never enter there again as the Undead.</t9177>
<t9178>As soon as I stepped into the circle where Madam Mina was sleeping, she woke up from her sleep and let out such a scream of pain upon seeing me that it was hard to bear.</t9178>
<t9179>“Come!” she said, “come, let's get away from this dreadful place!</t9179> <t9180>Let's go meet my husband, whom I know is coming towards us.”</t9180> <t9181>She looked weak, pale, and frail, but her eyes were pure and shone with enthusiasm.</t9181> <t9182>I was glad to see her paleness and illness, because my mind was filled with fresh fears about the rosy-cheeked vampire's sleep.</t9182>
<t9183>And so, with trust and hope, but still filled with fear, we advanced eastward to meet our friends - and him; because Madam Mina says she knows they are coming to meet us.</t9183>
<t9184>Mina Harker's diary</t9184>
<t9185>November 6.</t9185> <t9186>- It was almost evening when the Professor and I started heading east, knowing that Jonathan had arrived.</t9186> <t9187>Despite the steep downhill slope of the road, we weren't going fast because we had to take heavy blankets and shawls with us; we couldn't dare face the possibility of not having something to keep us warm in the cold and snow.</t9187> <t9188>We also had to take some of our supplies with us, because we were in a completely desolate place and, as far as we could see through the falling snow, there was no sign of any settlement in sight.</t9188> <t9189>After advancing about two kilometers, I got tired from the heavy walk and sat down to rest.</t9189> <t9190>Then we looked back and saw the place where the distinct outlines of Dracula's castle cut the sky, because we were so far down the hill it stood on that the perspective of the Carpathian Mountains was well below the castle.</t9190> <t9191>We saw it in all its glory, perched atop a three-hundred-meter-deep precipice; it seemed as if there was a great void between it and the summit of any adjacent mountain.</t9191> <t9192>There was something wild and sinister about this place.</t9192> <t9193>We could hear the howling of wolves in the distance.</t9193> <t9194>They were very far away, but even muffled by the deafening snow, their voices were filled with terror.</t9194> <t9195>I knew from Dr. Van Helsing's exploration of the surroundings that he was trying to find a strategic point where we would be less exposed in case of an attack.</t9195> <t9196>The rough road still stretched downward; we could trace it partly from the accumulated snow.</t9196>
<t9197>Soon after, the Professor signaled to me, and I stood up and went to him.</t9197> <t9198>He had found a perfect spot, a kind of natural hollow with an entrance like a door between two large rocks.</t9198> <t9199>He took my hand and led me inside: "Look!" he said, "You will be safe here, and if the wolves come, I can face them one by one."</t9199> <t9200>He carried our furs inside, prepared a secure nest for me, and tried to force me to eat some provisions.</t9200> <t9201>But I couldn't eat; even attempting it was repulsive to me, and although I wanted to please him, I couldn't bring myself to try.</t9201> <t9202>He looked very sad, but he did not scold me.</t9202> <t9203>He took his binoculars out of the bag, stood on top of the rock, and began to look at the horizon.</t9203> <t9204>Suddenly, he shouted:</t9204>
<t9205>"Look! Madam Mina! Look! Look!" I jumped up from my place and stood beside him on the rock; he handed me his binoculars and pointed.</t9205> <t9206>The snow was now falling even more heavily, and the fierce snowflakes were swirling as if caught in a vortex, because a strong wind had started to blow.</t9206> <t9207>But there were occasional gaps in the heavy snowfall, and I could see a long distance.</t9207> <t9208>From our height, it was possible to see a great range; in the distance, beyond the empty snowy fields, I could see the river winding like a black ribbon.</t9208> <t9209>Right in front of us and not very far away - in fact, so close that I wondered why we hadn't noticed them before - a group of horsemen was advancing rapidly.</t9209> <t9210>In the middle of them was a carriage, a long wagon that swayed from side to side with every bump in the road, like a dog's wagging tail.</t9210> <t9211>Since they stood out clearly against the snow, I could tell from the men's clothing that they were either peasants or Gypsies.</t9211>
<t9212>There was a large square chest in the car.</t9212> <t9213>My heart skipped a beat when I saw it, because I felt that the end had come.</t9213> <t9214>Evening was falling, and by that time, that Thing which had been imprisoned here would regain its freedom and escape all pursuits.</t9214> <t9215>I turned to the Professor in fear; I was very surprised not to see the Professor there.</t9215> <t9216>A second later, I saw him down below.</t9216> <t9217>He drew a circle around the rock, similar to the one we had taken refuge in last night.</t9217> <t9218>When he completed the drawing, he came back to me and said:</t9218>
<t9219>"At least here you will be safe from him!” He took the binoculars from me and, once the snow had stopped again, he scanned the area beneath us thoroughly.</t9219> <t9220>"Look,” he said, "they are coming fast; they are whipping their horses and galloping as fast as they can.”</t9220> <t9221>He paused and continued speaking in a muffled voice:</t9221>
<t9222>"They are running for the sunset."</t9222> <t9223>"We might be too late."</t9223> <t9224>"God’s will shall be done!”</t9224> <t9225>A blinding snowstorm came from below again and the entire landscape disappeared under the snow.</t9225> <t9226>But the storm passed quickly and once again the Professor's binoculars were fixed on the opening ahead of us.</t9226> <t9227>That's when the Professor suddenly shouted:</t9227>
<t9228>"Look! Look! Look! Look, two horsemen are rapidly coming from the south.</t9228> <t9229>It must be Quincey and John.</t9229> <t9230>Take the binoculars.</t9230> <t9231>Look before the snow hides everything!” I took the binoculars and looked.</t9231> <t9232>The two men coming could be Dr. Seward and Mr. Morris.</t9232> <t9233>In any case, I knew that neither of them was Jonathan.</t9233> <t9234>At the same time, I knew Jonathan wasn't far away; when I looked around, I saw two other men coming at lightning speed to the north of the approaching group.</t9234> <t9235>I knew one of them was Jonathan and concluded that the other was, of course, Lord Godalming.</t9235> <t9236>They were also chasing the group with the carriage.</t9236> <t9237>When I told this to the Professor, he shouted with joy like a schoolboy and, after watching carefully until the snow reduced visibility to zero, he propped his Winchester rifle against the rock at the entrance of our shelter and got it ready.</t9237> <t9238>“They are getting closer to each other,” he said.</t9238> <t9239>“When the time comes, we will see Gypsies everywhere.”</t9239> <t9240>I took my pistol in hand to use, because as we talked, the howling of the wolves grew stronger and closer.</t9240> <t9241>When the snowstorm subsided for a moment, we looked again.</t9241> <t9242>It was strange to see the snow falling around us in such large flakes and the sun shining even brighter as it set over the peaks of the distant mountains.</t9242> <t9243>When I scanned the surroundings with the binoculars, I saw dots moving here and there, in pairs, in threes, and in large groups - the wolves were gathering for their prey.</t9243>
<t9244>Every second we waited felt like a year.</t9244> <t9245>The wind was increasing in intensity, and the snowflakes swirling around us, creating small vortices, were being driven with great fury.</t9245> <t9246>At times, we couldn't even see the tip of our noses, but at other times, as the wind passed by with its echoing sound, it seemed to clear the airspace around us so we could see into the distance.</t9246> <t9247>We had become so accustomed to waiting for sunrise and sunset lately that we could predict exactly when it would happen, and we knew that the sun would set very soon.</t9247>
<t9248>It was hard to believe that our watches showed we had been waiting in that rocky shelter for less than half an hour until the newcomers began to approach us closely.</t9248> <t9249>The wind was now blowing more violently and harshly, mostly coming from the north.</t9249> <t9250>Apparently, the wind had driven the snow clouds away from us, because now there were only occasional bursts of snow.</t9250> <t9251>We could easily distinguish the members of both groups, those being chased and those doing the chasing.</t9251> <t9252>The strange thing was that the ones being chased seemed unaware of their pursuers or at least didn't care, but as the sun descended over the mountain peaks, they seemed to double their speed.</t9252>
<t9253>They were getting closer and closer.</t9253> <t9254>The Professor and I crouched behind our rock and took our weapons in hand; I could see that the Professor was determined not to let them pass through here.</t9254> <t9255>They were all unaware of our presence.</t9255>
<t9256>At the same time, two voices shouted, "Stop!"</t9256> <t9257>One of the voices was Jonathan's, high-pitched with anger; the other was Mr. Morris's, strong, determined, and calm in command.</t9257> <t9258>The Gypsies might not have known the language, but it was impossible to misunderstand the tone, no matter what language the words were spoken in; instinctively, they pulled the reins, and at that moment, Lord Godalming and Jonathan attacked from one side, while Dr. Seward and Mr. Morris attacked from the other.</t9258> <t9259>The chief, a magnificent-looking man sitting on his horse like a Centaur, signaled them to go with his hand and angrily commanded his companions to advance.</t9259> <t9260>They whipped their horses, and the horses surged forward; but the four men raised their Winchester rifles and unmistakably ordered them to stop.</t9260> <t9261>At the same time, Dr. Van Helsing and I stood up from behind the rock and aimed our weapons at the Gypsies.</t9261> <t9262>Seeing they were surrounded, they pulled the reins and stopped.</t9262> <t9263>Their leader turned to them and said something, upon which each of the Gypsies drew their weapon - knife or pistol - and stood ready to attack.</t9263> <t9264>An argument ensued instantly.</t9264>
<t9265>The leader of the community spurred his horse forward with a swift movement of the reins and, pointing first to the sun, which was now approaching the hills, and then to the castle, uttered some words I did not understand.</t9265> <t9266>In response, four men from our team dismounted from their horses and quickly ran towards the carriage.</t9266> <t9267>When I saw Jonathan putting himself in such danger, I should have been horrified, but the fire of battle must have affected me like the others; I felt no fear, only a wild and great desire to do something.</t9267> <t9268>Seeing the quick movement of our team, the chieftain gave an order; his men instantly formed an undisciplined circle around the carriage, each one pushing and shoving the other to carry out the command.</t9268>
<t9269>In the midst of all this, I could see Jonathan on one side of the circle of men and Quincey on the other, trying to clear a path to the carriage; it was clear they were determined to finish their work before sunset.</t9269> <t9270>Nothing could stop or even hinder them.</t9270> <t9271>Neither the guns and gleaming knives aimed by the Gypsies in front, nor the howling of the wolves behind seemed to catch their attention.</t9271> <t9272>Jonathan's boldness and evident determination seemed to have frightened and subdued those in front of him.</t9272> <t9273>In an instant, he jumped onto the carriage and, with what seemed like extraordinary strength, lifted the large chest and hurled it to the ground over the wheel.</t9273> <t9274>Meanwhile, Mr. Morris had to use force to get through the Gypsy circle on his side.</t9274> <t9275>During the time I watched Jonathan breathlessly, I saw out of the corner of my eye that Mr. Morris, in desperation, lunged forward and made a path through them, the Gypsies' knives flashing and stabbing him.</t9275> <t9276>He fended off the attacks with his large hunting knife, and at first, I thought he had safely overcome it, but then I saw him leap to Jonathan's side, who had jumped down from the carriage, clutching his side tightly with his left hand and blood gushing between his fingers.</t9276> <t9277>Still, he did not stop, for as Jonathan, in desperation, used the large kukri to pry open the lid from one end of the chest, Mr. Morris, in a frenzy, attacked the other end with his hunting knife.</t9277> <t9278>With the efforts of both men, the lid began to give way; the nails were pulled out with a sharp, scream-like creak, and the lid of the chest was thrown back.</t9278>
<t9279>At this moment, seeing that they were surrounded by Winchesters and at the mercy of Lord Godalming and Dr. Seward, the Gypsies gave up and ceased to resist.</t9279> <t9280>The sun had almost descended from the mountain peaks, and the long shadows of the entire group were cast upon the snow.</t9280> <t9281>I saw the Count lying on the soil that had spilled partially over him due to the hard fall from the cart.</t9281> <t9282>He was pale as death, resembling a mummy, and his red eyes shone with that terrible vengeful look I knew so well.</t9282>
<t9283>While looking at her, those eyes saw the setting sun and the expression of hatred turned into triumph.</t9283>
<t9284>But at that moment came the speed and brightness of Jonathan's large knife.</t9284> <t9285>I screamed when I saw the knife cut the throat; at the same time, Mr. Morris's hunting knife also plunged into the heart.</t9285>
<t9286>Everything that happened was like a miracle, but right before our eyes and in almost a single breath, the entire body turned to dust and disappeared from sight.</t9286> <t9287>Even in that final moment of death, I will be grateful for as long as I live that there was an expression of peace on that face that I could never have imagined.</t9287>
<t9288>Dracula's Castle now stood facing the red sky, and each stone of its broken battlements was emerging one by one in the light of the setting sun.</t9288>
<t9289>In some way, the Gypsies, who saw us as the reason for the extraordinary disappearance of the dead man, turned their backs without a word and moved away as if they wanted to save their lives.</t9289> <t9290>Those without horses jumped onto the horse-drawn carriage and shouted at the riders not to leave them behind.</t9290> <t9291>The wolves, which had pulled back to a safe distance, left us alone and followed them.</t9291>
<t9292>Mr. Morris, who had collapsed to the ground, was leaning on his elbow, holding the hand pressed against his side; blood was still gushing from between his fingers.</t9292> <t9293>I ran to his side, for the sacred circle no longer held me back; both doctors also ran to Mr. Morris.</t9293> <t9294>Jonathan knelt beside him, and the wounded man rested his head on Jonathan's shoulder.</t9294> <t9295>With a sigh and a feeble effort, he took my hand in his unbloodied one.</t9295> <t9296>He must have seen the pain in my heart on my face, for he was looking at me and smiling as he spoke:</t9296>
<t9297>“I am so happy to have been of use!”</t9297> <t9298>“Oh, my God!” he suddenly shouted; struggling to sit up and showing me something, “It was worth dying for this!</t9298> <t9299>Look! Look!”</t9299>
<t9300>The sun had now descended to the very peak of the mountain, and its red rays were falling on my face; it was as if my face was being bathed in a pink light.</t9300> <t9301>As the dying man continued to speak, all the men who were following his finger with their eyes suddenly dropped to their knees, and a deep and heartfelt "Amen!" was heard from all of them.</t9301>
<t9302>"Now, thank God that all this was not in vain!"</t9302> <t9303>"Look! Now, the snow is not more spotless than his forehead!"</t9303> <t9304>"The curse is lifted!"</t9304><t9305>"</t9305>
<t9306>And leaving us in great pain, smiling and in silence, the brave gentleman died.</t9306>
<t9307>Not</t9307>
<t9308>Seven years ago, we all went through fire, and since then, some of us believe that the happiness we have now is worth the pain we endured.</t9308> <t9309>The fact that our son's birthday is on the same day Quincey Morris died gives Mina and me extra joy.</t9309> <t9310>I know that his mother has a secret belief that a part of our brave friend's spirit has passed into him.</t9310> <t9311>The bundle of names he carries ties our small community together, but we call him Quincey.</t9311>
<t9312>This summer, we took a journey to Transylvania and went to that old place which holds -and still holds- very vivid and terrifying memories for all of us.</t9312> <t9313>It was almost impossible to believe that the things we saw with our own eyes and heard with our own ears were vivid realities.</t9313> <t9314>The traces of everything that happened had been erased.</t9314> <t9315>The castle was standing as before, rising over the desolation.</t9315>
<t9316>When we returned home, we began to talk about the old times, which we no longer remember with sorrow because Godalming and Seward had happy marriages.</t9316> <t9317>I took the documents out of the safe where they had been since we returned long ago.</t9317> <t9318>We were horrified by the fact that there were almost no original documents among all this pile of material where the records were arranged; apart from Mina's, Seward's, and my later journals and Van Helsing's notes, there was nothing but a heap of typewritten papers.</t9318> <t9319>Even if we had such a desire, we could not ask anyone to accept these documents as evidence of such a wild story.</t9319> <t9320>Van Helsing, with our son sitting on his knee, summarized the matter as follows:</t9320>
<t9321>“We don't need evidence; we don't want anyone to believe us!</t9321> <t9322>This child will one day know how brave and valiant his mother was.</t9322> <t9323>He already knows her sweetness and warm attention; later, he will understand how some men loved her and how they defied many things for her sake.</t9323><t9324>”</t9324>
<t9325>JONATHAN HARKER</t9325>
